[ ] 85983
[ ] 85984  /*****************************************************************************
[ ] 85985  ** What follows is a massive switch statement where each case implements a
[ ] 85986  ** separate instruction in the virtual machine.  If we follow the usual
[ ] 85987  ** indentation conventions, each case should be indented by 6 spaces.  But
[ ] 85988  ** that is a lot of wasted space on the left margin.  So the code within
[ ] 85989  ** the switch statement will break with convention and be flush-left. Another
[ ] 85990  ** big comment (similar to this one) will mark the point in the code where
[ ] 85991  ** we transition back to normal indentation.
[ ] 85992  **
[ ] 85993  ** The formatting of each case is important.  The makefile for SQLite
[ ] 85994  ** generates two C files "opcodes.h" and "opcodes.c" by scanning this
[ ] 85995  ** file looking for lines that begin with "case OP_".  The opcodes.h files
[ ] 85996  ** will be filled with #defines that give unique integer values to each
[ ] 85997  ** opcode and the opcodes.c file is filled with an array of strings where
[ ] 85998  ** each string is the symbolic name for the corresponding opcode.  If the
[ ] 85999  ** case statement is followed by a comment of the form "/# same as ... #/"
[ ] 86000  ** that comment is used to determine the particular value of the opcode.
[ ] 86001  **
[ ] 86002  ** Other keywords in the comment that follows each case are used to
[ ] 86003  ** construct the OPFLG_INITIALIZER value that initializes opcodeProperty[].
[ ] 86004  ** Keywords include: in1, in2, in3, out2, out3.  See
[ ] 86005  ** the mkopcodeh.awk script for additional information.
[ ] 86006  **
[ ] 86007  ** Documentation about VDBE opcodes is generated by scanning this file
[ ] 86008  ** for lines of that contain "Opcode:".  That line and all subsequent
[ ] 86009  ** comment lines are used in the generation of the opcode.html documentation
[ ] 86010  ** file.
[ ] 86011  **
[ ] 86012  ** SUMMARY:
[ ] 86013  **
[ ] 86014  **     Formatting is important to scripts that scan this file.
[ ] 86015  **     Do not deviate from the formatting style currently in use.
[ ] 86016  **
[ ] 86017  *****************************************************************************/
[ ] 86018
[ ] 86019  /* Opcode:  Goto * P2 * * *
[ ] 86020  **
[ ] 86021  ** An unconditional jump to address P2.
[ ] 86022  ** The next instruction executed will be
[ ] 86023  ** the one at index P2 from the beginning of
[ ] 86024  ** the program.
[ ] 86025  **
[ ] 86026  ** The P1 parameter is not actually used by this opcode.  However, it
[ ] 86027  ** is sometimes set to 1 instead of 0 as a hint to the command-line shell
[ ] 86028  ** that this Goto is the bottom of a loop and that the lines from P2 down
[ ] 86029  ** to the current line should be indented for EXPLAIN output.
[ ] 86030  */
[W] 86031  case OP_Goto: {             /* jump */
[ ] 86032
[W] 86033  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 86034    /* In debuggging mode, when the p5 flags is set on an OP_Goto, that
[ ] 86035    ** means we should really jump back to the preceeding OP_ReleaseReg
[ ] 86036    ** instruction. */
[W] 86037    if( pOp->p5 ){
[ ] 86038      assert( pOp->p2 < (int)(pOp - aOp) );
[ ] 86039      assert( pOp->p2 > 1 );
[ ] 86040      pOp = &aOp[pOp->p2 - 2];
[ ] 86041      assert( pOp[1].opcode==OP_ReleaseReg );
[ ] 86042      goto check_for_interrupt;
[ ] 86043    }
[W] 86044  #endif
[ ] 86045
[W] 86046  jump_to_p2_and_check_for_interrupt:
[W] 86047    pOp = &aOp[pOp->p2 - 1];
[ ] 86048
[ ] 86049    /* Opcodes that are used as the bottom of a loop (OP_Next, OP_Prev,
[ ] 86050    ** OP_VNext, or OP_SorterNext) all jump here upon
[ ] 86051    ** completion.  Check to see if sqlite3_interrupt() has been called
[ ] 86052    ** or if the progress callback needs to be invoked.
[ ] 86053    **
[ ] 86054    ** This code uses unstructured "goto" statements and does not look clean.
[ ] 86055    ** But that is not due to sloppy coding habits. The code is written this
[ ] 86056    ** way for performance, to avoid having to run the interrupt and progress
[ ] 86057    ** checks on every opcode.  This helps sqlite3_step() to run about 1.5%
[ ] 86058    ** faster according to "valgrind --tool=cachegrind" */
[W] 86059  check_for_interrupt:
[W] 86060    if( AtomicLoad(&db->u1.isInterrupted) ) goto abort_due_to_interrupt;
[W] 86061  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_PROGRESS_CALLBACK
[ ] 86062    /* Call the progress callback if it is configured and the required number
[ ] 86063    ** of VDBE ops have been executed (either since this invocation of
[ ] 86064    ** sqlite3VdbeExec() or since last time the progress callback was called).
[ ] 86065    ** If the progress callback returns non-zero, exit the virtual machine with
[ ] 86066    ** a return code SQLITE_ABORT.
[ ] 86067    */
[W] 86068    while( nVmStep>=nProgressLimit && db->xProgress!=0 ){
[W] 86069      assert( db->nProgressOps!=0 );
[W] 86070      nProgressLimit += db->nProgressOps;

[ ] 86072        nProgressLimit = 0xffffffff;
[ ] 86073        rc = SQLITE_INTERRUPT;
[ ] 86074        goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 86075      }
[W] 86076    }
[W] 86077  #endif
[ ] 86078
[W] 86079    break;
[W] 86080  }
[ ] 86081
[ ] 86082  /* Opcode:  Gosub P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 86083  **
[ ] 86084  ** Write the current address onto register P1
[ ] 86085  ** and then jump to address P2.
[ ] 86086  */
[W] 86087  case OP_Gosub: {            /* jump */
[ ] 86088    assert( pOp->p1>0 && pOp->p1<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 86089    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86090    assert( VdbeMemDynamic(pIn1)==0 );
[ ] 86091    memAboutToChange(p, pIn1);
[ ] 86092    pIn1->flags = MEM_Int;
[ ] 86093    pIn1->u.i = (int)(pOp-aOp);
[ ] 86094    REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p1, pIn1);
[ ] 86095
[ ] 86096    /* Most jump operations do a goto to this spot in order to update
[ ] 86097    ** the pOp pointer. */
[B] 86098  jump_to_p2:
[B] 86099    pOp = &aOp[pOp->p2 - 1];
[B] 86100    break;
[ ] 86101  }
[ ] 86102
[ ] 86103  /* Opcode:  Return P1 * * * *
[ ] 86104  **
[ ] 86105  ** Jump to the next instruction after the address in register P1.  After
[ ] 86106  ** the jump, register P1 becomes undefined.
[ ] 86107  */
[ ] 86108  case OP_Return: {           /* in1 */
[ ] 86109    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86110    assert( pIn1->flags==MEM_Int );
[ ] 86111    pOp = &aOp[pIn1->u.i];
[ ] 86112    pIn1->flags = MEM_Undefined;
[ ] 86113    break;
[ ] 86114  }
[ ] 86115
[ ] 86116  /* Opcode: InitCoroutine P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86117  **
[ ] 86118  ** Set up register P1 so that it will Yield to the coroutine
[ ] 86119  ** located at address P3.
[ ] 86120  **
[ ] 86121  ** If P2!=0 then the coroutine implementation immediately follows
[ ] 86122  ** this opcode.  So jump over the coroutine implementation to
[ ] 86123  ** address P2.
[ ] 86124  **
[ ] 86125  ** See also: EndCoroutine
[ ] 86126  */
[ ] 86127  case OP_InitCoroutine: {     /* jump */
[ ] 86128    assert( pOp->p1>0 &&  pOp->p1<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 86129    assert( pOp->p2>=0 && pOp->p2<p->nOp );
[ ] 86130    assert( pOp->p3>=0 && pOp->p3<p->nOp );
[ ] 86131    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86132    assert( !VdbeMemDynamic(pOut) );
[ ] 86133    pOut->u.i = pOp->p3 - 1;
[ ] 86134    pOut->flags = MEM_Int;
[ ] 86135    if( pOp->p2 ) goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 86136    break;
[ ] 86137  }
[ ] 86138
[ ] 86139  /* Opcode:  EndCoroutine P1 * * * *
[ ] 86140  **
[ ] 86141  ** The instruction at the address in register P1 is a Yield.
[ ] 86142  ** Jump to the P2 parameter of that Yield.
[ ] 86143  ** After the jump, register P1 becomes undefined.
[ ] 86144  **
[ ] 86145  ** See also: InitCoroutine
[ ] 86146  */
[ ] 86147  case OP_EndCoroutine: {           /* in1 */
[ ] 86148    VdbeOp *pCaller;
[ ] 86149    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86150    assert( pIn1->flags==MEM_Int );
[ ] 86151    assert( pIn1->u.i>=0 && pIn1->u.i<p->nOp );
[ ] 86152    pCaller = &aOp[pIn1->u.i];
[ ] 86153    assert( pCaller->opcode==OP_Yield );
[ ] 86154    assert( pCaller->p2>=0 && pCaller->p2<p->nOp );
[ ] 86155    pOp = &aOp[pCaller->p2 - 1];
[ ] 86156    pIn1->flags = MEM_Undefined;
[ ] 86157    break;
[ ] 86158  }
[ ] 86159
[ ] 86160  /* Opcode:  Yield P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 86161  **
[ ] 86162  ** Swap the program counter with the value in register P1.  This
[ ] 86163  ** has the effect of yielding to a coroutine.
[ ] 86164  **
[ ] 86165  ** If the coroutine that is launched by this instruction ends with
[ ] 86166  ** Yield or Return then continue to the next instruction.  But if
[ ] 86167  ** the coroutine launched by this instruction ends with
[ ] 86168  ** EndCoroutine, then jump to P2 rather than continuing with the
[ ] 86169  ** next instruction.
[ ] 86170  **
[ ] 86171  ** See also: InitCoroutine
[ ] 86172  */
[ ] 86173  case OP_Yield: {            /* in1, jump */
[ ] 86174    int pcDest;
[ ] 86175    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86176    assert( VdbeMemDynamic(pIn1)==0 );
[ ] 86177    pIn1->flags = MEM_Int;
[ ] 86178    pcDest = (int)pIn1->u.i;
[ ] 86179    pIn1->u.i = (int)(pOp - aOp);
[ ] 86180    REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p1, pIn1);
[ ] 86181    pOp = &aOp[pcDest];
[ ] 86182    break;
[ ] 86183  }
[ ] 86184
[ ] 86185  /* Opcode:  HaltIfNull  P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 86186  ** Synopsis: if r[P3]=null halt
[ ] 86187  **
[ ] 86188  ** Check the value in register P3.  If it is NULL then Halt using
[ ] 86189  ** parameter P1, P2, and P4 as if this were a Halt instruction.  If the
[ ] 86190  ** value in register P3 is not NULL, then this routine is a no-op.
[ ] 86191  ** The P5 parameter should be 1.
[ ] 86192  */
[ ] 86193  case OP_HaltIfNull: {      /* in3 */
[ ] 86194    pIn3 = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 86195  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 86196    if( pOp->p2==OE_Abort ){ sqlite3VdbeAssertAbortable(p); }
[ ] 86197  #endif
[ ] 86198    if( (pIn3->flags & MEM_Null)==0 ) break;
[ ] 86199    /* Fall through into OP_Halt */
[ ] 86200  }
[ ] 86201
[ ] 86202  /* Opcode:  Halt P1 P2 * P4 P5
[ ] 86203  **
[ ] 86204  ** Exit immediately.  All open cursors, etc are closed
[ ] 86205  ** automatically.
[ ] 86206  **
[ ] 86207  ** P1 is the result code returned by sqlite3_exec(), sqlite3_reset(),
[ ] 86208  ** or sqlite3_finalize().  For a normal halt, this should be SQLITE_OK (0).
[ ] 86209  ** For errors, it can be some other value.  If P1!=0 then P2 will determine
[ ] 86210  ** whether or not to rollback the current transaction.  Do not rollback
[ ] 86211  ** if P2==OE_Fail. Do the rollback if P2==OE_Rollback.  If P2==OE_Abort,
[ ] 86212  ** then back out all changes that have occurred during this execution of the
[ ] 86213  ** VDBE, but do not rollback the transaction.
[ ] 86214  **
[ ] 86215  ** If P4 is not null then it is an error message string.
[ ] 86216  **
[ ] 86217  ** P5 is a value between 0 and 4, inclusive, that modifies the P4 string.
[ ] 86218  **
[ ] 86219  **    0:  (no change)
[ ] 86220  **    1:  NOT NULL contraint failed: P4
[ ] 86221  **    2:  UNIQUE constraint failed: P4
[ ] 86222  **    3:  CHECK constraint failed: P4
[ ] 86223  **    4:  FOREIGN KEY constraint failed: P4
[ ] 86224  **
[ ] 86225  ** If P5 is not zero and P4 is NULL, then everything after the ":" is
[ ] 86226  ** omitted.
[ ] 86227  **
[ ] 86228  ** There is an implied "Halt 0 0 0" instruction inserted at the very end of
[ ] 86229  ** every program.  So a jump past the last instruction of the program
[ ] 86230  ** is the same as executing Halt.
[ ] 86231  */
[B] 86232  case OP_Halt: {
[B] 86233    VdbeFrame *pFrame;
[B] 86234    int pcx;
[ ] 86235
[B] 86236    pcx = (int)(pOp - aOp);
[B] 86237  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[B] 86238    if( pOp->p2==OE_Abort ){ sqlite3VdbeAssertAbortable(p); }
[B] 86239  #endif
[B] 86240    if( pOp->p1==SQLITE_OK && p->pFrame ){
[ ] 86241      /* Halt the sub-program. Return control to the parent frame. */
[ ] 86242      pFrame = p->pFrame;
[ ] 86243      p->pFrame = pFrame->pParent;
[ ] 86244      p->nFrame--;
[ ] 86245      sqlite3VdbeSetChanges(db, p->nChange);
[ ] 86246      pcx = sqlite3VdbeFrameRestore(pFrame);
[ ] 86247      if( pOp->p2==OE_Ignore ){
[ ] 86248        /* Instruction pcx is the OP_Program that invoked the sub-program
[ ] 86249        ** currently being halted. If the p2 instruction of this OP_Halt
[ ] 86250        ** instruction is set to OE_Ignore, then the sub-program is throwing
[ ] 86251        ** an IGNORE exception. In this case jump to the address specified
[ ] 86252        ** as the p2 of the calling OP_Program.  */
[ ] 86253        pcx = p->aOp[pcx].p2-1;
[ ] 86254      }
[ ] 86255      aOp = p->aOp;
[ ] 86256      aMem = p->aMem;
[ ] 86257      pOp = &aOp[pcx];
[ ] 86258      break;
[ ] 86259    }
[B] 86260    p->rc = pOp->p1;
[B] 86261    p->errorAction = (u8)pOp->p2;
[B] 86262    p->pc = pcx;
[B] 86263    assert( pOp->p5<=4 );
[B] 86264    if( p->rc ){
[ ] 86265      if( pOp->p5 ){
[ ] 86266        static const char * const azType[] = { "NOT NULL", "UNIQUE", "CHECK",
[ ] 86267                                               "FOREIGN KEY" };
[ ] 86268        testcase( pOp->p5==1 );
[ ] 86269        testcase( pOp->p5==2 );
[ ] 86270        testcase( pOp->p5==3 );
[ ] 86271        testcase( pOp->p5==4 );
[ ] 86272        sqlite3VdbeError(p, "%s constraint failed", azType[pOp->p5-1]);
[ ] 86273        if( pOp->p4.z ){
[ ] 86274          p->zErrMsg = sqlite3MPrintf(db, "%z: %s", p->zErrMsg, pOp->p4.z);
[ ] 86275        }
[ ] 86276      }else{
[ ] 86277        sqlite3VdbeError(p, "%s", pOp->p4.z);
[ ] 86278      }
[ ] 86279      sqlite3_log(pOp->p1, "abort at %d in [%s]: %s", pcx, p->zSql, p->zErrMsg);
[ ] 86280    }
[B] 86281    rc = sqlite3VdbeHalt(p);
[B] 86282    assert( rc==SQLITE_BUSY || rc==SQLITE_OK || rc==SQLITE_ERROR );
[B] 86283    if( rc==SQLITE_BUSY ){
[ ] 86284      p->rc = SQLITE_BUSY;
[B] 86285    }else{
[B] 86286      assert( rc==SQLITE_OK || (p->rc&0xff)==SQLITE_CONSTRAINT );
[B] 86287      assert( rc==SQLITE_OK || db->nDeferredCons>0 || db->nDeferredImmCons>0 );
[B] 86288      rc = p->rc ? SQLITE_ERROR : SQLITE_DONE;
[B] 86289    }
[B] 86290    goto vdbe_return;
[B] 86291  }
[ ] 86292
[ ] 86293  /* Opcode: Integer P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 86294  ** Synopsis: r[P2]=P1
[ ] 86295  **
[ ] 86296  ** The 32-bit integer value P1 is written into register P2.
[ ] 86297  */
[B] 86298  case OP_Integer: {         /* out2 */
[W] 86299    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[W] 86300    pOut->u.i = pOp->p1;
[W] 86301    break;
[B] 86302  }
[ ] 86303
[ ] 86304  /* Opcode: Int64 * P2 * P4 *
[ ] 86305  ** Synopsis: r[P2]=P4
[ ] 86306  **
[ ] 86307  ** P4 is a pointer to a 64-bit integer value.
[ ] 86308  ** Write that value into register P2.
[ ] 86309  */
[W] 86310  case OP_Int64: {           /* out2 */
[W] 86311    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[W] 86312    assert( pOp->p4.pI64!=0 );
[W] 86313    pOut->u.i = *pOp->p4.pI64;
[W] 86314    break;
[W] 86315  }
[ ] 86316
[ ] 86317  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_FLOATING_POINT
[ ] 86318  /* Opcode: Real * P2 * P4 *
[ ] 86319  ** Synopsis: r[P2]=P4
[ ] 86320  **
[ ] 86321  ** P4 is a pointer to a 64-bit floating point value.
[ ] 86322  ** Write that value into register P2.
[ ] 86323  */
[W] 86324  case OP_Real: {            /* same as TK_FLOAT, out2 */
[W] 86325    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[W] 86326    pOut->flags = MEM_Real;
[W] 86327    assert( !sqlite3IsNaN(*pOp->p4.pReal) );
[W] 86328    pOut->u.r = *pOp->p4.pReal;
[W] 86329    break;
[W] 86330  }
[ ] 86331  #endif
[ ] 86332
[ ] 86333  /* Opcode: String8 * P2 * P4 *
[ ] 86334  ** Synopsis: r[P2]='P4'
[ ] 86335  **
[ ] 86336  ** P4 points to a nul terminated UTF-8 string. This opcode is transformed
[ ] 86337  ** into a String opcode before it is executed for the first time.  During
[ ] 86338  ** this transformation, the length of string P4 is computed and stored
[ ] 86339  ** as the P1 parameter.
[ ] 86340  */
[ ] 86341  case OP_String8: {         /* same as TK_STRING, out2 */
[ ] 86342    assert( pOp->p4.z!=0 );
[ ] 86343    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 86344    pOp->p1 = sqlite3Strlen30(pOp->p4.z);
[ ] 86345
[ ] 86346  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_UTF16
[ ] 86347    if( encoding!=SQLITE_UTF8 ){
[ ] 86348      rc = sqlite3VdbeMemSetStr(pOut, pOp->p4.z, -1, SQLITE_UTF8, SQLITE_STATIC);
[ ] 86349      assert( rc==SQLITE_OK || rc==SQLITE_TOOBIG );
[ ] 86350      if( rc ) goto too_big;
[ ] 86351      if( SQLITE_OK!=sqlite3VdbeChangeEncoding(pOut, encoding) ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 86352      assert( pOut->szMalloc>0 && pOut->zMalloc==pOut->z );
[ ] 86353      assert( VdbeMemDynamic(pOut)==0 );
[ ] 86354      pOut->szMalloc = 0;
[ ] 86355      pOut->flags |= MEM_Static;
[ ] 86356      if( pOp->p4type==P4_DYNAMIC ){
[ ] 86357        sqlite3DbFree(db, pOp->p4.z);
[ ] 86358      }
[ ] 86359      pOp->p4type = P4_DYNAMIC;
[ ] 86360      pOp->p4.z = pOut->z;
[ ] 86361      pOp->p1 = pOut->n;
[ ] 86362    }
[ ] 86363  #endif
[ ] 86364    if( pOp->p1>db->aLimit[SQLITE_LIMIT_LENGTH] ){
[ ] 86365      goto too_big;
[ ] 86366    }
[ ] 86367    pOp->opcode = OP_String;
[ ] 86368    assert( rc==SQLITE_OK );
[ ] 86369    /* Fall through to the next case, OP_String */
[ ] 86370  }
[ ] 86371
[ ] 86372  /* Opcode: String P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 86373  ** Synopsis: r[P2]='P4' (len=P1)
[ ] 86374  **
[ ] 86375  ** The string value P4 of length P1 (bytes) is stored in register P2.
[ ] 86376  **
[ ] 86377  ** If P3 is not zero and the content of register P3 is equal to P5, then
[ ] 86378  ** the datatype of the register P2 is converted to BLOB.  The content is
[ ] 86379  ** the same sequence of bytes, it is merely interpreted as a BLOB instead
[ ] 86380  ** of a string, as if it had been CAST.  In other words:
[ ] 86381  **
[ ] 86382  ** if( P3!=0 and reg[P3]==P5 ) reg[P2] := CAST(reg[P2] as BLOB)
[ ] 86383  */
[ ] 86384  case OP_String: {          /* out2 */
[ ] 86385    assert( pOp->p4.z!=0 );
[ ] 86386    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 86387    pOut->flags = MEM_Str|MEM_Static|MEM_Term;
[ ] 86388    pOut->z = pOp->p4.z;
[ ] 86389    pOut->n = pOp->p1;
[ ] 86390    pOut->enc = encoding;
[ ] 86391    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pOut);
[ ] 86392  #ifndef SQLITE_LIKE_DOESNT_MATCH_BLOBS
[ ] 86393    if( pOp->p3>0 ){
[ ] 86394      assert( pOp->p3<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 86395      pIn3 = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 86396      assert( pIn3->flags & MEM_Int );
[ ] 86397      if( pIn3->u.i==pOp->p5 ) pOut->flags = MEM_Blob|MEM_Static|MEM_Term;
[ ] 86398    }
[ ] 86399  #endif
[ ] 86400    break;
[ ] 86401  }
[ ] 86402
[ ] 86403  /* Opcode: Null P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86404  ** Synopsis: r[P2..P3]=NULL
[ ] 86405  **
[ ] 86406  ** Write a NULL into registers P2.  If P3 greater than P2, then also write
[ ] 86407  ** NULL into register P3 and every register in between P2 and P3.  If P3
[ ] 86408  ** is less than P2 (typically P3 is zero) then only register P2 is
[ ] 86409  ** set to NULL.
[ ] 86410  **
[ ] 86411  ** If the P1 value is non-zero, then also set the MEM_Cleared flag so that
[ ] 86412  ** NULL values will not compare equal even if SQLITE_NULLEQ is set on
[ ] 86413  ** OP_Ne or OP_Eq.
[ ] 86414  */
[ ] 86415  case OP_Null: {           /* out2 */
[ ] 86416    int cnt;
[ ] 86417    u16 nullFlag;
[ ] 86418    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 86419    cnt = pOp->p3-pOp->p2;
[ ] 86420    assert( pOp->p3<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 86421    pOut->flags = nullFlag = pOp->p1 ? (MEM_Null|MEM_Cleared) : MEM_Null;
[ ] 86422    pOut->n = 0;
[ ] 86423  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 86424    pOut->uTemp = 0;
[ ] 86425  #endif
[ ] 86426    while( cnt>0 ){
[ ] 86427      pOut++;
[ ] 86428      memAboutToChange(p, pOut);
[ ] 86429      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pOut);
[ ] 86430      pOut->flags = nullFlag;
[ ] 86431      pOut->n = 0;
[ ] 86432      cnt--;
[ ] 86433    }
[ ] 86434    break;
[ ] 86435  }
[ ] 86436
[ ] 86437  /* Opcode: SoftNull P1 * * * *
[ ] 86438  ** Synopsis: r[P1]=NULL
[ ] 86439  **
[ ] 86440  ** Set register P1 to have the value NULL as seen by the OP_MakeRecord
[ ] 86441  ** instruction, but do not free any string or blob memory associated with
[ ] 86442  ** the register, so that if the value was a string or blob that was
[ ] 86443  ** previously copied using OP_SCopy, the copies will continue to be valid.
[ ] 86444  */
[ ] 86445  case OP_SoftNull: {
[ ] 86446    assert( pOp->p1>0 && pOp->p1<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 86447    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86448    pOut->flags = (pOut->flags&~(MEM_Undefined|MEM_AffMask))|MEM_Null;
[ ] 86449    break;
[ ] 86450  }
[ ] 86451
[ ] 86452  /* Opcode: Blob P1 P2 * P4 *
[ ] 86453  ** Synopsis: r[P2]=P4 (len=P1)
[ ] 86454  **
[ ] 86455  ** P4 points to a blob of data P1 bytes long.  Store this
[ ] 86456  ** blob in register P2.
[ ] 86457  */
[ ] 86458  case OP_Blob: {                /* out2 */
[ ] 86459    assert( pOp->p1 <= SQLITE_MAX_LENGTH );
[ ] 86460    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 86461    sqlite3VdbeMemSetStr(pOut, pOp->p4.z, pOp->p1, 0, 0);
[ ] 86462    pOut->enc = encoding;
[ ] 86463    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pOut);
[ ] 86464    break;
[ ] 86465  }
[ ] 86466
[ ] 86467  /* Opcode: Variable P1 P2 * P4 *
[ ] 86468  ** Synopsis: r[P2]=parameter(P1,P4)
[ ] 86469  **
[ ] 86470  ** Transfer the values of bound parameter P1 into register P2
[ ] 86471  **
[ ] 86472  ** If the parameter is named, then its name appears in P4.
[ ] 86473  ** The P4 value is used by sqlite3_bind_parameter_name().
[ ] 86474  */
[ ] 86475  case OP_Variable: {            /* out2 */
[ ] 86476    Mem *pVar;       /* Value being transferred */
[ ] 86477
[ ] 86478    assert( pOp->p1>0 && pOp->p1<=p->nVar );
[ ] 86479    assert( pOp->p4.z==0 || pOp->p4.z==sqlite3VListNumToName(p->pVList,pOp->p1) );
[ ] 86480    pVar = &p->aVar[pOp->p1 - 1];
[ ] 86481    if( sqlite3VdbeMemTooBig(pVar) ){
[ ] 86482      goto too_big;
[ ] 86483    }
[ ] 86484    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 86485    if( VdbeMemDynamic(pOut) ) sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pOut);
[ ] 86486    memcpy(pOut, pVar, MEMCELLSIZE);
[ ] 86487    pOut->flags &= ~(MEM_Dyn|MEM_Ephem);
[ ] 86488    pOut->flags |= MEM_Static|MEM_FromBind;
[ ] 86489    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pOut);
[ ] 86490    break;
[ ] 86491  }
[ ] 86492
[ ] 86493  /* Opcode: Move P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86494  ** Synopsis: r[P2@P3]=r[P1@P3]
[ ] 86495  **
[ ] 86496  ** Move the P3 values in register P1..P1+P3-1 over into
[ ] 86497  ** registers P2..P2+P3-1.  Registers P1..P1+P3-1 are
[ ] 86498  ** left holding a NULL.  It is an error for register ranges
[ ] 86499  ** P1..P1+P3-1 and P2..P2+P3-1 to overlap.  It is an error
[ ] 86500  ** for P3 to be less than 1.
[ ] 86501  */
[ ] 86502  case OP_Move: {
[ ] 86503    int n;           /* Number of registers left to copy */
[ ] 86504    int p1;          /* Register to copy from */
[ ] 86505    int p2;          /* Register to copy to */
[ ] 86506
[ ] 86507    n = pOp->p3;
[ ] 86508    p1 = pOp->p1;
[ ] 86509    p2 = pOp->p2;
[ ] 86510    assert( n>0 && p1>0 && p2>0 );
[ ] 86511    assert( p1+n<=p2 || p2+n<=p1 );
[ ] 86512
[ ] 86513    pIn1 = &aMem[p1];
[ ] 86514    pOut = &aMem[p2];
[ ] 86515    do{
[ ] 86516      assert( pOut<=&aMem[(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)] );
[ ] 86517      assert( pIn1<=&aMem[(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)] );
[ ] 86518      assert( memIsValid(pIn1) );
[ ] 86519      memAboutToChange(p, pOut);
[ ] 86520      sqlite3VdbeMemMove(pOut, pIn1);
[ ] 86521  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 86522      pIn1->pScopyFrom = 0;
[ ] 86523      { int i;
[ ] 86524        for(i=1; i<p->nMem; i++){
[ ] 86525          if( aMem[i].pScopyFrom==pIn1 ){
[ ] 86526            aMem[i].pScopyFrom = pOut;
[ ] 86527          }
[ ] 86528        }
[ ] 86529      }
[ ] 86530  #endif
[ ] 86531      Deephemeralize(pOut);
[ ] 86532      REGISTER_TRACE(p2++, pOut);
[ ] 86533      pIn1++;
[ ] 86534      pOut++;
[ ] 86535    }while( --n );
[ ] 86536    break;
[ ] 86537  }
[ ] 86538
[ ] 86539  /* Opcode: Copy P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86540  ** Synopsis: r[P2@P3+1]=r[P1@P3+1]
[ ] 86541  **
[ ] 86542  ** Make a copy of registers P1..P1+P3 into registers P2..P2+P3.
[ ] 86543  **
[ ] 86544  ** This instruction makes a deep copy of the value.  A duplicate
[ ] 86545  ** is made of any string or blob constant.  See also OP_SCopy.
[ ] 86546  */
[ ] 86547  case OP_Copy: {
[ ] 86548    int n;
[ ] 86549
[ ] 86550    n = pOp->p3;
[ ] 86551    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86552    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 86553    assert( pOut!=pIn1 );
[ ] 86554    while( 1 ){
[ ] 86555      memAboutToChange(p, pOut);
[ ] 86556      sqlite3VdbeMemShallowCopy(pOut, pIn1, MEM_Ephem);
[ ] 86557      Deephemeralize(pOut);
[ ] 86558  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 86559      pOut->pScopyFrom = 0;
[ ] 86560  #endif
[ ] 86561      REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p2+pOp->p3-n, pOut);
[ ] 86562      if( (n--)==0 ) break;
[ ] 86563      pOut++;
[ ] 86564      pIn1++;
[ ] 86565    }
[ ] 86566    break;
[ ] 86567  }
[ ] 86568
[ ] 86569  /* Opcode: SCopy P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 86570  ** Synopsis: r[P2]=r[P1]
[ ] 86571  **
[ ] 86572  ** Make a shallow copy of register P1 into register P2.
[ ] 86573  **
[ ] 86574  ** This instruction makes a shallow copy of the value.  If the value
[ ] 86575  ** is a string or blob, then the copy is only a pointer to the
[ ] 86576  ** original and hence if the original changes so will the copy.
[ ] 86577  ** Worse, if the original is deallocated, the copy becomes invalid.
[ ] 86578  ** Thus the program must guarantee that the original will not change
[ ] 86579  ** during the lifetime of the copy.  Use OP_Copy to make a complete
[ ] 86580  ** copy.
[ ] 86581  */
[ ] 86582  case OP_SCopy: {            /* out2 */
[ ] 86583    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86584    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 86585    assert( pOut!=pIn1 );
[ ] 86586    sqlite3VdbeMemShallowCopy(pOut, pIn1, MEM_Ephem);
[ ] 86587  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 86588    pOut->pScopyFrom = pIn1;
[ ] 86589    pOut->mScopyFlags = pIn1->flags;
[ ] 86590  #endif
[ ] 86591    break;
[ ] 86592  }
[ ] 86593
[ ] 86594  /* Opcode: IntCopy P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 86595  ** Synopsis: r[P2]=r[P1]
[ ] 86596  **
[ ] 86597  ** Transfer the integer value held in register P1 into register P2.
[ ] 86598  **
[ ] 86599  ** This is an optimized version of SCopy that works only for integer
[ ] 86600  ** values.
[ ] 86601  */
[ ] 86602  case OP_IntCopy: {            /* out2 */
[ ] 86603    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86604    assert( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Int)!=0 );
[ ] 86605    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 86606    sqlite3VdbeMemSetInt64(pOut, pIn1->u.i);
[ ] 86607    break;
[ ] 86608  }
[ ] 86609
[ ] 86610  /* Opcode: ResultRow P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 86611  ** Synopsis: output=r[P1@P2]
[ ] 86612  **
[ ] 86613  ** The registers P1 through P1+P2-1 contain a single row of
[ ] 86614  ** results. This opcode causes the sqlite3_step() call to terminate
[ ] 86615  ** with an SQLITE_ROW return code and it sets up the sqlite3_stmt
[ ] 86616  ** structure to provide access to the r(P1)..r(P1+P2-1) values as
[ ] 86617  ** the result row.
[ ] 86618  */
[W] 86619  case OP_ResultRow: {
[W] 86620    Mem *pMem;
[W] 86621    int i;
[W] 86622    assert( p->nResColumn==pOp->p2 );
[W] 86623    assert( pOp->p1>0 );
[W] 86624    assert( pOp->p1+pOp->p2<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)+1 );
[ ] 86625
[ ] 86626    /* If this statement has violated immediate foreign key constraints, do
[ ] 86627    ** not return the number of rows modified. And do not RELEASE the statement
[ ] 86628    ** transaction. It needs to be rolled back.  */
[W] 86629    if( SQLITE_OK!=(rc = sqlite3VdbeCheckFk(p, 0)) ){
[ ] 86630      assert( db->flags&SQLITE_CountRows );
[ ] 86631      assert( p->usesStmtJournal );
[ ] 86632      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 86633    }
[ ] 86634
[ ] 86635    /* If the SQLITE_CountRows flag is set in sqlite3.flags mask, then
[ ] 86636    ** DML statements invoke this opcode to return the number of rows
[ ] 86637    ** modified to the user. This is the only way that a VM that
[ ] 86638    ** opens a statement transaction may invoke this opcode.
[ ] 86639    **
[ ] 86640    ** In case this is such a statement, close any statement transaction
[ ] 86641    ** opened by this VM before returning control to the user. This is to
[ ] 86642    ** ensure that statement-transactions are always nested, not overlapping.
[ ] 86643    ** If the open statement-transaction is not closed here, then the user
[ ] 86644    ** may step another VM that opens its own statement transaction. This
[ ] 86645    ** may lead to overlapping statement transactions.
[ ] 86646    **
[ ] 86647    ** The statement transaction is never a top-level transaction.  Hence
[ ] 86648    ** the RELEASE call below can never fail.
[ ] 86649    */
[W] 86650    assert( p->iStatement==0 || db->flags&SQLITE_CountRows );
[W] 86651    rc = sqlite3VdbeCloseStatement(p, SAVEPOINT_RELEASE);
[W] 86652    assert( rc==SQLITE_OK );
[ ] 86653
[ ] 86654    /* Invalidate all ephemeral cursor row caches */
[W] 86655    p->cacheCtr = (p->cacheCtr + 2)|1;
[ ] 86656
[ ] 86657    /* Make sure the results of the current row are \000 terminated
[ ] 86658    ** and have an assigned type.  The results are de-ephemeralized as
[ ] 86659    ** a side effect.
[ ] 86660    */
[W] 86661    pMem = p->pResultSet = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[W] 86662    for(i=0; i<pOp->p2; i++){
[W] 86663      assert( memIsValid(&pMem[i]) );
[W] 86664      Deephemeralize(&pMem[i]);
[W] 86665      assert( (pMem[i].flags & MEM_Ephem)==0
[W] 86666              || (pMem[i].flags & (MEM_Str|MEM_Blob))==0 );
[W] 86667      sqlite3VdbeMemNulTerminate(&pMem[i]);
[W] 86668      REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p1+i, &pMem[i]);
[W] 86669  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 86670      /* The registers in the result will not be used again when the
[ ] 86671      ** prepared statement restarts.  This is because sqlite3_column()
[ ] 86672      ** APIs might have caused type conversions of made other changes to
[ ] 86673      ** the register values.  Therefore, we can go ahead and break any
[ ] 86674      ** OP_SCopy dependencies. */
[W] 86675      pMem[i].pScopyFrom = 0;
[W] 86676  #endif
[W] 86677    }
[W] 86678    if( db->mallocFailed ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 86679
[W] 86680    if( db->mTrace & SQLITE_TRACE_ROW ){
[ ] 86681      db->xTrace(SQLITE_TRACE_ROW, db->pTraceArg, p, 0);
[ ] 86682    }
[ ] 86683
[ ] 86684
[ ] 86685    /* Return SQLITE_ROW
[ ] 86686    */
[W] 86687    p->pc = (int)(pOp - aOp) + 1;
[W] 86688    rc = SQLITE_ROW;
[W] 86689    goto vdbe_return;
[W] 86690  }
[ ] 86691
[ ] 86692  /* Opcode: Concat P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86693  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P2]+r[P1]
[ ] 86694  **
[ ] 86695  ** Add the text in register P1 onto the end of the text in
[ ] 86696  ** register P2 and store the result in register P3.
[ ] 86697  ** If either the P1 or P2 text are NULL then store NULL in P3.
[ ] 86698  **
[ ] 86699  **   P3 = P2 || P1
[ ] 86700  **
[ ] 86701  ** It is illegal for P1 and P3 to be the same register. Sometimes,
[ ] 86702  ** if P3 is the same register as P2, the implementation is able
[ ] 86703  ** to avoid a memcpy().
[ ] 86704  */
[ ] 86705  case OP_Concat: {           /* same as TK_CONCAT, in1, in2, out3 */
[ ] 86706    i64 nByte;          /* Total size of the output string or blob */
[ ] 86707    u16 flags1;         /* Initial flags for P1 */
[ ] 86708    u16 flags2;         /* Initial flags for P2 */
[ ] 86709
[ ] 86710    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 86711    pIn2 = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 86712    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 86713    testcase( pOut==pIn2 );
[ ] 86714    assert( pIn1!=pOut );
[ ] 86715    flags1 = pIn1->flags;
[ ] 86716    testcase( flags1 & MEM_Null );
[ ] 86717    testcase( pIn2->flags & MEM_Null );
[ ] 86718    if( (flags1 | pIn2->flags) & MEM_Null ){
[ ] 86719      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pOut);
[ ] 86720      break;
[ ] 86721    }
[ ] 86722    if( (flags1 & (MEM_Str|MEM_Blob))==0 ){
[ ] 86723      if( sqlite3VdbeMemStringify(pIn1,encoding,0) ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 86724      flags1 = pIn1->flags & ~MEM_Str;
[ ] 86725    }else if( (flags1 & MEM_Zero)!=0 ){
[ ] 86726      if( sqlite3VdbeMemExpandBlob(pIn1) ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 86727      flags1 = pIn1->flags & ~MEM_Str;
[ ] 86728    }
[ ] 86729    flags2 = pIn2->flags;
[ ] 86730    if( (flags2 & (MEM_Str|MEM_Blob))==0 ){
[ ] 86731      if( sqlite3VdbeMemStringify(pIn2,encoding,0) ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 86732      flags2 = pIn2->flags & ~MEM_Str;
[ ] 86733    }else if( (flags2 & MEM_Zero)!=0 ){
[ ] 86734      if( sqlite3VdbeMemExpandBlob(pIn2) ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 86735      flags2 = pIn2->flags & ~MEM_Str;
[ ] 86736    }
[ ] 86737    nByte = pIn1->n + pIn2->n;
[ ] 86738    if( nByte>db->aLimit[SQLITE_LIMIT_LENGTH] ){
[ ] 86739      goto too_big;
[ ] 86740    }
[ ] 86741    if( sqlite3VdbeMemGrow(pOut, (int)nByte+3, pOut==pIn2) ){
[ ] 86742      goto no_mem;
[ ] 86743    }
[ ] 86744    MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Str);
[ ] 86745    if( pOut!=pIn2 ){
[ ] 86746      memcpy(pOut->z, pIn2->z, pIn2->n);
[ ] 86747      assert( (pIn2->flags & MEM_Dyn) == (flags2 & MEM_Dyn) );
[ ] 86748      pIn2->flags = flags2;
[ ] 86749    }
[ ] 86750    memcpy(&pOut->z[pIn2->n], pIn1->z, pIn1->n);
[ ] 86751    assert( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Dyn) == (flags1 & MEM_Dyn) );
[ ] 86752    pIn1->flags = flags1;
[ ] 86753    pOut->z[nByte]=0;
[ ] 86754    pOut->z[nByte+1] = 0;
[ ] 86755    pOut->z[nByte+2] = 0;
[ ] 86756    pOut->flags |= MEM_Term;
[ ] 86757    pOut->n = (int)nByte;
[ ] 86758    pOut->enc = encoding;
[ ] 86759    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pOut);
[ ] 86760    break;
[ ] 86761  }
[ ] 86762
[ ] 86763  /* Opcode: Add P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86764  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P1]+r[P2]
[ ] 86765  **
[ ] 86766  ** Add the value in register P1 to the value in register P2
[ ] 86767  ** and store the result in register P3.
[ ] 86768  ** If either input is NULL, the result is NULL.
[ ] 86769  */
[ ] 86770  /* Opcode: Multiply P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86771  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P1]*r[P2]
[ ] 86772  **
[ ] 86773  **
[ ] 86774  ** Multiply the value in register P1 by the value in register P2
[ ] 86775  ** and store the result in register P3.
[ ] 86776  ** If either input is NULL, the result is NULL.
[ ] 86777  */
[ ] 86778  /* Opcode: Subtract P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86779  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P2]-r[P1]
[ ] 86780  **
[ ] 86781  ** Subtract the value in register P1 from the value in register P2
[ ] 86782  ** and store the result in register P3.
[ ] 86783  ** If either input is NULL, the result is NULL.
[ ] 86784  */
[ ] 86785  /* Opcode: Divide P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86786  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P2]/r[P1]
[ ] 86787  **
[ ] 86788  ** Divide the value in register P1 by the value in register P2
[ ] 86789  ** and store the result in register P3 (P3=P2/P1). If the value in
[ ] 86790  ** register P1 is zero, then the result is NULL. If either input is
[ ] 86791  ** NULL, the result is NULL.
[ ] 86792  */
[ ] 86793  /* Opcode: Remainder P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86794  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P2]%r[P1]
[ ] 86795  **
[ ] 86796  ** Compute the remainder after integer register P2 is divided by
[ ] 86797  ** register P1 and store the result in register P3.
[ ] 86798  ** If the value in register P1 is zero the result is NULL.
[ ] 86799  ** If either operand is NULL, the result is NULL.
[ ] 86800  */
[ ] 86801  case OP_Add:                   /* same as TK_PLUS, in1, in2, out3 */
[ ] 86802  case OP_Subtract:              /* same as TK_MINUS, in1, in2, out3 */
[W] 86803  case OP_Multiply:              /* same as TK_STAR, in1, in2, out3 */
[W] 86804  case OP_Divide:                /* same as TK_SLASH, in1, in2, out3 */
[W] 86805  case OP_Remainder: {           /* same as TK_REM, in1, in2, out3 */
[W] 86806    u16 flags;      /* Combined MEM_* flags from both inputs */
[W] 86807    u16 type1;      /* Numeric type of left operand */
[W] 86808    u16 type2;      /* Numeric type of right operand */
[W] 86809    i64 iA;         /* Integer value of left operand */
[W] 86810    i64 iB;         /* Integer value of right operand */
[W] 86811    double rA;      /* Real value of left operand */
[W] 86812    double rB;      /* Real value of right operand */
[ ] 86813
[W] 86814    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[W] 86815    type1 = numericType(pIn1);
[W] 86816    pIn2 = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[W] 86817    type2 = numericType(pIn2);
[W] 86818    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[W] 86819    flags = pIn1->flags | pIn2->flags;
[W] 86820    if( (type1 & type2 & MEM_Int)!=0 ){
[W] 86821      iA = pIn1->u.i;
[W] 86822      iB = pIn2->u.i;
[W] 86823      switch( pOp->opcode ){
[ ] 86824        case OP_Add:       if( sqlite3AddInt64(&iB,iA) ) goto fp_math;  break;
[ ] 86825        case OP_Subtract:  if( sqlite3SubInt64(&iB,iA) ) goto fp_math;  break;
[W] 86826        case OP_Multiply:  if( sqlite3MulInt64(&iB,iA) ) goto fp_math;  break;
[W] 86827        case OP_Divide: {
[ ] 86828          if( iA==0 ) goto arithmetic_result_is_null;
[ ] 86829          if( iA==-1 && iB==SMALLEST_INT64 ) goto fp_math;
[ ] 86830          iB /= iA;
[ ] 86831          break;
[ ] 86832        }
[W] 86833        default: {
[W] 86834          if( iA==0 ) goto arithmetic_result_is_null;
[W] 86835          if( iA==-1 ) iA = 1;
[W] 86836          iB %= iA;
[W] 86837          break;
[W] 86838        }
[W] 86839      }
[W] 86840      pOut->u.i = iB;
[W] 86841      MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Int);
[W] 86842    }else if( (flags & MEM_Null)!=0 ){
[ ] 86843      goto arithmetic_result_is_null;
[ ] 86844    }else{
[ ] 86845  fp_math:
[ ] 86846      rA = sqlite3VdbeRealValue(pIn1);
[ ] 86847      rB = sqlite3VdbeRealValue(pIn2);
[ ] 86848      switch( pOp->opcode ){
[ ] 86849        case OP_Add:         rB += rA;       break;
[ ] 86850        case OP_Subtract:    rB -= rA;       break;
[ ] 86851        case OP_Multiply:    rB *= rA;       break;
[ ] 86852        case OP_Divide: {
[ ] 86853          /* (double)0 In case of SQLITE_OMIT_FLOATING_POINT... */
[ ] 86854          if( rA==(double)0 ) goto arithmetic_result_is_null;
[ ] 86855          rB /= rA;
[ ] 86856          break;
[ ] 86857        }
[ ] 86858        default: {
[ ] 86859          iA = sqlite3VdbeIntValue(pIn1);
[ ] 86860          iB = sqlite3VdbeIntValue(pIn2);
[ ] 86861          if( iA==0 ) goto arithmetic_result_is_null;
[ ] 86862          if( iA==-1 ) iA = 1;
[ ] 86863          rB = (double)(iB % iA);
[ ] 86864          break;
[ ] 86865        }
[ ] 86866      }
[ ] 86867  #ifdef SQLITE_OMIT_FLOATING_POINT
[ ] 86868      pOut->u.i = rB;
[ ] 86869      MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Int);
[ ] 86870  #else
[ ] 86871      if( sqlite3IsNaN(rB) ){
[ ] 86872        goto arithmetic_result_is_null;
[ ] 86873      }
[ ] 86874      pOut->u.r = rB;
[ ] 86875      MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Real);
[ ] 86876  #endif
[ ] 86877    }
[W] 86878    break;
[ ] 86879
[W] 86880  arithmetic_result_is_null:
[ ] 86881    sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pOut);
[ ] 86882    break;
[W] 86883  }
[ ] 86884
[ ] 86885  /* Opcode: CollSeq P1 * * P4
[ ] 86886  **
[ ] 86887  ** P4 is a pointer to a CollSeq object. If the next call to a user function
[ ] 86888  ** or aggregate calls sqlite3GetFuncCollSeq(), this collation sequence will
[ ] 86889  ** be returned. This is used by the built-in min(), max() and nullif()
[ ] 86890  ** functions.
[ ] 86891  **
[ ] 86892  ** If P1 is not zero, then it is a register that a subsequent min() or
[ ] 86893  ** max() aggregate will set to 1 if the current row is not the minimum or
[ ] 86894  ** maximum.  The P1 register is initialized to 0 by this instruction.
[ ] 86895  **
[ ] 86896  ** The interface used by the implementation of the aforementioned functions
[ ] 86897  ** to retrieve the collation sequence set by this opcode is not available
[ ] 86898  ** publicly.  Only built-in functions have access to this feature.
[ ] 86899  */
[ ] 86900  case OP_CollSeq: {
[ ] 86901    assert( pOp->p4type==P4_COLLSEQ );
[ ] 86902    if( pOp->p1 ){
[ ] 86903      sqlite3VdbeMemSetInt64(&aMem[pOp->p1], 0);
[ ] 86904    }
[ ] 86905    break;
[ ] 86906  }
[ ] 86907
[ ] 86908  /* Opcode: BitAnd P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86909  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P1]&r[P2]
[ ] 86910  **
[ ] 86911  ** Take the bit-wise AND of the values in register P1 and P2 and
[ ] 86912  ** store the result in register P3.
[ ] 86913  ** If either input is NULL, the result is NULL.
[ ] 86914  */
[ ] 86915  /* Opcode: BitOr P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86916  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P1]|r[P2]
[ ] 86917  **
[ ] 86918  ** Take the bit-wise OR of the values in register P1 and P2 and
[ ] 86919  ** store the result in register P3.
[ ] 86920  ** If either input is NULL, the result is NULL.
[ ] 86921  */
[ ] 86922  /* Opcode: ShiftLeft P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86923  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P2]<<r[P1]
[ ] 86924  **
[ ] 86925  ** Shift the integer value in register P2 to the left by the
[ ] 86926  ** number of bits specified by the integer in register P1.
[ ] 86927  ** Store the result in register P3.
[ ] 86928  ** If either input is NULL, the result is NULL.
[ ] 86929  */
[ ] 86930  /* Opcode: ShiftRight P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 86931  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=r[P2]>>r[P1]
[ ] 86932  **
[ ] 86933  ** Shift the integer value in register P2 to the right by the
[ ] 86934  ** number of bits specified by the integer in register P1.
[ ] 86935  ** Store the result in register P3.
[ ] 86936  ** If either input is NULL, the result is NULL.
[ ] 86937  */
[ ] 86938  case OP_BitAnd:                 /* same as TK_BITAND, in1, in2, out3 */
[ ] 86939  case OP_BitOr:                  /* same as TK_BITOR, in1, in2, out3 */
[ ] 86940  case OP_ShiftLeft:              /* same as TK_LSHIFT, in1, in2, out3 */
[W] 86941  case OP_ShiftRight: {           /* same as TK_RSHIFT, in1, in2, out3 */ <-- BLOCKER
[W] 86942    i64 iA;
[W] 86943    u64 uA;
[W] 86944    i64 iB;
[W] 86945    u8 op;
[ ] 86946
[W] 86947    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[W] 86948    pIn2 = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[W] 86949    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[W] 86950    if( (pIn1->flags | pIn2->flags) & MEM_Null ){
[ ] 86951      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pOut);
[ ] 86952      break;
[ ] 86953    }
[W] 86954    iA = sqlite3VdbeIntValue(pIn2);
[W] 86955    iB = sqlite3VdbeIntValue(pIn1);
[W] 86956    op = pOp->opcode;
[W] 86957    if( op==OP_BitAnd ){
[ ] 86958      iA &= iB;
[W] 86959    }else if( op==OP_BitOr ){
[ ] 86960      iA |= iB;
[W] 86961    }else if( iB!=0 ){
[W] 86962      assert( op==OP_ShiftRight || op==OP_ShiftLeft );
[ ] 86963
[ ] 86964      /* If shifting by a negative amount, shift in the other direction */
[W] 86965      if( iB<0 ){
[ ] 86966        assert( OP_ShiftRight==OP_ShiftLeft+1 );
[ ] 86967        op = 2*OP_ShiftLeft + 1 - op;
[ ] 86968        iB = iB>(-64) ? -iB : 64;
[ ] 86969      }
[ ] 86970
[W] 86971      if( iB>=64 ){
[ ] 86972        iA = (iA>=0 || op==OP_ShiftLeft) ? 0 : -1;
[W] 86973      }else{
[W] 86974        memcpy(&uA, &iA, sizeof(uA));
[W] 86975        if( op==OP_ShiftLeft ){
[ ] 86976          uA <<= iB;
[W] 86977        }else{
[W] 86978          uA >>= iB;
[ ] 86979          /* Sign-extend on a right shift of a negative number */
[W] 86980          if( iA<0 ) uA |= ((((u64)0xffffffff)<<32)|0xffffffff) << (64-iB);
[W] 86981        }
[W] 86982        memcpy(&iA, &uA, sizeof(iA));
[W] 86983      }
[W] 86984    }
[W] 86985    pOut->u.i = iA;
[W] 86986    MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Int);
[W] 86987    break;
[W] 86988  }
[ ] 86989
[ ] 86990  /* Opcode: AddImm  P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 86991  ** Synopsis: r[P1]=r[P1]+P2
[ ] 86992  **
[ ] 86993  ** Add the constant P2 to the value in register P1.
[ ] 86994  ** The result is always an integer.
[ ] 86995  **
[ ] 86996  ** To force any register to be an integer, just add 0.
[ ] 86997  */
[ ] 86998  case OP_AddImm: {            /* in1 */
[ ] 86999    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87000    memAboutToChange(p, pIn1);
[ ] 87001    sqlite3VdbeMemIntegerify(pIn1);
[ ] 87002    pIn1->u.i += pOp->p2;
[ ] 87003    break;
[W] 87004  }
[ ] 87005
[ ] 87006  /* Opcode: MustBeInt P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 87007  **
[ ] 87008  ** Force the value in register P1 to be an integer.  If the value
[ ] 87009  ** in P1 is not an integer and cannot be converted into an integer
[ ] 87010  ** without data loss, then jump immediately to P2, or if P2==0
[ ] 87011  ** raise an SQLITE_MISMATCH exception.
[ ] 87012  */
[ ] 87013  case OP_MustBeInt: {            /* jump, in1 */
[ ] 87014    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87015    if( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Int)==0 ){
[ ] 87016      applyAffinity(pIn1, SQLITE_AFF_NUMERIC, encoding);
[ ] 87017      if( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Int)==0 ){
[ ] 87018        VdbeBranchTaken(1, 2);
[ ] 87019        if( pOp->p2==0 ){
[ ] 87020          rc = SQLITE_MISMATCH;
[ ] 87021          goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 87022        }else{
[ ] 87023          goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87024        }
[ ] 87025      }
[ ] 87026    }
[ ] 87027    VdbeBranchTaken(0, 2);
[ ] 87028    MemSetTypeFlag(pIn1, MEM_Int);
[ ] 87029    break;
[ ] 87030  }
[ ] 87031
[ ] 87032  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_FLOATING_POINT
[ ] 87033  /* Opcode: RealAffinity P1 * * * *
[ ] 87034  **
[ ] 87035  ** If register P1 holds an integer convert it to a real value.
[ ] 87036  **
[ ] 87037  ** This opcode is used when extracting information from a column that
[ ] 87038  ** has REAL affinity.  Such column values may still be stored as
[ ] 87039  ** integers, for space efficiency, but after extraction we want them
[ ] 87040  ** to have only a real value.
[ ] 87041  */
[ ] 87042  case OP_RealAffinity: {                  /* in1 */
[ ] 87043    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87044    if( pIn1->flags & (MEM_Int|MEM_IntReal) ){
[ ] 87045      testcase( pIn1->flags & MEM_Int );
[ ] 87046      testcase( pIn1->flags & MEM_IntReal );
[ ] 87047      sqlite3VdbeMemRealify(pIn1);
[ ] 87048      REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p1, pIn1);
[ ] 87049    }
[ ] 87050    break;
[ ] 87051  }
[ ] 87052  #endif
[ ] 87053
[ ] 87054  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_CAST
[ ] 87055  /* Opcode: Cast P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 87056  ** Synopsis: affinity(r[P1])
[ ] 87057  **
[ ] 87058  ** Force the value in register P1 to be the type defined by P2.
[ ] 87059  **
[ ] 87060  ** <ul>
[ ] 87061  ** <li> P2=='A' &rarr; BLOB
[ ] 87062  ** <li> P2=='B' &rarr; TEXT
[ ] 87063  ** <li> P2=='C' &rarr; NUMERIC
[ ] 87064  ** <li> P2=='D' &rarr; INTEGER
[ ] 87065  ** <li> P2=='E' &rarr; REAL
[ ] 87066  ** </ul>
[ ] 87067  **
[ ] 87068  ** A NULL value is not changed by this routine.  It remains NULL.
[ ] 87069  */
[ ] 87070  case OP_Cast: {                  /* in1 */
[ ] 87071    assert( pOp->p2>=SQLITE_AFF_BLOB && pOp->p2<=SQLITE_AFF_REAL );
[ ] 87072    testcase( pOp->p2==SQLITE_AFF_TEXT );
[ ] 87073    testcase( pOp->p2==SQLITE_AFF_BLOB );
[ ] 87074    testcase( pOp->p2==SQLITE_AFF_NUMERIC );
[ ] 87075    testcase( pOp->p2==SQLITE_AFF_INTEGER );
[ ] 87076    testcase( pOp->p2==SQLITE_AFF_REAL );
[ ] 87077    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87078    memAboutToChange(p, pIn1);
[ ] 87079    rc = ExpandBlob(pIn1);
[ ] 87080    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 87081    rc = sqlite3VdbeMemCast(pIn1, pOp->p2, encoding);
[ ] 87082    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 87083    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pIn1);
[ ] 87084    REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p1, pIn1);
[ ] 87085    break;
[ ] 87086  }
[ ] 87087  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_CAST */
[ ] 87088
[ ] 87089  /* Opcode: Eq P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 87090  ** Synopsis: IF r[P3]==r[P1]
[ ] 87091  **
[ ] 87092  ** Compare the values in register P1 and P3.  If reg(P3)==reg(P1) then
[ ] 87093  ** jump to address P2.  Or if the SQLITE_STOREP2 flag is set in P5, then
[ ] 87094  ** store the result of comparison in register P2.
[ ] 87095  **
[ ] 87096  ** The SQLITE_AFF_MASK portion of P5 must be an affinity character -
[ ] 87097  ** SQLITE_AFF_TEXT, SQLITE_AFF_INTEGER, and so forth. An attempt is made
[ ] 87098  ** to coerce both inputs according to this affinity before the
[ ] 87099  ** comparison is made. If the SQLITE_AFF_MASK is 0x00, then numeric
[ ] 87100  ** affinity is used. Note that the affinity conversions are stored
[ ] 87101  ** back into the input registers P1 and P3.  So this opcode can cause
[ ] 87102  ** persistent changes to registers P1 and P3.
[ ] 87103  **
[ ] 87104  ** Once any conversions have taken place, and neither value is NULL,
[ ] 87105  ** the values are compared. If both values are blobs then memcmp() is
[ ] 87106  ** used to determine the results of the comparison.  If both values
[ ] 87107  ** are text, then the appropriate collating function specified in
[ ] 87108  ** P4 is used to do the comparison.  If P4 is not specified then
[ ] 87109  ** memcmp() is used to compare text string.  If both values are
[ ] 87110  ** numeric, then a numeric comparison is used. If the two values
[ ] 87111  ** are of different types, then numbers are considered less than
[ ] 87112  ** strings and strings are considered less than blobs.
[ ] 87113  **
[ ] 87114  ** If SQLITE_NULLEQ is set in P5 then the result of comparison is always either
[ ] 87115  ** true or false and is never NULL.  If both operands are NULL then the result
[ ] 87116  ** of comparison is true.  If either operand is NULL then the result is false.
[ ] 87117  ** If neither operand is NULL the result is the same as it would be if
[ ] 87118  ** the SQLITE_NULLEQ flag were omitted from P5.
[ ] 87119  **
[ ] 87120  ** If both SQLITE_STOREP2 and SQLITE_KEEPNULL flags are set then the
[ ] 87121  ** content of r[P2] is only changed if the new value is NULL or 0 (false).
[ ] 87122  ** In other words, a prior r[P2] value will not be overwritten by 1 (true).
[ ] 87123  */
[ ] 87124  /* Opcode: Ne P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 87125  ** Synopsis: IF r[P3]!=r[P1]
[ ] 87126  **
[ ] 87127  ** This works just like the Eq opcode except that the jump is taken if
[ ] 87128  ** the operands in registers P1 and P3 are not equal.  See the Eq opcode for
[ ] 87129  ** additional information.
[ ] 87130  **
[ ] 87131  ** If both SQLITE_STOREP2 and SQLITE_KEEPNULL flags are set then the
[ ] 87132  ** content of r[P2] is only changed if the new value is NULL or 1 (true).
[ ] 87133  ** In other words, a prior r[P2] value will not be overwritten by 0 (false).
[ ] 87134  */
[ ] 87135  /* Opcode: Lt P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 87136  ** Synopsis: IF r[P3]<r[P1]
[ ] 87137  **
[ ] 87138  ** Compare the values in register P1 and P3.  If reg(P3)<reg(P1) then
[ ] 87139  ** jump to address P2.  Or if the SQLITE_STOREP2 flag is set in P5 store
[ ] 87140  ** the result of comparison (0 or 1 or NULL) into register P2.
[ ] 87141  **
[ ] 87142  ** If the SQLITE_JUMPIFNULL bit of P5 is set and either reg(P1) or
[ ] 87143  ** reg(P3) is NULL then the take the jump.  If the SQLITE_JUMPIFNULL
[ ] 87144  ** bit is clear then fall through if either operand is NULL.
[ ] 87145  **
[ ] 87146  ** The SQLITE_AFF_MASK portion of P5 must be an affinity character -
[ ] 87147  ** SQLITE_AFF_TEXT, SQLITE_AFF_INTEGER, and so forth. An attempt is made
[ ] 87148  ** to coerce both inputs according to this affinity before the
[ ] 87149  ** comparison is made. If the SQLITE_AFF_MASK is 0x00, then numeric
[ ] 87150  ** affinity is used. Note that the affinity conversions are stored
[ ] 87151  ** back into the input registers P1 and P3.  So this opcode can cause
[ ] 87152  ** persistent changes to registers P1 and P3.
[ ] 87153  **
[ ] 87154  ** Once any conversions have taken place, and neither value is NULL,
[ ] 87155  ** the values are compared. If both values are blobs then memcmp() is
[ ] 87156  ** used to determine the results of the comparison.  If both values
[ ] 87157  ** are text, then the appropriate collating function specified in
[ ] 87158  ** P4 is  used to do the comparison.  If P4 is not specified then
[ ] 87159  ** memcmp() is used to compare text string.  If both values are
[ ] 87160  ** numeric, then a numeric comparison is used. If the two values
[ ] 87161  ** are of different types, then numbers are considered less than
[ ] 87162  ** strings and strings are considered less than blobs.
[ ] 87163  */
[ ] 87164  /* Opcode: Le P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 87165  ** Synopsis: IF r[P3]<=r[P1]
[ ] 87166  **
[ ] 87167  ** This works just like the Lt opcode except that the jump is taken if
[ ] 87168  ** the content of register P3 is less than or equal to the content of
[ ] 87169  ** register P1.  See the Lt opcode for additional information.
[ ] 87170  */
[ ] 87171  /* Opcode: Gt P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 87172  ** Synopsis: IF r[P3]>r[P1]
[ ] 87173  **
[ ] 87174  ** This works just like the Lt opcode except that the jump is taken if
[ ] 87175  ** the content of register P3 is greater than the content of
[ ] 87176  ** register P1.  See the Lt opcode for additional information.
[ ] 87177  */
[ ] 87178  /* Opcode: Ge P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 87179  ** Synopsis: IF r[P3]>=r[P1]
[ ] 87180  **
[ ] 87181  ** This works just like the Lt opcode except that the jump is taken if
[ ] 87182  ** the content of register P3 is greater than or equal to the content of
[ ] 87183  ** register P1.  See the Lt opcode for additional information.
[ ] 87184  */
[W] 87185  case OP_Eq:               /* same as TK_EQ, jump, in1, in3 */
[W] 87186  case OP_Ne:               /* same as TK_NE, jump, in1, in3 */
[W] 87187  case OP_Lt:               /* same as TK_LT, jump, in1, in3 */
[W] 87188  case OP_Le:               /* same as TK_LE, jump, in1, in3 */
[W] 87189  case OP_Gt:               /* same as TK_GT, jump, in1, in3 */
[W] 87190  case OP_Ge: {             /* same as TK_GE, jump, in1, in3 */
[W] 87191    int res, res2;      /* Result of the comparison of pIn1 against pIn3 */
[W] 87192    char affinity;      /* Affinity to use for comparison */
[W] 87193    u16 flags1;         /* Copy of initial value of pIn1->flags */
[W] 87194    u16 flags3;         /* Copy of initial value of pIn3->flags */
[ ] 87195
[W] 87196    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[W] 87197    pIn3 = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[W] 87198    flags1 = pIn1->flags;
[W] 87199    flags3 = pIn3->flags;
[W] 87200    if( (flags1 | flags3)&MEM_Null ){
[ ] 87201      /* One or both operands are NULL */
[ ] 87202      if( pOp->p5 & SQLITE_NULLEQ ){
[ ] 87203        /* If SQLITE_NULLEQ is set (which will only happen if the operator is
[ ] 87204        ** OP_Eq or OP_Ne) then take the jump or not depending on whether
[ ] 87205        ** or not both operands are null.
[ ] 87206        */
[ ] 87207        assert( (flags1 & MEM_Cleared)==0 );
[ ] 87208        assert( (pOp->p5 & SQLITE_JUMPIFNULL)==0 || CORRUPT_DB );
[ ] 87209        testcase( (pOp->p5 & SQLITE_JUMPIFNULL)!=0 );
[ ] 87210        if( (flags1&flags3&MEM_Null)!=0
[ ] 87211         && (flags3&MEM_Cleared)==0
[ ] 87212        ){
[ ] 87213          res = 0;  /* Operands are equal */
[ ] 87214        }else{
[ ] 87215          res = ((flags3 & MEM_Null) ? -1 : +1);  /* Operands are not equal */
[ ] 87216        }
[ ] 87217      }else{
[ ] 87218        /* SQLITE_NULLEQ is clear and at least one operand is NULL,
[ ] 87219        ** then the result is always NULL.
[ ] 87220        ** The jump is taken if the SQLITE_JUMPIFNULL bit is set.
[ ] 87221        */
[ ] 87222        if( pOp->p5 & SQLITE_STOREP2 ){
[ ] 87223          pOut = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 87224          iCompare = 1;    /* Operands are not equal */
[ ] 87225          memAboutToChange(p, pOut);
[ ] 87226          MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Null);
[ ] 87227          REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p2, pOut);
[ ] 87228        }else{
[ ] 87229          VdbeBranchTaken(2,3);
[ ] 87230          if( pOp->p5 & SQLITE_JUMPIFNULL ){
[ ] 87231            goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87232          }
[ ] 87233        }
[ ] 87234        break;
[ ] 87235      }
[W] 87236    }else{
[ ] 87237      /* Neither operand is NULL.  Do a comparison. */
[W] 87238      affinity = pOp->p5 & SQLITE_AFF_MASK;
[W] 87239      if( affinity>=SQLITE_AFF_NUMERIC ){
[ ] 87240        if( (flags1 | flags3)&MEM_Str ){
[ ] 87241          if( (flags1 & (MEM_Int|MEM_IntReal|MEM_Real|MEM_Str))==MEM_Str ){
[ ] 87242            applyNumericAffinity(pIn1,0);
[ ] 87243            testcase( flags3==pIn3->flags );
[ ] 87244            flags3 = pIn3->flags;
[ ] 87245          }
[ ] 87246          if( (flags3 & (MEM_Int|MEM_IntReal|MEM_Real|MEM_Str))==MEM_Str ){
[ ] 87247            applyNumericAffinity(pIn3,0);
[ ] 87248          }
[ ] 87249        }
[ ] 87250        /* Handle the common case of integer comparison here, as an
[ ] 87251        ** optimization, to avoid a call to sqlite3MemCompare() */
[ ] 87252        if( (pIn1->flags & pIn3->flags & MEM_Int)!=0 ){
[ ] 87253          if( pIn3->u.i > pIn1->u.i ){ res = +1; goto compare_op; }
[ ] 87254          if( pIn3->u.i < pIn1->u.i ){ res = -1; goto compare_op; }
[ ] 87255          res = 0;
[ ] 87256          goto compare_op;
[ ] 87257        }
[W] 87258      }else if( affinity==SQLITE_AFF_TEXT ){
[ ] 87259        if( (flags1 & MEM_Str)==0 && (flags1&(MEM_Int|MEM_Real|MEM_IntReal))!=0 ){
[ ] 87260          testcase( pIn1->flags & MEM_Int );
[ ] 87261          testcase( pIn1->flags & MEM_Real );
[ ] 87262          testcase( pIn1->flags & MEM_IntReal );
[ ] 87263          sqlite3VdbeMemStringify(pIn1, encoding, 1);
[ ] 87264          testcase( (flags1&MEM_Dyn) != (pIn1->flags&MEM_Dyn) );
[ ] 87265          flags1 = (pIn1->flags & ~MEM_TypeMask) | (flags1 & MEM_TypeMask);
[ ] 87266          if( NEVER(pIn1==pIn3) ) flags3 = flags1 | MEM_Str;
[ ] 87267        }
[ ] 87268        if( (flags3 & MEM_Str)==0 && (flags3&(MEM_Int|MEM_Real|MEM_IntReal))!=0 ){
[ ] 87269          testcase( pIn3->flags & MEM_Int );
[ ] 87270          testcase( pIn3->flags & MEM_Real );
[ ] 87271          testcase( pIn3->flags & MEM_IntReal );
[ ] 87272          sqlite3VdbeMemStringify(pIn3, encoding, 1);
[ ] 87273          testcase( (flags3&MEM_Dyn) != (pIn3->flags&MEM_Dyn) );
[ ] 87274          flags3 = (pIn3->flags & ~MEM_TypeMask) | (flags3 & MEM_TypeMask);
[ ] 87275        }
[ ] 87276      }
[W] 87277      assert( pOp->p4type==P4_COLLSEQ || pOp->p4.pColl==0 );
[W] 87278      res = sqlite3MemCompare(pIn3, pIn1, pOp->p4.pColl);
[W] 87279    }
[W] 87280  compare_op:
[ ] 87281    /* At this point, res is negative, zero, or positive if reg[P1] is
[ ] 87282    ** less than, equal to, or greater than reg[P3], respectively.  Compute
[ ] 87283    ** the answer to this operator in res2, depending on what the comparison
[ ] 87284    ** operator actually is.  The next block of code depends on the fact
[ ] 87285    ** that the 6 comparison operators are consecutive integers in this
[ ] 87286    ** order:  NE, EQ, GT, LE, LT, GE */
[W] 87287    assert( OP_Eq==OP_Ne+1 ); assert( OP_Gt==OP_Ne+2 ); assert( OP_Le==OP_Ne+3 );
[W] 87288    assert( OP_Lt==OP_Ne+4 ); assert( OP_Ge==OP_Ne+5 );
[W] 87289    if( res<0 ){                        /* ne, eq, gt, le, lt, ge */
[W] 87290      static const unsigned char aLTb[] = { 1,  0,  0,  1,  1,  0 };
[W] 87291      res2 = aLTb[pOp->opcode - OP_Ne];
[W] 87292    }else if( res==0 ){
[W] 87293      static const unsigned char aEQb[] = { 0,  1,  0,  1,  0,  1 };
[W] 87294      res2 = aEQb[pOp->opcode - OP_Ne];
[W] 87295    }else{
[W] 87296      static const unsigned char aGTb[] = { 1,  0,  1,  0,  0,  1 };
[W] 87297      res2 = aGTb[pOp->opcode - OP_Ne];
[W] 87298    }
[ ] 87299
[ ] 87300    /* Undo any changes made by applyAffinity() to the input registers. */
[W] 87301    assert( (pIn3->flags & MEM_Dyn) == (flags3 & MEM_Dyn) );
[W] 87302    pIn3->flags = flags3;
[W] 87303    assert( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Dyn) == (flags1 & MEM_Dyn) );
[W] 87304    pIn1->flags = flags1;
[ ] 87305
[W] 87306    if( pOp->p5 & SQLITE_STOREP2 ){
[W] 87307      pOut = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[W] 87308      iCompare = res;
[W] 87309      if( (pOp->p5 & SQLITE_KEEPNULL)!=0 ){
[ ] 87310        /* The KEEPNULL flag prevents OP_Eq from overwriting a NULL with 1
[ ] 87311        ** and prevents OP_Ne from overwriting NULL with 0.  This flag
[ ] 87312        ** is only used in contexts where either:
[ ] 87313        **   (1) op==OP_Eq && (r[P2]==NULL || r[P2]==0)
[ ] 87314        **   (2) op==OP_Ne && (r[P2]==NULL || r[P2]==1)
[ ] 87315        ** Therefore it is not necessary to check the content of r[P2] for
[ ] 87316        ** NULL. */
[ ] 87317        assert( pOp->opcode==OP_Ne || pOp->opcode==OP_Eq );
[ ] 87318        assert( res2==0 || res2==1 );
[ ] 87319        testcase( res2==0 && pOp->opcode==OP_Eq );
[ ] 87320        testcase( res2==1 && pOp->opcode==OP_Eq );
[ ] 87321        testcase( res2==0 && pOp->opcode==OP_Ne );
[ ] 87322        testcase( res2==1 && pOp->opcode==OP_Ne );
[ ] 87323        if( (pOp->opcode==OP_Eq)==res2 ) break;
[ ] 87324      }
[W] 87325      memAboutToChange(p, pOut);
[W] 87326      MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Int);
[W] 87327      pOut->u.i = res2;
[W] 87328      REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p2, pOut);
[W] 87329    }else{
[ ] 87330      VdbeBranchTaken(res2!=0, (pOp->p5 & SQLITE_NULLEQ)?2:3);
[ ] 87331      if( res2 ){
[ ] 87332        goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87333      }
[ ] 87334    }
[W] 87335    break;
[W] 87336  }
[ ] 87337
[ ] 87338  /* Opcode: ElseNotEq * P2 * * *
[ ] 87339  **
[ ] 87340  ** This opcode must follow an OP_Lt or OP_Gt comparison operator.  There
[ ] 87341  ** can be zero or more OP_ReleaseReg opcodes intervening, but no other
[ ] 87342  ** opcodes are allowed to occur between this instruction and the previous
[ ] 87343  ** OP_Lt or OP_Gt.  Furthermore, the prior OP_Lt or OP_Gt must have the
[ ] 87344  ** SQLITE_STOREP2 bit set in the P5 field.
[ ] 87345  **
[ ] 87346  ** If result of an OP_Eq comparison on the same two operands as the
[ ] 87347  ** prior OP_Lt or OP_Gt would have been NULL or false (0), then then
[ ] 87348  ** jump to P2.  If the result of an OP_Eq comparison on the two previous
[ ] 87349  ** operands would have been true (1), then fall through.
[ ] 87350  */
[W] 87351  case OP_ElseNotEq: {       /* same as TK_ESCAPE, jump */
[ ] 87352
[ ] 87353  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 87354    /* Verify the preconditions of this opcode - that it follows an OP_Lt or
[ ] 87355    ** OP_Gt with the SQLITE_STOREP2 flag set, with zero or more intervening
[ ] 87356    ** OP_ReleaseReg opcodes */
[ ] 87357    int iAddr;
[ ] 87358    for(iAddr = (int)(pOp - aOp) - 1; ALWAYS(iAddr>=0); iAddr--){
[ ] 87359      if( aOp[iAddr].opcode==OP_ReleaseReg ) continue;
[ ] 87360      assert( aOp[iAddr].opcode==OP_Lt || aOp[iAddr].opcode==OP_Gt );
[ ] 87361      assert( aOp[iAddr].p5 & SQLITE_STOREP2 );
[ ] 87362      break;
[ ] 87363    }
[ ] 87364  #endif /* SQLITE_DEBUG */
[ ] 87365    VdbeBranchTaken(iCompare!=0, 2);
[ ] 87366    if( iCompare!=0 ) goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87367    break;
[ ] 87368  }
[ ] 87369
[ ] 87370
[ ] 87371  /* Opcode: Permutation * * * P4 *
[ ] 87372  **
[ ] 87373  ** Set the permutation used by the OP_Compare operator in the next
[ ] 87374  ** instruction.  The permutation is stored in the P4 operand.
[ ] 87375  **
[ ] 87376  ** The permutation is only valid until the next OP_Compare that has
[ ] 87377  ** the OPFLAG_PERMUTE bit set in P5. Typically the OP_Permutation should
[ ] 87378  ** occur immediately prior to the OP_Compare.
[ ] 87379  **
[ ] 87380  ** The first integer in the P4 integer array is the length of the array
[ ] 87381  ** and does not become part of the permutation.
[ ] 87382  */
[ ] 87383  case OP_Permutation: {
[ ] 87384    assert( pOp->p4type==P4_INTARRAY );
[ ] 87385    assert( pOp->p4.ai );
[ ] 87386    assert( pOp[1].opcode==OP_Compare );
[ ] 87387    assert( pOp[1].p5 & OPFLAG_PERMUTE );
[ ] 87388    break;
[ ] 87389  }
[ ] 87390
[ ] 87391  /* Opcode: Compare P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 87392  ** Synopsis: r[P1@P3] <-> r[P2@P3]
[ ] 87393  **
[ ] 87394  ** Compare two vectors of registers in reg(P1)..reg(P1+P3-1) (call this
[ ] 87395  ** vector "A") and in reg(P2)..reg(P2+P3-1) ("B").  Save the result of
[ ] 87396  ** the comparison for use by the next OP_Jump instruct.
[ ] 87397  **
[ ] 87398  ** If P5 has the OPFLAG_PERMUTE bit set, then the order of comparison is
[ ] 87399  ** determined by the most recent OP_Permutation operator.  If the
[ ] 87400  ** OPFLAG_PERMUTE bit is clear, then register are compared in sequential
[ ] 87401  ** order.
[ ] 87402  **
[ ] 87403  ** P4 is a KeyInfo structure that defines collating sequences and sort
[ ] 87404  ** orders for the comparison.  The permutation applies to registers
[ ] 87405  ** only.  The KeyInfo elements are used sequentially.
[ ] 87406  **
[ ] 87407  ** The comparison is a sort comparison, so NULLs compare equal,
[ ] 87408  ** NULLs are less than numbers, numbers are less than strings,
[ ] 87409  ** and strings are less than blobs.
[ ] 87410  */
[ ] 87411  case OP_Compare: {
[ ] 87412    int n;
[ ] 87413    int i;
[ ] 87414    int p1;
[ ] 87415    int p2;
[ ] 87416    const KeyInfo *pKeyInfo;
[ ] 87417    int idx;
[ ] 87418    CollSeq *pColl;    /* Collating sequence to use on this term */
[ ] 87419    int bRev;          /* True for DESCENDING sort order */
[ ] 87420    int *aPermute;     /* The permutation */
[ ] 87421
[ ] 87422    if( (pOp->p5 & OPFLAG_PERMUTE)==0 ){
[ ] 87423      aPermute = 0;
[ ] 87424    }else{
[ ] 87425      assert( pOp>aOp );
[ ] 87426      assert( pOp[-1].opcode==OP_Permutation );
[ ] 87427      assert( pOp[-1].p4type==P4_INTARRAY );
[ ] 87428      aPermute = pOp[-1].p4.ai + 1;
[ ] 87429      assert( aPermute!=0 );
[ ] 87430    }
[ ] 87431    n = pOp->p3;
[ ] 87432    pKeyInfo = pOp->p4.pKeyInfo;
[ ] 87433    assert( n>0 );
[ ] 87434    assert( pKeyInfo!=0 );
[ ] 87435    p1 = pOp->p1;
[ ] 87436    p2 = pOp->p2;
[ ] 87437  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 87438    if( aPermute ){
[ ] 87439      int k, mx = 0;
[ ] 87440      for(k=0; k<n; k++) if( aPermute[k]>mx ) mx = aPermute[k];
[ ] 87441      assert( p1>0 && p1+mx<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)+1 );
[ ] 87442      assert( p2>0 && p2+mx<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)+1 );
[ ] 87443    }else{
[ ] 87444      assert( p1>0 && p1+n<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)+1 );
[ ] 87445      assert( p2>0 && p2+n<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)+1 );
[ ] 87446    }
[ ] 87447  #endif /* SQLITE_DEBUG */
[ ] 87448    for(i=0; i<n; i++){
[ ] 87449      idx = aPermute ? aPermute[i] : i;
[ ] 87450      assert( memIsValid(&aMem[p1+idx]) );
[ ] 87451      assert( memIsValid(&aMem[p2+idx]) );
[ ] 87452      REGISTER_TRACE(p1+idx, &aMem[p1+idx]);
[ ] 87453      REGISTER_TRACE(p2+idx, &aMem[p2+idx]);
[ ] 87454      assert( i<pKeyInfo->nKeyField );
[ ] 87455      pColl = pKeyInfo->aColl[i];
[ ] 87456      bRev = (pKeyInfo->aSortFlags[i] & KEYINFO_ORDER_DESC);
[ ] 87457      iCompare = sqlite3MemCompare(&aMem[p1+idx], &aMem[p2+idx], pColl);
[ ] 87458      if( iCompare ){
[ ] 87459        if( (pKeyInfo->aSortFlags[i] & KEYINFO_ORDER_BIGNULL)
[ ] 87460         && ((aMem[p1+idx].flags & MEM_Null) || (aMem[p2+idx].flags & MEM_Null))
[ ] 87461        ){
[ ] 87462          iCompare = -iCompare;
[ ] 87463        }
[ ] 87464        if( bRev ) iCompare = -iCompare;
[ ] 87465        break;
[ ] 87466      }
[ ] 87467    }
[ ] 87468    break;
[ ] 87469  }
[ ] 87470
[ ] 87471  /* Opcode: Jump P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 87472  **
[ ] 87473  ** Jump to the instruction at address P1, P2, or P3 depending on whether
[ ] 87474  ** in the most recent OP_Compare instruction the P1 vector was less than
[ ] 87475  ** equal to, or greater than the P2 vector, respectively.
[ ] 87476  */
[ ] 87477  case OP_Jump: {             /* jump */
[ ] 87478    if( iCompare<0 ){
[ ] 87479      VdbeBranchTaken(0,4); pOp = &aOp[pOp->p1 - 1];
[ ] 87480    }else if( iCompare==0 ){
[ ] 87481      VdbeBranchTaken(1,4); pOp = &aOp[pOp->p2 - 1];
[ ] 87482    }else{
[ ] 87483      VdbeBranchTaken(2,4); pOp = &aOp[pOp->p3 - 1];
[ ] 87484    }
[ ] 87485    break;
[ ] 87486  }
[ ] 87487
[ ] 87488  /* Opcode: And P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 87489  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=(r[P1] && r[P2])
[ ] 87490  **
[ ] 87491  ** Take the logical AND of the values in registers P1 and P2 and
[ ] 87492  ** write the result into register P3.
[ ] 87493  **
[ ] 87494  ** If either P1 or P2 is 0 (false) then the result is 0 even if
[ ] 87495  ** the other input is NULL.  A NULL and true or two NULLs give
[ ] 87496  ** a NULL output.
[ ] 87497  */
[ ] 87498  /* Opcode: Or P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 87499  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=(r[P1] || r[P2])
[ ] 87500  **
[ ] 87501  ** Take the logical OR of the values in register P1 and P2 and
[ ] 87502  ** store the answer in register P3.
[ ] 87503  **
[ ] 87504  ** If either P1 or P2 is nonzero (true) then the result is 1 (true)
[ ] 87505  ** even if the other input is NULL.  A NULL and false or two NULLs
[ ] 87506  ** give a NULL output.
[ ] 87507  */
[ ] 87508  case OP_And:              /* same as TK_AND, in1, in2, out3 */
[ ] 87509  case OP_Or: {             /* same as TK_OR, in1, in2, out3 */
[ ] 87510    int v1;    /* Left operand:  0==FALSE, 1==TRUE, 2==UNKNOWN or NULL */
[ ] 87511    int v2;    /* Right operand: 0==FALSE, 1==TRUE, 2==UNKNOWN or NULL */
[ ] 87512
[ ] 87513    v1 = sqlite3VdbeBooleanValue(&aMem[pOp->p1], 2);
[ ] 87514    v2 = sqlite3VdbeBooleanValue(&aMem[pOp->p2], 2);
[ ] 87515    if( pOp->opcode==OP_And ){
[ ] 87516      static const unsigned char and_logic[] = { 0, 0, 0, 0, 1, 2, 0, 2, 2 };
[ ] 87517      v1 = and_logic[v1*3+v2];
[ ] 87518    }else{
[ ] 87519      static const unsigned char or_logic[] = { 0, 1, 2, 1, 1, 1, 2, 1, 2 };
[ ] 87520      v1 = or_logic[v1*3+v2];
[ ] 87521    }
[ ] 87522    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 87523    if( v1==2 ){
[ ] 87524      MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Null);
[ ] 87525    }else{
[ ] 87526      pOut->u.i = v1;
[ ] 87527      MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Int);
[ ] 87528    }
[ ] 87529    break;
[ ] 87530  }
[ ] 87531
[ ] 87532  /* Opcode: IsTrue P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 87533  ** Synopsis: r[P2] = coalesce(r[P1]==TRUE,P3) ^ P4
[ ] 87534  **
[ ] 87535  ** This opcode implements the IS TRUE, IS FALSE, IS NOT TRUE, and
[ ] 87536  ** IS NOT FALSE operators.
[ ] 87537  **
[ ] 87538  ** Interpret the value in register P1 as a boolean value.  Store that
[ ] 87539  ** boolean (a 0 or 1) in register P2.  Or if the value in register P1 is
[ ] 87540  ** NULL, then the P3 is stored in register P2.  Invert the answer if P4
[ ] 87541  ** is 1.
[ ] 87542  **
[ ] 87543  ** The logic is summarized like this:
[ ] 87544  **
[ ] 87545  ** <ul>
[ ] 87546  ** <li> If P3==0 and P4==0  then  r[P2] := r[P1] IS TRUE
[ ] 87547  ** <li> If P3==1 and P4==1  then  r[P2] := r[P1] IS FALSE
[ ] 87548  ** <li> If P3==0 and P4==1  then  r[P2] := r[P1] IS NOT TRUE
[ ] 87549  ** <li> If P3==1 and P4==0  then  r[P2] := r[P1] IS NOT FALSE
[ ] 87550  ** </ul>
[ ] 87551  */
[ ] 87552  case OP_IsTrue: {               /* in1, out2 */
[ ] 87553    assert( pOp->p4type==P4_INT32 );
[ ] 87554    assert( pOp->p4.i==0 || pOp->p4.i==1 );
[ ] 87555    assert( pOp->p3==0 || pOp->p3==1 );
[ ] 87556    sqlite3VdbeMemSetInt64(&aMem[pOp->p2],
[ ] 87557        sqlite3VdbeBooleanValue(&aMem[pOp->p1], pOp->p3) ^ pOp->p4.i);
[ ] 87558    break;
[ ] 87559  }
[ ] 87560
[ ] 87561  /* Opcode: Not P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 87562  ** Synopsis: r[P2]= !r[P1]
[ ] 87563  **
[ ] 87564  ** Interpret the value in register P1 as a boolean value.  Store the
[ ] 87565  ** boolean complement in register P2.  If the value in register P1 is
[ ] 87566  ** NULL, then a NULL is stored in P2.
[ ] 87567  */
[ ] 87568  case OP_Not: {                /* same as TK_NOT, in1, out2 */
[ ] 87569    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87570    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 87571    if( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Null)==0 ){
[ ] 87572      sqlite3VdbeMemSetInt64(pOut, !sqlite3VdbeBooleanValue(pIn1,0));
[ ] 87573    }else{
[ ] 87574      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pOut);
[ ] 87575    }
[ ] 87576    break;
[ ] 87577  }
[ ] 87578
[ ] 87579  /* Opcode: BitNot P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 87580  ** Synopsis: r[P2]= ~r[P1]
[ ] 87581  **
[ ] 87582  ** Interpret the content of register P1 as an integer.  Store the
[ ] 87583  ** ones-complement of the P1 value into register P2.  If P1 holds
[ ] 87584  ** a NULL then store a NULL in P2.
[ ] 87585  */
[ ] 87586  case OP_BitNot: {             /* same as TK_BITNOT, in1, out2 */
[ ] 87587    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87588    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 87589    sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pOut);
[ ] 87590    if( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Null)==0 ){
[ ] 87591      pOut->flags = MEM_Int;
[ ] 87592      pOut->u.i = ~sqlite3VdbeIntValue(pIn1);
[ ] 87593    }
[ ] 87594    break;
[ ] 87595  }
[ ] 87596
[ ] 87597  /* Opcode: Once P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 87598  **
[ ] 87599  ** Fall through to the next instruction the first time this opcode is
[ ] 87600  ** encountered on each invocation of the byte-code program.  Jump to P2
[ ] 87601  ** on the second and all subsequent encounters during the same invocation.
[ ] 87602  **
[ ] 87603  ** Top-level programs determine first invocation by comparing the P1
[ ] 87604  ** operand against the P1 operand on the OP_Init opcode at the beginning
[ ] 87605  ** of the program.  If the P1 values differ, then fall through and make
[ ] 87606  ** the P1 of this opcode equal to the P1 of OP_Init.  If P1 values are
[ ] 87607  ** the same then take the jump.
[ ] 87608  **
[ ] 87609  ** For subprograms, there is a bitmask in the VdbeFrame that determines
[ ] 87610  ** whether or not the jump should be taken.  The bitmask is necessary
[ ] 87611  ** because the self-altering code trick does not work for recursive
[ ] 87612  ** triggers.
[ ] 87613  */
[ ] 87614  case OP_Once: {             /* jump */
[ ] 87615    u32 iAddr;                /* Address of this instruction */
[ ] 87616    assert( p->aOp[0].opcode==OP_Init );
[ ] 87617    if( p->pFrame ){
[ ] 87618      iAddr = (int)(pOp - p->aOp);
[ ] 87619      if( (p->pFrame->aOnce[iAddr/8] & (1<<(iAddr & 7)))!=0 ){
[ ] 87620        VdbeBranchTaken(1, 2);
[ ] 87621        goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87622      }
[ ] 87623      p->pFrame->aOnce[iAddr/8] |= 1<<(iAddr & 7);
[ ] 87624    }else{
[ ] 87625      if( p->aOp[0].p1==pOp->p1 ){
[ ] 87626        VdbeBranchTaken(1, 2);
[ ] 87627        goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87628      }
[ ] 87629    }
[ ] 87630    VdbeBranchTaken(0, 2);
[ ] 87631    pOp->p1 = p->aOp[0].p1;
[ ] 87632    break;
[ ] 87633  }
[ ] 87634
[ ] 87635  /* Opcode: If P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 87636  **
[ ] 87637  ** Jump to P2 if the value in register P1 is true.  The value
[ ] 87638  ** is considered true if it is numeric and non-zero.  If the value
[ ] 87639  ** in P1 is NULL then take the jump if and only if P3 is non-zero.
[ ] 87640  */
[ ] 87641  case OP_If:  {               /* jump, in1 */
[ ] 87642    int c;
[ ] 87643    c = sqlite3VdbeBooleanValue(&aMem[pOp->p1], pOp->p3);
[ ] 87644    VdbeBranchTaken(c!=0, 2);
[ ] 87645    if( c ) goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87646    break;
[ ] 87647  }
[ ] 87648
[ ] 87649  /* Opcode: IfNot P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 87650  **
[ ] 87651  ** Jump to P2 if the value in register P1 is False.  The value
[ ] 87652  ** is considered false if it has a numeric value of zero.  If the value
[ ] 87653  ** in P1 is NULL then take the jump if and only if P3 is non-zero.
[ ] 87654  */
[ ] 87655  case OP_IfNot: {            /* jump, in1 */
[ ] 87656    int c;
[ ] 87657    c = !sqlite3VdbeBooleanValue(&aMem[pOp->p1], !pOp->p3);
[ ] 87658    VdbeBranchTaken(c!=0, 2);
[ ] 87659    if( c ) goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87660    break;
[ ] 87661  }
[ ] 87662
[ ] 87663  /* Opcode: IsNull P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 87664  ** Synopsis: if r[P1]==NULL goto P2
[ ] 87665  **
[ ] 87666  ** Jump to P2 if the value in register P1 is NULL.
[ ] 87667  */
[ ] 87668  case OP_IsNull: {            /* same as TK_ISNULL, jump, in1 */
[ ] 87669    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87670    VdbeBranchTaken( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Null)!=0, 2);
[ ] 87671    if( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Null)!=0 ){
[ ] 87672      goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87673    }
[ ] 87674    break;
[ ] 87675  }
[ ] 87676
[ ] 87677  /* Opcode: NotNull P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 87678  ** Synopsis: if r[P1]!=NULL goto P2
[ ] 87679  **
[ ] 87680  ** Jump to P2 if the value in register P1 is not NULL.
[ ] 87681  */
[ ] 87682  case OP_NotNull: {            /* same as TK_NOTNULL, jump, in1 */
[ ] 87683    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87684    VdbeBranchTaken( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Null)==0, 2);
[ ] 87685    if( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Null)==0 ){
[ ] 87686      goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87687    }
[ ] 87688    break;
[ ] 87689  }
[ ] 87690
[ ] 87691  /* Opcode: IfNullRow P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 87692  ** Synopsis: if P1.nullRow then r[P3]=NULL, goto P2
[ ] 87693  **
[ ] 87694  ** Check the cursor P1 to see if it is currently pointing at a NULL row.
[ ] 87695  ** If it is, then set register P3 to NULL and jump immediately to P2.
[ ] 87696  ** If P1 is not on a NULL row, then fall through without making any
[ ] 87697  ** changes.
[ ] 87698  */
[ ] 87699  case OP_IfNullRow: {         /* jump */
[ ] 87700    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<p->nCursor );
[ ] 87701    assert( p->apCsr[pOp->p1]!=0 );
[ ] 87702    if( p->apCsr[pOp->p1]->nullRow ){
[ ] 87703      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(aMem + pOp->p3);
[ ] 87704      goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 87705    }
[ ] 87706    break;
[ ] 87707  }
[ ] 87708
[ ] 87709  #ifdef SQLITE_ENABLE_OFFSET_SQL_FUNC
[ ] 87710  /* Opcode: Offset P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 87711  ** Synopsis: r[P3] = sqlite_offset(P1)
[ ] 87712  **
[ ] 87713  ** Store in register r[P3] the byte offset into the database file that is the
[ ] 87714  ** start of the payload for the record at which that cursor P1 is currently
[ ] 87715  ** pointing.
[ ] 87716  **
[ ] 87717  ** P2 is the column number for the argument to the sqlite_offset() function.
[ ] 87718  ** This opcode does not use P2 itself, but the P2 value is used by the
[ ] 87719  ** code generator.  The P1, P2, and P3 operands to this opcode are the
[ ] 87720  ** same as for OP_Column.
[ ] 87721  **
[ ] 87722  ** This opcode is only available if SQLite is compiled with the
[ ] 87723  ** -DSQLITE_ENABLE_OFFSET_SQL_FUNC option.
[ ] 87724  */
[ ] 87725  case OP_Offset: {          /* out3 */
[ ] 87726    VdbeCursor *pC;    /* The VDBE cursor */
[ ] 87727    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<p->nCursor );
[ ] 87728    pC = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87729    pOut = &p->aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 87730    if( NEVER(pC==0) || pC->eCurType!=CURTYPE_BTREE ){
[ ] 87731      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pOut);
[ ] 87732    }else{
[ ] 87733      sqlite3VdbeMemSetInt64(pOut, sqlite3BtreeOffset(pC->uc.pCursor));
[ ] 87734    }
[ ] 87735    break;
[ ] 87736  }
[ ] 87737  #endif /* SQLITE_ENABLE_OFFSET_SQL_FUNC */
[ ] 87738
[ ] 87739  /* Opcode: Column P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 87740  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=PX
[ ] 87741  **
[ ] 87742  ** Interpret the data that cursor P1 points to as a structure built using
[ ] 87743  ** the MakeRecord instruction.  (See the MakeRecord opcode for additional
[ ] 87744  ** information about the format of the data.)  Extract the P2-th column
[ ] 87745  ** from this record.  If there are less that (P2+1)
[ ] 87746  ** values in the record, extract a NULL.
[ ] 87747  **
[ ] 87748  ** The value extracted is stored in register P3.
[ ] 87749  **
[ ] 87750  ** If the record contains fewer than P2 fields, then extract a NULL.  Or,
[ ] 87751  ** if the P4 argument is a P4_MEM use the value of the P4 argument as
[ ] 87752  ** the result.
[ ] 87753  **
[ ] 87754  ** If the OPFLAG_LENGTHARG and OPFLAG_TYPEOFARG bits are set on P5 then
[ ] 87755  ** the result is guaranteed to only be used as the argument of a length()
[ ] 87756  ** or typeof() function, respectively.  The loading of large blobs can be
[ ] 87757  ** skipped for length() and all content loading can be skipped for typeof().
[ ] 87758  */
[ ] 87759  case OP_Column: {
[ ] 87760    int p2;            /* column number to retrieve */
[ ] 87761    VdbeCursor *pC;    /* The VDBE cursor */
[ ] 87762    BtCursor *pCrsr;   /* The BTree cursor */
[ ] 87763    u32 *aOffset;      /* aOffset[i] is offset to start of data for i-th column */
[ ] 87764    int len;           /* The length of the serialized data for the column */
[ ] 87765    int i;             /* Loop counter */
[ ] 87766    Mem *pDest;        /* Where to write the extracted value */
[ ] 87767    Mem sMem;          /* For storing the record being decoded */
[ ] 87768    const u8 *zData;   /* Part of the record being decoded */
[ ] 87769    const u8 *zHdr;    /* Next unparsed byte of the header */
[ ] 87770    const u8 *zEndHdr; /* Pointer to first byte after the header */
[ ] 87771    u64 offset64;      /* 64-bit offset */
[ ] 87772    u32 t;             /* A type code from the record header */
[ ] 87773    Mem *pReg;         /* PseudoTable input register */
[ ] 87774
[ ] 87775    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<p->nCursor );
[ ] 87776    pC = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 87777    assert( pC!=0 );
[ ] 87778    p2 = pOp->p2;
[ ] 87779
[ ] 87780    /* If the cursor cache is stale (meaning it is not currently point at
