[ ] 87781    ** the correct row) then bring it up-to-date by doing the necessary
[ ] 87782    ** B-Tree seek. */
[ ] 87783    rc = sqlite3VdbeCursorMoveto(&pC, &p2);
[ ] 87784    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 87785
[ ] 87786    assert( pOp->p3>0 && pOp->p3<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 87787    pDest = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 87788    memAboutToChange(p, pDest);
[ ] 87789    assert( pC!=0 );
[ ] 87790    assert( p2<pC->nField );
[ ] 87791    aOffset = pC->aOffset;
[ ] 87792    assert( pC->eCurType!=CURTYPE_VTAB );
[ ] 87793    assert( pC->eCurType!=CURTYPE_PSEUDO || pC->nullRow );
[ ] 87794    assert( pC->eCurType!=CURTYPE_SORTER );
[ ] 87795
[ ] 87796    if( pC->cacheStatus!=p->cacheCtr ){                /*OPTIMIZATION-IF-FALSE*/
[ ] 87797      if( pC->nullRow ){
[ ] 87798        if( pC->eCurType==CURTYPE_PSEUDO ){
[ ] 87799          /* For the special case of as pseudo-cursor, the seekResult field
[ ] 87800          ** identifies the register that holds the record */
[ ] 87801          assert( pC->seekResult>0 );
[ ] 87802          pReg = &aMem[pC->seekResult];
[ ] 87803          assert( pReg->flags & MEM_Blob );
[ ] 87804          assert( memIsValid(pReg) );
[ ] 87805          pC->payloadSize = pC->szRow = pReg->n;
[ ] 87806          pC->aRow = (u8*)pReg->z;
[ ] 87807        }else{
[ ] 87808          sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pDest);
[ ] 87809          goto op_column_out;
[ ] 87810        }
[ ] 87811      }else{
[ ] 87812        pCrsr = pC->uc.pCursor;
[ ] 87813        assert( pC->eCurType==CURTYPE_BTREE );
[ ] 87814        assert( pCrsr );
[ ] 87815        assert( sqlite3BtreeCursorIsValid(pCrsr) );
[ ] 87816        pC->payloadSize = sqlite3BtreePayloadSize(pCrsr);
[ ] 87817        pC->aRow = sqlite3BtreePayloadFetch(pCrsr, &pC->szRow);
[ ] 87818        assert( pC->szRow<=pC->payloadSize );
[ ] 87819        assert( pC->szRow<=65536 );  /* Maximum page size is 64KiB */
[ ] 87820        if( pC->payloadSize > (u32)db->aLimit[SQLITE_LIMIT_LENGTH] ){
[ ] 87821          goto too_big;
[ ] 87822        }
[ ] 87823      }
[ ] 87824      pC->cacheStatus = p->cacheCtr;
[ ] 87825      pC->iHdrOffset = getVarint32(pC->aRow, aOffset[0]);
[ ] 87826      pC->nHdrParsed = 0;
[ ] 87827
[ ] 87828
[ ] 87829      if( pC->szRow<aOffset[0] ){      /*OPTIMIZATION-IF-FALSE*/
[ ] 87830        /* pC->aRow does not have to hold the entire row, but it does at least
[ ] 87831        ** need to cover the header of the record.  If pC->aRow does not contain
[ ] 87832        ** the complete header, then set it to zero, forcing the header to be
[ ] 87833        ** dynamically allocated. */
[ ] 87834        pC->aRow = 0;
[ ] 87835        pC->szRow = 0;
[ ] 87836
[ ] 87837        /* Make sure a corrupt database has not given us an oversize header.
[ ] 87838        ** Do this now to avoid an oversize memory allocation.
[ ] 87839        **
[ ] 87840        ** Type entries can be between 1 and 5 bytes each.  But 4 and 5 byte
[ ] 87841        ** types use so much data space that there can only be 4096 and 32 of
[ ] 87842        ** them, respectively.  So the maximum header length results from a
[ ] 87843        ** 3-byte type for each of the maximum of 32768 columns plus three
[ ] 87844        ** extra bytes for the header length itself.  32768*3 + 3 = 98307.
[ ] 87845        */
[ ] 87846        if( aOffset[0] > 98307 || aOffset[0] > pC->payloadSize ){
[ ] 87847          goto op_column_corrupt;
[ ] 87848        }
[ ] 87849      }else{
[ ] 87850        /* This is an optimization.  By skipping over the first few tests
[ ] 87851        ** (ex: pC->nHdrParsed<=p2) in the next section, we achieve a
[ ] 87852        ** measurable performance gain.
[ ] 87853        **
[ ] 87854        ** This branch is taken even if aOffset[0]==0.  Such a record is never
[ ] 87855        ** generated by SQLite, and could be considered corruption, but we
[ ] 87856        ** accept it for historical reasons.  When aOffset[0]==0, the code this
[ ] 87857        ** branch jumps to reads past the end of the record, but never more
[ ] 87858        ** than a few bytes.  Even if the record occurs at the end of the page
[ ] 87859        ** content area, the "page header" comes after the page content and so
[ ] 87860        ** this overread is harmless.  Similar overreads can occur for a corrupt
[ ] 87861        ** database file.
[ ] 87862        */
[ ] 87863        zData = pC->aRow;
[ ] 87864        assert( pC->nHdrParsed<=p2 );         /* Conditional skipped */
[ ] 87865        testcase( aOffset[0]==0 );
[ ] 87866        goto op_column_read_header;
[ ] 87867      }
[ ] 87868    }
[ ] 87869
[ ] 87870    /* Make sure at least the first p2+1 entries of the header have been
[ ] 87871    ** parsed and valid information is in aOffset[] and pC->aType[].
[ ] 87872    */
[ ] 87873    if( pC->nHdrParsed<=p2 ){
[ ] 87874      /* If there is more header available for parsing in the record, try
[ ] 87875      ** to extract additional fields up through the p2+1-th field
[ ] 87876      */
[ ] 87877      if( pC->iHdrOffset<aOffset[0] ){
[ ] 87878        /* Make sure zData points to enough of the record to cover the header. */
[ ] 87879        if( pC->aRow==0 ){
[ ] 87880          memset(&sMem, 0, sizeof(sMem));
[ ] 87881          rc = sqlite3VdbeMemFromBtreeZeroOffset(pC->uc.pCursor,aOffset[0],&sMem);
[ ] 87882          if( rc!=SQLITE_OK ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 87883          zData = (u8*)sMem.z;
[ ] 87884        }else{
[ ] 87885          zData = pC->aRow;
[ ] 87886        }
[ ] 87887
[ ] 87888        /* Fill in pC->aType[i] and aOffset[i] values through the p2-th field. */
[ ] 87889      op_column_read_header:
[ ] 87890        i = pC->nHdrParsed;
[ ] 87891        offset64 = aOffset[i];
[ ] 87892        zHdr = zData + pC->iHdrOffset;
[ ] 87893        zEndHdr = zData + aOffset[0];
[ ] 87894        testcase( zHdr>=zEndHdr );
[ ] 87895        do{
[ ] 87896          if( (pC->aType[i] = t = zHdr[0])<0x80 ){
[ ] 87897            zHdr++;
[ ] 87898            offset64 += sqlite3VdbeOneByteSerialTypeLen(t);
[ ] 87899          }else{
[ ] 87900            zHdr += sqlite3GetVarint32(zHdr, &t);
[ ] 87901            pC->aType[i] = t;
[ ] 87902            offset64 += sqlite3VdbeSerialTypeLen(t);
[ ] 87903          }
[ ] 87904          aOffset[++i] = (u32)(offset64 & 0xffffffff);
[ ] 87905        }while( i<=p2 && zHdr<zEndHdr );
[ ] 87906
[ ] 87907        /* The record is corrupt if any of the following are true:
[ ] 87908        ** (1) the bytes of the header extend past the declared header size
[ ] 87909        ** (2) the entire header was used but not all data was used
[ ] 87910        ** (3) the end of the data extends beyond the end of the record.
[ ] 87911        */
[ ] 87912        if( (zHdr>=zEndHdr && (zHdr>zEndHdr || offset64!=pC->payloadSize))
[ ] 87913         || (offset64 > pC->payloadSize)
[ ] 87914        ){
[ ] 87915          if( aOffset[0]==0 ){
[ ] 87916            i = 0;
[ ] 87917            zHdr = zEndHdr;
[ ] 87918          }else{
[ ] 87919            if( pC->aRow==0 ) sqlite3VdbeMemRelease(&sMem);
[ ] 87920            goto op_column_corrupt;
[ ] 87921          }
[ ] 87922        }
[ ] 87923
[ ] 87924        pC->nHdrParsed = i;
[ ] 87925        pC->iHdrOffset = (u32)(zHdr - zData);
[ ] 87926        if( pC->aRow==0 ) sqlite3VdbeMemRelease(&sMem);
[ ] 87927      }else{
[ ] 87928        t = 0;
[ ] 87929      }
[ ] 87930
[ ] 87931      /* If after trying to extract new entries from the header, nHdrParsed is
[ ] 87932      ** still not up to p2, that means that the record has fewer than p2
[ ] 87933      ** columns.  So the result will be either the default value or a NULL.
[ ] 87934      */
[ ] 87935      if( pC->nHdrParsed<=p2 ){
[ ] 87936        if( pOp->p4type==P4_MEM ){
[ ] 87937          sqlite3VdbeMemShallowCopy(pDest, pOp->p4.pMem, MEM_Static);
[ ] 87938        }else{
[ ] 87939          sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pDest);
[ ] 87940        }
[ ] 87941        goto op_column_out;
[ ] 87942      }
[ ] 87943    }else{
[ ] 87944      t = pC->aType[p2];
[ ] 87945    }
[ ] 87946
[ ] 87947    /* Extract the content for the p2+1-th column.  Control can only
[ ] 87948    ** reach this point if aOffset[p2], aOffset[p2+1], and pC->aType[p2] are
[ ] 87949    ** all valid.
[ ] 87950    */
[ ] 87951    assert( p2<pC->nHdrParsed );
[ ] 87952    assert( rc==SQLITE_OK );
[ ] 87953    assert( sqlite3VdbeCheckMemInvariants(pDest) );
[ ] 87954    if( VdbeMemDynamic(pDest) ){
[ ] 87955      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pDest);
[ ] 87956    }
[ ] 87957    assert( t==pC->aType[p2] );
[ ] 87958    if( pC->szRow>=aOffset[p2+1] ){
[ ] 87959      /* This is the common case where the desired content fits on the original
[ ] 87960      ** page - where the content is not on an overflow page */
[ ] 87961      zData = pC->aRow + aOffset[p2];
[ ] 87962      if( t<12 ){
[ ] 87963        sqlite3VdbeSerialGet(zData, t, pDest);
[ ] 87964      }else{
[ ] 87965        /* If the column value is a string, we need a persistent value, not
[ ] 87966        ** a MEM_Ephem value.  This branch is a fast short-cut that is equivalent
[ ] 87967        ** to calling sqlite3VdbeSerialGet() and sqlite3VdbeDeephemeralize().
[ ] 87968        */
[ ] 87969        static const u16 aFlag[] = { MEM_Blob, MEM_Str|MEM_Term };
[ ] 87970        pDest->n = len = (t-12)/2;
[ ] 87971        pDest->enc = encoding;
[ ] 87972        if( pDest->szMalloc < len+2 ){
[ ] 87973          pDest->flags = MEM_Null;
[ ] 87974          if( sqlite3VdbeMemGrow(pDest, len+2, 0) ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 87975        }else{
[ ] 87976          pDest->z = pDest->zMalloc;
[ ] 87977        }
[ ] 87978        memcpy(pDest->z, zData, len);
[ ] 87979        pDest->z[len] = 0;
[ ] 87980        pDest->z[len+1] = 0;
[ ] 87981        pDest->flags = aFlag[t&1];
[ ] 87982      }
[ ] 87983    }else{
[ ] 87984      pDest->enc = encoding;
[ ] 87985      /* This branch happens only when content is on overflow pages */
[ ] 87986      if( ((pOp->p5 & (OPFLAG_LENGTHARG|OPFLAG_TYPEOFARG))!=0
[ ] 87987            && ((t>=12 && (t&1)==0) || (pOp->p5 & OPFLAG_TYPEOFARG)!=0))
[ ] 87988       || (len = sqlite3VdbeSerialTypeLen(t))==0
[ ] 87989      ){
[ ] 87990        /* Content is irrelevant for
[ ] 87991        **    1. the typeof() function,
[ ] 87992        **    2. the length(X) function if X is a blob, and
[ ] 87993        **    3. if the content length is zero.
[ ] 87994        ** So we might as well use bogus content rather than reading
[ ] 87995        ** content from disk.
[ ] 87996        **
[ ] 87997        ** Although sqlite3VdbeSerialGet() may read at most 8 bytes from the
[ ] 87998        ** buffer passed to it, debugging function VdbeMemPrettyPrint() may
[ ] 87999        ** read more.  Use the global constant sqlite3CtypeMap[] as the array,
[ ] 88000        ** as that array is 256 bytes long (plenty for VdbeMemPrettyPrint())
[ ] 88001        ** and it begins with a bunch of zeros.
[ ] 88002        */
[ ] 88003        sqlite3VdbeSerialGet((u8*)sqlite3CtypeMap, t, pDest);
[ ] 88004      }else{
[ ] 88005        rc = sqlite3VdbeMemFromBtree(pC->uc.pCursor, aOffset[p2], len, pDest);
[ ] 88006        if( rc!=SQLITE_OK ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88007        sqlite3VdbeSerialGet((const u8*)pDest->z, t, pDest);
[ ] 88008        pDest->flags &= ~MEM_Ephem;
[ ] 88009      }
[ ] 88010    }
[ ] 88011
[ ] 88012  op_column_out:
[ ] 88013    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pDest);
[ ] 88014    REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p3, pDest);
[ ] 88015    break;
[ ] 88016
[ ] 88017  op_column_corrupt:
[ ] 88018    if( aOp[0].p3>0 ){
[ ] 88019      pOp = &aOp[aOp[0].p3-1];
[ ] 88020      break;
[ ] 88021    }else{
[ ] 88022      rc = SQLITE_CORRUPT_BKPT;
[ ] 88023      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88024    }
[ ] 88025  }
[ ] 88026
[ ] 88027  /* Opcode: Affinity P1 P2 * P4 *
[ ] 88028  ** Synopsis: affinity(r[P1@P2])
[ ] 88029  **
[ ] 88030  ** Apply affinities to a range of P2 registers starting with P1.
[ ] 88031  **
[ ] 88032  ** P4 is a string that is P2 characters long. The N-th character of the
[ ] 88033  ** string indicates the column affinity that should be used for the N-th
[ ] 88034  ** memory cell in the range.
[ ] 88035  */
[ ] 88036  case OP_Affinity: {
[ ] 88037    const char *zAffinity;   /* The affinity to be applied */
[ ] 88038
[ ] 88039    zAffinity = pOp->p4.z;
[ ] 88040    assert( zAffinity!=0 );
[ ] 88041    assert( pOp->p2>0 );
[ ] 88042    assert( zAffinity[pOp->p2]==0 );
[ ] 88043    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 88044    while( 1 /*exit-by-break*/ ){
[ ] 88045      assert( pIn1 <= &p->aMem[(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)] );
[ ] 88046      assert( zAffinity[0]==SQLITE_AFF_NONE || memIsValid(pIn1) );
[ ] 88047      applyAffinity(pIn1, zAffinity[0], encoding);
[ ] 88048      if( zAffinity[0]==SQLITE_AFF_REAL && (pIn1->flags & MEM_Int)!=0 ){
[ ] 88049        /* When applying REAL affinity, if the result is still an MEM_Int
[ ] 88050        ** that will fit in 6 bytes, then change the type to MEM_IntReal
[ ] 88051        ** so that we keep the high-resolution integer value but know that
[ ] 88052        ** the type really wants to be REAL. */
[ ] 88053        testcase( pIn1->u.i==140737488355328LL );
[ ] 88054        testcase( pIn1->u.i==140737488355327LL );
[ ] 88055        testcase( pIn1->u.i==-140737488355328LL );
[ ] 88056        testcase( pIn1->u.i==-140737488355329LL );
[ ] 88057        if( pIn1->u.i<=140737488355327LL && pIn1->u.i>=-140737488355328LL ){
[ ] 88058          pIn1->flags |= MEM_IntReal;
[ ] 88059          pIn1->flags &= ~MEM_Int;
[ ] 88060        }else{
[ ] 88061          pIn1->u.r = (double)pIn1->u.i;
[ ] 88062          pIn1->flags |= MEM_Real;
[ ] 88063          pIn1->flags &= ~MEM_Int;
[ ] 88064        }
[ ] 88065      }
[ ] 88066      REGISTER_TRACE((int)(pIn1-aMem), pIn1);
[ ] 88067      zAffinity++;
[ ] 88068      if( zAffinity[0]==0 ) break;
[ ] 88069      pIn1++;
[ ] 88070    }
[ ] 88071    break;
[ ] 88072  }
[ ] 88073
[ ] 88074  /* Opcode: MakeRecord P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 88075  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=mkrec(r[P1@P2])
[ ] 88076  **
[ ] 88077  ** Convert P2 registers beginning with P1 into the [record format]
[ ] 88078  ** use as a data record in a database table or as a key
[ ] 88079  ** in an index.  The OP_Column opcode can decode the record later.
[ ] 88080  **
[ ] 88081  ** P4 may be a string that is P2 characters long.  The N-th character of the
[ ] 88082  ** string indicates the column affinity that should be used for the N-th
[ ] 88083  ** field of the index key.
[ ] 88084  **
[ ] 88085  ** The mapping from character to affinity is given by the SQLITE_AFF_
[ ] 88086  ** macros defined in sqliteInt.h.
[ ] 88087  **
[ ] 88088  ** If P4 is NULL then all index fields have the affinity BLOB.
[ ] 88089  */
[ ] 88090  case OP_MakeRecord: {
[ ] 88091    Mem *pRec;             /* The new record */
[ ] 88092    u64 nData;             /* Number of bytes of data space */
[ ] 88093    int nHdr;              /* Number of bytes of header space */
[ ] 88094    i64 nByte;             /* Data space required for this record */
[ ] 88095    i64 nZero;             /* Number of zero bytes at the end of the record */
[ ] 88096    int nVarint;           /* Number of bytes in a varint */
[ ] 88097    u32 serial_type;       /* Type field */
[ ] 88098    Mem *pData0;           /* First field to be combined into the record */
[ ] 88099    Mem *pLast;            /* Last field of the record */
[ ] 88100    int nField;            /* Number of fields in the record */
[ ] 88101    char *zAffinity;       /* The affinity string for the record */
[ ] 88102    int file_format;       /* File format to use for encoding */
[ ] 88103    u32 len;               /* Length of a field */
[ ] 88104    u8 *zHdr;              /* Where to write next byte of the header */
[ ] 88105    u8 *zPayload;          /* Where to write next byte of the payload */
[ ] 88106
[ ] 88107    /* Assuming the record contains N fields, the record format looks
[ ] 88108    ** like this:
[ ] 88109    **
[ ] 88110    ** ------------------------------------------------------------------------
[ ] 88111    ** | hdr-size | type 0 | type 1 | ... | type N-1 | data0 | ... | data N-1 |
[ ] 88112    ** ------------------------------------------------------------------------
[ ] 88113    **
[ ] 88114    ** Data(0) is taken from register P1.  Data(1) comes from register P1+1
[ ] 88115    ** and so forth.
[ ] 88116    **
[ ] 88117    ** Each type field is a varint representing the serial type of the
[ ] 88118    ** corresponding data element (see sqlite3VdbeSerialType()). The
[ ] 88119    ** hdr-size field is also a varint which is the offset from the beginning
[ ] 88120    ** of the record to data0.
[ ] 88121    */
[ ] 88122    nData = 0;         /* Number of bytes of data space */
[ ] 88123    nHdr = 0;          /* Number of bytes of header space */
[ ] 88124    nZero = 0;         /* Number of zero bytes at the end of the record */
[ ] 88125    nField = pOp->p1;
[ ] 88126    zAffinity = pOp->p4.z;
[ ] 88127    assert( nField>0 && pOp->p2>0 && pOp->p2+nField<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)+1 );
[ ] 88128    pData0 = &aMem[nField];
[ ] 88129    nField = pOp->p2;
[ ] 88130    pLast = &pData0[nField-1];
[ ] 88131    file_format = p->minWriteFileFormat;
[ ] 88132
[ ] 88133    /* Identify the output register */
[ ] 88134    assert( pOp->p3<pOp->p1 || pOp->p3>=pOp->p1+pOp->p2 );
[ ] 88135    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 88136    memAboutToChange(p, pOut);
[ ] 88137
[ ] 88138    /* Apply the requested affinity to all inputs
[ ] 88139    */
[ ] 88140    assert( pData0<=pLast );
[ ] 88141    if( zAffinity ){
[ ] 88142      pRec = pData0;
[ ] 88143      do{
[ ] 88144        applyAffinity(pRec, zAffinity[0], encoding);
[ ] 88145        if( zAffinity[0]==SQLITE_AFF_REAL && (pRec->flags & MEM_Int) ){
[ ] 88146          pRec->flags |= MEM_IntReal;
[ ] 88147          pRec->flags &= ~(MEM_Int);
[ ] 88148        }
[ ] 88149        REGISTER_TRACE((int)(pRec-aMem), pRec);
[ ] 88150        zAffinity++;
[ ] 88151        pRec++;
[ ] 88152        assert( zAffinity[0]==0 || pRec<=pLast );
[ ] 88153      }while( zAffinity[0] );
[ ] 88154    }
[ ] 88155
[ ] 88156  #ifdef SQLITE_ENABLE_NULL_TRIM
[ ] 88157    /* NULLs can be safely trimmed from the end of the record, as long as
[ ] 88158    ** as the schema format is 2 or more and none of the omitted columns
[ ] 88159    ** have a non-NULL default value.  Also, the record must be left with
[ ] 88160    ** at least one field.  If P5>0 then it will be one more than the
[ ] 88161    ** index of the right-most column with a non-NULL default value */
[ ] 88162    if( pOp->p5 ){
[ ] 88163      while( (pLast->flags & MEM_Null)!=0 && nField>pOp->p5 ){
[ ] 88164        pLast--;
[ ] 88165        nField--;
[ ] 88166      }
[ ] 88167    }
[ ] 88168  #endif
[ ] 88169
[ ] 88170    /* Loop through the elements that will make up the record to figure
[ ] 88171    ** out how much space is required for the new record.  After this loop,
[ ] 88172    ** the Mem.uTemp field of each term should hold the serial-type that will
[ ] 88173    ** be used for that term in the generated record:
[ ] 88174    **
[ ] 88175    **   Mem.uTemp value    type
[ ] 88176    **   ---------------    ---------------
[ ] 88177    **      0               NULL
[ ] 88178    **      1               1-byte signed integer
[ ] 88179    **      2               2-byte signed integer
[ ] 88180    **      3               3-byte signed integer
[ ] 88181    **      4               4-byte signed integer
[ ] 88182    **      5               6-byte signed integer
[ ] 88183    **      6               8-byte signed integer
[ ] 88184    **      7               IEEE float
[ ] 88185    **      8               Integer constant 0
[ ] 88186    **      9               Integer constant 1
[ ] 88187    **     10,11            reserved for expansion
[ ] 88188    **    N>=12 and even    BLOB
[ ] 88189    **    N>=13 and odd     text
[ ] 88190    **
[ ] 88191    ** The following additional values are computed:
[ ] 88192    **     nHdr        Number of bytes needed for the record header
[ ] 88193    **     nData       Number of bytes of data space needed for the record
[ ] 88194    **     nZero       Zero bytes at the end of the record
[ ] 88195    */
[ ] 88196    pRec = pLast;
[ ] 88197    do{
[ ] 88198      assert( memIsValid(pRec) );
[ ] 88199      if( pRec->flags & MEM_Null ){
[ ] 88200        if( pRec->flags & MEM_Zero ){
[ ] 88201          /* Values with MEM_Null and MEM_Zero are created by xColumn virtual
[ ] 88202          ** table methods that never invoke sqlite3_result_xxxxx() while
[ ] 88203          ** computing an unchanging column value in an UPDATE statement.
[ ] 88204          ** Give such values a special internal-use-only serial-type of 10
[ ] 88205          ** so that they can be passed through to xUpdate and have
[ ] 88206          ** a true sqlite3_value_nochange(). */
[ ] 88207          assert( pOp->p5==OPFLAG_NOCHNG_MAGIC || CORRUPT_DB );
[ ] 88208          pRec->uTemp = 10;
[ ] 88209        }else{
[ ] 88210          pRec->uTemp = 0;
[ ] 88211        }
[ ] 88212        nHdr++;
[ ] 88213      }else if( pRec->flags & (MEM_Int|MEM_IntReal) ){
[ ] 88214        /* Figure out whether to use 1, 2, 4, 6 or 8 bytes. */
[ ] 88215        i64 i = pRec->u.i;
[ ] 88216        u64 uu;
[ ] 88217        testcase( pRec->flags & MEM_Int );
[ ] 88218        testcase( pRec->flags & MEM_IntReal );
[ ] 88219        if( i<0 ){
[ ] 88220          uu = ~i;
[ ] 88221        }else{
[ ] 88222          uu = i;
[ ] 88223        }
[ ] 88224        nHdr++;
[ ] 88225        testcase( uu==127 );               testcase( uu==128 );
[ ] 88226        testcase( uu==32767 );             testcase( uu==32768 );
[ ] 88227        testcase( uu==8388607 );           testcase( uu==8388608 );
[ ] 88228        testcase( uu==2147483647 );        testcase( uu==2147483648 );
[ ] 88229        testcase( uu==140737488355327LL ); testcase( uu==140737488355328LL );
[ ] 88230        if( uu<=127 ){
[ ] 88231          if( (i&1)==i && file_format>=4 ){
[ ] 88232            pRec->uTemp = 8+(u32)uu;
[ ] 88233          }else{
[ ] 88234            nData++;
[ ] 88235            pRec->uTemp = 1;
[ ] 88236          }
[ ] 88237        }else if( uu<=32767 ){
[ ] 88238          nData += 2;
[ ] 88239          pRec->uTemp = 2;
[ ] 88240        }else if( uu<=8388607 ){
[ ] 88241          nData += 3;
[ ] 88242          pRec->uTemp = 3;
[ ] 88243        }else if( uu<=2147483647 ){
[ ] 88244          nData += 4;
[ ] 88245          pRec->uTemp = 4;
[ ] 88246        }else if( uu<=140737488355327LL ){
[ ] 88247          nData += 6;
[ ] 88248          pRec->uTemp = 5;
[ ] 88249        }else{
[ ] 88250          nData += 8;
[ ] 88251          if( pRec->flags & MEM_IntReal ){
[ ] 88252            /* If the value is IntReal and is going to take up 8 bytes to store
[ ] 88253            ** as an integer, then we might as well make it an 8-byte floating
[ ] 88254            ** point value */
[ ] 88255            pRec->u.r = (double)pRec->u.i;
[ ] 88256            pRec->flags &= ~MEM_IntReal;
[ ] 88257            pRec->flags |= MEM_Real;
[ ] 88258            pRec->uTemp = 7;
[ ] 88259          }else{
[ ] 88260            pRec->uTemp = 6;
[ ] 88261          }
[ ] 88262        }
[ ] 88263      }else if( pRec->flags & MEM_Real ){
[ ] 88264        nHdr++;
[ ] 88265        nData += 8;
[ ] 88266        pRec->uTemp = 7;
[ ] 88267      }else{
[ ] 88268        assert( db->mallocFailed || pRec->flags&(MEM_Str|MEM_Blob) );
[ ] 88269        assert( pRec->n>=0 );
[ ] 88270        len = (u32)pRec->n;
[ ] 88271        serial_type = (len*2) + 12 + ((pRec->flags & MEM_Str)!=0);
[ ] 88272        if( pRec->flags & MEM_Zero ){
[ ] 88273          serial_type += pRec->u.nZero*2;
[ ] 88274          if( nData ){
[ ] 88275            if( sqlite3VdbeMemExpandBlob(pRec) ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 88276            len += pRec->u.nZero;
[ ] 88277          }else{
[ ] 88278            nZero += pRec->u.nZero;
[ ] 88279          }
[ ] 88280        }
[ ] 88281        nData += len;
[ ] 88282        nHdr += sqlite3VarintLen(serial_type);
[ ] 88283        pRec->uTemp = serial_type;
[ ] 88284      }
[ ] 88285      if( pRec==pData0 ) break;
[ ] 88286      pRec--;
[ ] 88287    }while(1);
[ ] 88288
[ ] 88289    /* EVIDENCE-OF: R-22564-11647 The header begins with a single varint
[ ] 88290    ** which determines the total number of bytes in the header. The varint
[ ] 88291    ** value is the size of the header in bytes including the size varint
[ ] 88292    ** itself. */
[ ] 88293    testcase( nHdr==126 );
[ ] 88294    testcase( nHdr==127 );
[ ] 88295    if( nHdr<=126 ){
[ ] 88296      /* The common case */
[ ] 88297      nHdr += 1;
[ ] 88298    }else{
[ ] 88299      /* Rare case of a really large header */
[ ] 88300      nVarint = sqlite3VarintLen(nHdr);
[ ] 88301      nHdr += nVarint;
[ ] 88302      if( nVarint<sqlite3VarintLen(nHdr) ) nHdr++;
[ ] 88303    }
[ ] 88304    nByte = nHdr+nData;
[ ] 88305
[ ] 88306    /* Make sure the output register has a buffer large enough to store
[ ] 88307    ** the new record. The output register (pOp->p3) is not allowed to
[ ] 88308    ** be one of the input registers (because the following call to
[ ] 88309    ** sqlite3VdbeMemClearAndResize() could clobber the value before it is used).
[ ] 88310    */
[ ] 88311    if( nByte+nZero<=pOut->szMalloc ){
[ ] 88312      /* The output register is already large enough to hold the record.
[ ] 88313      ** No error checks or buffer enlargement is required */
[ ] 88314      pOut->z = pOut->zMalloc;
[ ] 88315    }else{
[ ] 88316      /* Need to make sure that the output is not too big and then enlarge
[ ] 88317      ** the output register to hold the full result */
[ ] 88318      if( nByte+nZero>db->aLimit[SQLITE_LIMIT_LENGTH] ){
[ ] 88319        goto too_big;
[ ] 88320      }
[ ] 88321      if( sqlite3VdbeMemClearAndResize(pOut, (int)nByte) ){
[ ] 88322        goto no_mem;
[ ] 88323      }
[ ] 88324    }
[ ] 88325    pOut->n = (int)nByte;
[ ] 88326    pOut->flags = MEM_Blob;
[ ] 88327    if( nZero ){
[ ] 88328      pOut->u.nZero = nZero;
[ ] 88329      pOut->flags |= MEM_Zero;
[ ] 88330    }
[ ] 88331    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pOut);
[ ] 88332    zHdr = (u8 *)pOut->z;
[ ] 88333    zPayload = zHdr + nHdr;
[ ] 88334
[ ] 88335    /* Write the record */
[ ] 88336    zHdr += putVarint32(zHdr, nHdr);
[ ] 88337    assert( pData0<=pLast );
[ ] 88338    pRec = pData0;
[ ] 88339    do{
[ ] 88340      serial_type = pRec->uTemp;
[ ] 88341      /* EVIDENCE-OF: R-06529-47362 Following the size varint are one or more
[ ] 88342      ** additional varints, one per column. */
[ ] 88343      zHdr += putVarint32(zHdr, serial_type);            /* serial type */
[ ] 88344      /* EVIDENCE-OF: R-64536-51728 The values for each column in the record
[ ] 88345      ** immediately follow the header. */
[ ] 88346      zPayload += sqlite3VdbeSerialPut(zPayload, pRec, serial_type); /* content */
[ ] 88347    }while( (++pRec)<=pLast );
[ ] 88348    assert( nHdr==(int)(zHdr - (u8*)pOut->z) );
[ ] 88349    assert( nByte==(int)(zPayload - (u8*)pOut->z) );
[ ] 88350
[ ] 88351    assert( pOp->p3>0 && pOp->p3<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 88352    REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p3, pOut);
[ ] 88353    break;
[ ] 88354  }
[ ] 88355
[ ] 88356  /* Opcode: Count P1 P2 p3 * *
[ ] 88357  ** Synopsis: r[P2]=count()
[ ] 88358  **
[ ] 88359  ** Store the number of entries (an integer value) in the table or index
[ ] 88360  ** opened by cursor P1 in register P2.
[ ] 88361  **
[ ] 88362  ** If P3==0, then an exact count is obtained, which involves visiting
[ ] 88363  ** every btree page of the table.  But if P3 is non-zero, an estimate
[ ] 88364  ** is returned based on the current cursor position.
[ ] 88365  */
[ ] 88366  case OP_Count: {         /* out2 */
[ ] 88367    i64 nEntry;
[ ] 88368    BtCursor *pCrsr;
[ ] 88369
[ ] 88370    assert( p->apCsr[pOp->p1]->eCurType==CURTYPE_BTREE );
[ ] 88371    pCrsr = p->apCsr[pOp->p1]->uc.pCursor;
[ ] 88372    assert( pCrsr );
[ ] 88373    if( pOp->p3 ){
[ ] 88374      nEntry = sqlite3BtreeRowCountEst(pCrsr);
[ ] 88375    }else{
[ ] 88376      nEntry = 0;  /* Not needed.  Only used to silence a warning. */
[ ] 88377      rc = sqlite3BtreeCount(db, pCrsr, &nEntry);
[ ] 88378      if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88379    }
[ ] 88380    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 88381    pOut->u.i = nEntry;
[ ] 88382    goto check_for_interrupt;
[ ] 88383  }
[ ] 88384
[ ] 88385  /* Opcode: Savepoint P1 * * P4 *
[ ] 88386  **
[ ] 88387  ** Open, release or rollback the savepoint named by parameter P4, depending
[ ] 88388  ** on the value of P1. To open a new savepoint set P1==0 (SAVEPOINT_BEGIN).
[ ] 88389  ** To release (commit) an existing savepoint set P1==1 (SAVEPOINT_RELEASE).
[ ] 88390  ** To rollback an existing savepoint set P1==2 (SAVEPOINT_ROLLBACK).
[ ] 88391  */
[ ] 88392  case OP_Savepoint: {
[ ] 88393    int p1;                         /* Value of P1 operand */
[ ] 88394    char *zName;                    /* Name of savepoint */
[ ] 88395    int nName;
[ ] 88396    Savepoint *pNew;
[ ] 88397    Savepoint *pSavepoint;
[ ] 88398    Savepoint *pTmp;
[ ] 88399    int iSavepoint;
[ ] 88400    int ii;
[ ] 88401
[ ] 88402    p1 = pOp->p1;
[ ] 88403    zName = pOp->p4.z;
[ ] 88404
[ ] 88405    /* Assert that the p1 parameter is valid. Also that if there is no open
[ ] 88406    ** transaction, then there cannot be any savepoints.
[ ] 88407    */
[ ] 88408    assert( db->pSavepoint==0 || db->autoCommit==0 );
[ ] 88409    assert( p1==SAVEPOINT_BEGIN||p1==SAVEPOINT_RELEASE||p1==SAVEPOINT_ROLLBACK );
[ ] 88410    assert( db->pSavepoint || db->isTransactionSavepoint==0 );
[ ] 88411    assert( checkSavepointCount(db) );
[ ] 88412    assert( p->bIsReader );
[ ] 88413
[ ] 88414    if( p1==SAVEPOINT_BEGIN ){
[ ] 88415      if( db->nVdbeWrite>0 ){
[ ] 88416        /* A new savepoint cannot be created if there are active write
[ ] 88417        ** statements (i.e. open read/write incremental blob handles).
[ ] 88418        */
[ ] 88419        sqlite3VdbeError(p, "cannot open savepoint - SQL statements in progress");
[ ] 88420        rc = SQLITE_BUSY;
[ ] 88421      }else{
[ ] 88422        nName = sqlite3Strlen30(zName);
[ ] 88423
[ ] 88424  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 88425        /* This call is Ok even if this savepoint is actually a transaction
[ ] 88426        ** savepoint (and therefore should not prompt xSavepoint()) callbacks.
[ ] 88427        ** If this is a transaction savepoint being opened, it is guaranteed
[ ] 88428        ** that the db->aVTrans[] array is empty.  */
[ ] 88429        assert( db->autoCommit==0 || db->nVTrans==0 );
[ ] 88430        rc = sqlite3VtabSavepoint(db, SAVEPOINT_BEGIN,
[ ] 88431                                  db->nStatement+db->nSavepoint);
[ ] 88432        if( rc!=SQLITE_OK ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88433  #endif
[ ] 88434
[ ] 88435        /* Create a new savepoint structure. */
[ ] 88436        pNew = sqlite3DbMallocRawNN(db, sizeof(Savepoint)+nName+1);
[ ] 88437        if( pNew ){
[ ] 88438          pNew->zName = (char *)&pNew[1];
[ ] 88439          memcpy(pNew->zName, zName, nName+1);
[ ] 88440
[ ] 88441          /* If there is no open transaction, then mark this as a special
[ ] 88442          ** "transaction savepoint". */
[ ] 88443          if( db->autoCommit ){
[ ] 88444            db->autoCommit = 0;
[ ] 88445            db->isTransactionSavepoint = 1;
[ ] 88446          }else{
[ ] 88447            db->nSavepoint++;
[ ] 88448          }
[ ] 88449
[ ] 88450          /* Link the new savepoint into the database handle's list. */
[ ] 88451          pNew->pNext = db->pSavepoint;
[ ] 88452          db->pSavepoint = pNew;
[ ] 88453          pNew->nDeferredCons = db->nDeferredCons;
[ ] 88454          pNew->nDeferredImmCons = db->nDeferredImmCons;
[ ] 88455        }
[ ] 88456      }
[ ] 88457    }else{
[ ] 88458      assert( p1==SAVEPOINT_RELEASE || p1==SAVEPOINT_ROLLBACK );
[ ] 88459      iSavepoint = 0;
[ ] 88460
[ ] 88461      /* Find the named savepoint. If there is no such savepoint, then an
[ ] 88462      ** an error is returned to the user.  */
[ ] 88463      for(
[ ] 88464        pSavepoint = db->pSavepoint;
[ ] 88465        pSavepoint && sqlite3StrICmp(pSavepoint->zName, zName);
[ ] 88466        pSavepoint = pSavepoint->pNext
[ ] 88467      ){
[ ] 88468        iSavepoint++;
[ ] 88469      }
[ ] 88470      if( !pSavepoint ){
[ ] 88471        sqlite3VdbeError(p, "no such savepoint: %s", zName);
[ ] 88472        rc = SQLITE_ERROR;
[ ] 88473      }else if( db->nVdbeWrite>0 && p1==SAVEPOINT_RELEASE ){
[ ] 88474        /* It is not possible to release (commit) a savepoint if there are
[ ] 88475        ** active write statements.
[ ] 88476        */
[ ] 88477        sqlite3VdbeError(p, "cannot release savepoint - "
[ ] 88478                            "SQL statements in progress");
[ ] 88479        rc = SQLITE_BUSY;
[ ] 88480      }else{
[ ] 88481
[ ] 88482        /* Determine whether or not this is a transaction savepoint. If so,
[ ] 88483        ** and this is a RELEASE command, then the current transaction
[ ] 88484        ** is committed.
[ ] 88485        */
[ ] 88486        int isTransaction = pSavepoint->pNext==0 && db->isTransactionSavepoint;
[ ] 88487        if( isTransaction && p1==SAVEPOINT_RELEASE ){
[ ] 88488          if( (rc = sqlite3VdbeCheckFk(p, 1))!=SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 88489            goto vdbe_return;
[ ] 88490          }
[ ] 88491          db->autoCommit = 1;
[ ] 88492          if( sqlite3VdbeHalt(p)==SQLITE_BUSY ){
[ ] 88493            p->pc = (int)(pOp - aOp);
[ ] 88494            db->autoCommit = 0;
[ ] 88495            p->rc = rc = SQLITE_BUSY;
[ ] 88496            goto vdbe_return;
[ ] 88497          }
[ ] 88498          rc = p->rc;
[ ] 88499          if( rc ){
[ ] 88500            db->autoCommit = 0;
[ ] 88501          }else{
[ ] 88502            db->isTransactionSavepoint = 0;
[ ] 88503          }
[ ] 88504        }else{
[ ] 88505          int isSchemaChange;
[ ] 88506          iSavepoint = db->nSavepoint - iSavepoint - 1;
[ ] 88507          if( p1==SAVEPOINT_ROLLBACK ){
[ ] 88508            isSchemaChange = (db->mDbFlags & DBFLAG_SchemaChange)!=0;
[ ] 88509            for(ii=0; ii<db->nDb; ii++){
[ ] 88510              rc = sqlite3BtreeTripAllCursors(db->aDb[ii].pBt,
[ ] 88511                                         SQLITE_ABORT_ROLLBACK,
[ ] 88512                                         isSchemaChange==0);
[ ] 88513              if( rc!=SQLITE_OK ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88514            }
[ ] 88515          }else{
[ ] 88516            assert( p1==SAVEPOINT_RELEASE );
[ ] 88517            isSchemaChange = 0;
[ ] 88518          }
[ ] 88519          for(ii=0; ii<db->nDb; ii++){
[ ] 88520            rc = sqlite3BtreeSavepoint(db->aDb[ii].pBt, p1, iSavepoint);
[ ] 88521            if( rc!=SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 88522              goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88523            }
[ ] 88524          }
[ ] 88525          if( isSchemaChange ){
[ ] 88526            sqlite3ExpirePreparedStatements(db, 0);
[ ] 88527            sqlite3ResetAllSchemasOfConnection(db);
[ ] 88528            db->mDbFlags |= DBFLAG_SchemaChange;
[ ] 88529          }
[ ] 88530        }
[ ] 88531        if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88532
[ ] 88533        /* Regardless of whether this is a RELEASE or ROLLBACK, destroy all
[ ] 88534        ** savepoints nested inside of the savepoint being operated on. */
[ ] 88535        while( db->pSavepoint!=pSavepoint ){
[ ] 88536          pTmp = db->pSavepoint;
[ ] 88537          db->pSavepoint = pTmp->pNext;
[ ] 88538          sqlite3DbFree(db, pTmp);
[ ] 88539          db->nSavepoint--;
[ ] 88540        }
[ ] 88541
[ ] 88542        /* If it is a RELEASE, then destroy the savepoint being operated on
[ ] 88543        ** too. If it is a ROLLBACK TO, then set the number of deferred
[ ] 88544        ** constraint violations present in the database to the value stored
[ ] 88545        ** when the savepoint was created.  */
[ ] 88546        if( p1==SAVEPOINT_RELEASE ){
[ ] 88547          assert( pSavepoint==db->pSavepoint );
[ ] 88548          db->pSavepoint = pSavepoint->pNext;
[ ] 88549          sqlite3DbFree(db, pSavepoint);
[ ] 88550          if( !isTransaction ){
[ ] 88551            db->nSavepoint--;
[ ] 88552          }
[ ] 88553        }else{
[ ] 88554          assert( p1==SAVEPOINT_ROLLBACK );
[ ] 88555          db->nDeferredCons = pSavepoint->nDeferredCons;
[ ] 88556          db->nDeferredImmCons = pSavepoint->nDeferredImmCons;
[ ] 88557        }
[ ] 88558
[ ] 88559        if( !isTransaction || p1==SAVEPOINT_ROLLBACK ){
[ ] 88560          rc = sqlite3VtabSavepoint(db, p1, iSavepoint);
[ ] 88561          if( rc!=SQLITE_OK ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88562        }
[ ] 88563      }
[ ] 88564    }
[ ] 88565    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88566
[ ] 88567    break;
[ ] 88568  }
[ ] 88569
[ ] 88570  /* Opcode: AutoCommit P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 88571  **
[ ] 88572  ** Set the database auto-commit flag to P1 (1 or 0). If P2 is true, roll
[ ] 88573  ** back any currently active btree transactions. If there are any active
[ ] 88574  ** VMs (apart from this one), then a ROLLBACK fails.  A COMMIT fails if
[ ] 88575  ** there are active writing VMs or active VMs that use shared cache.
[ ] 88576  **
[ ] 88577  ** This instruction causes the VM to halt.
[ ] 88578  */
[ ] 88579  case OP_AutoCommit: {
[ ] 88580    int desiredAutoCommit;
[ ] 88581    int iRollback;
[ ] 88582
[ ] 88583    desiredAutoCommit = pOp->p1;
[ ] 88584    iRollback = pOp->p2;
[ ] 88585    assert( desiredAutoCommit==1 || desiredAutoCommit==0 );
[ ] 88586    assert( desiredAutoCommit==1 || iRollback==0 );
[ ] 88587    assert( db->nVdbeActive>0 );  /* At least this one VM is active */
[ ] 88588    assert( p->bIsReader );
[ ] 88589
[ ] 88590    if( desiredAutoCommit!=db->autoCommit ){
[ ] 88591      if( iRollback ){
[ ] 88592        assert( desiredAutoCommit==1 );
[ ] 88593        sqlite3RollbackAll(db, SQLITE_ABORT_ROLLBACK);
[ ] 88594        db->autoCommit = 1;
[ ] 88595      }else if( desiredAutoCommit && db->nVdbeWrite>0 ){
[ ] 88596        /* If this instruction implements a COMMIT and other VMs are writing
[ ] 88597        ** return an error indicating that the other VMs must complete first.
[ ] 88598        */
[ ] 88599        sqlite3VdbeError(p, "cannot commit transaction - "
[ ] 88600                            "SQL statements in progress");
[ ] 88601        rc = SQLITE_BUSY;
[ ] 88602        goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88603      }else if( (rc = sqlite3VdbeCheckFk(p, 1))!=SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 88604        goto vdbe_return;
[ ] 88605      }else{
[ ] 88606        db->autoCommit = (u8)desiredAutoCommit;
[ ] 88607      }
[ ] 88608      if( sqlite3VdbeHalt(p)==SQLITE_BUSY ){
[ ] 88609        p->pc = (int)(pOp - aOp);
[ ] 88610        db->autoCommit = (u8)(1-desiredAutoCommit);
[ ] 88611        p->rc = rc = SQLITE_BUSY;
[ ] 88612        goto vdbe_return;
[ ] 88613      }
[ ] 88614      sqlite3CloseSavepoints(db);
[ ] 88615      if( p->rc==SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 88616        rc = SQLITE_DONE;
[ ] 88617      }else{
[ ] 88618        rc = SQLITE_ERROR;
[ ] 88619      }
[ ] 88620      goto vdbe_return;
[ ] 88621    }else{
[ ] 88622      sqlite3VdbeError(p,
[ ] 88623          (!desiredAutoCommit)?"cannot start a transaction within a transaction":(
[ ] 88624          (iRollback)?"cannot rollback - no transaction is active":
[ ] 88625                     "cannot commit - no transaction is active"));
[ ] 88626
[ ] 88627      rc = SQLITE_ERROR;
[ ] 88628      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88629    }
[ ] 88630    /*NOTREACHED*/ assert(0);
[ ] 88631  }
[ ] 88632
[ ] 88633  /* Opcode: Transaction P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 88634  **
[ ] 88635  ** Begin a transaction on database P1 if a transaction is not already
[ ] 88636  ** active.
[ ] 88637  ** If P2 is non-zero, then a write-transaction is started, or if a
[ ] 88638  ** read-transaction is already active, it is upgraded to a write-transaction.
[ ] 88639  ** If P2 is zero, then a read-transaction is started.
[ ] 88640  **
[ ] 88641  ** P1 is the index of the database file on which the transaction is
[ ] 88642  ** started.  Index 0 is the main database file and index 1 is the
[ ] 88643  ** file used for temporary tables.  Indices of 2 or more are used for
[ ] 88644  ** attached databases.
[ ] 88645  **
[ ] 88646  ** If a write-transaction is started and the Vdbe.usesStmtJournal flag is
[ ] 88647  ** true (this flag is set if the Vdbe may modify more than one row and may
[ ] 88648  ** throw an ABORT exception), a statement transaction may also be opened.
[ ] 88649  ** More specifically, a statement transaction is opened iff the database
[ ] 88650  ** connection is currently not in autocommit mode, or if there are other
[ ] 88651  ** active statements. A statement transaction allows the changes made by this
[ ] 88652  ** VDBE to be rolled back after an error without having to roll back the
[ ] 88653  ** entire transaction. If no error is encountered, the statement transaction
[ ] 88654  ** will automatically commit when the VDBE halts.
[ ] 88655  **
[ ] 88656  ** If P5!=0 then this opcode also checks the schema cookie against P3
[ ] 88657  ** and the schema generation counter against P4.
[ ] 88658  ** The cookie changes its value whenever the database schema changes.
[ ] 88659  ** This operation is used to detect when that the cookie has changed
[ ] 88660  ** and that the current process needs to reread the schema.  If the schema
[ ] 88661  ** cookie in P3 differs from the schema cookie in the database header or
[ ] 88662  ** if the schema generation counter in P4 differs from the current
[ ] 88663  ** generation counter, then an SQLITE_SCHEMA error is raised and execution
[ ] 88664  ** halts.  The sqlite3_step() wrapper function might then reprepare the
[ ] 88665  ** statement and rerun it from the beginning.
[ ] 88666  */
[ ] 88667  case OP_Transaction: {
[ ] 88668    Btree *pBt;
[ ] 88669    int iMeta = 0;
[ ] 88670
[ ] 88671    assert( p->bIsReader );
[ ] 88672    assert( p->readOnly==0 || pOp->p2==0 );
[ ] 88673    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<db->nDb );
[ ] 88674    assert( DbMaskTest(p->btreeMask, pOp->p1) );
[ ] 88675    if( pOp->p2 && (db->flags & SQLITE_QueryOnly)!=0 ){
[ ] 88676      rc = SQLITE_READONLY;
[ ] 88677      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88678    }
[ ] 88679    pBt = db->aDb[pOp->p1].pBt;
[ ] 88680
[ ] 88681    if( pBt ){
[ ] 88682      rc = sqlite3BtreeBeginTrans(pBt, pOp->p2, &iMeta);
[ ] 88683      testcase( rc==SQLITE_BUSY_SNAPSHOT );
[ ] 88684      testcase( rc==SQLITE_BUSY_RECOVERY );
[ ] 88685      if( rc!=SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 88686        if( (rc&0xff)==SQLITE_BUSY ){
[ ] 88687          p->pc = (int)(pOp - aOp);
[ ] 88688          p->rc = rc;
[ ] 88689          goto vdbe_return;
[ ] 88690        }
[ ] 88691        goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88692      }
[ ] 88693
[ ] 88694      if( p->usesStmtJournal
[ ] 88695       && pOp->p2
[ ] 88696       && (db->autoCommit==0 || db->nVdbeRead>1)
[ ] 88697      ){
[ ] 88698        assert( sqlite3BtreeIsInTrans(pBt) );
[ ] 88699        if( p->iStatement==0 ){
[ ] 88700          assert( db->nStatement>=0 && db->nSavepoint>=0 );
[ ] 88701          db->nStatement++;
[ ] 88702          p->iStatement = db->nSavepoint + db->nStatement;
[ ] 88703        }
[ ] 88704
[ ] 88705        rc = sqlite3VtabSavepoint(db, SAVEPOINT_BEGIN, p->iStatement-1);
[ ] 88706        if( rc==SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 88707          rc = sqlite3BtreeBeginStmt(pBt, p->iStatement);
[ ] 88708        }
[ ] 88709
[ ] 88710        /* Store the current value of the database handles deferred constraint
[ ] 88711        ** counter. If the statement transaction needs to be rolled back,
[ ] 88712        ** the value of this counter needs to be restored too.  */
[ ] 88713        p->nStmtDefCons = db->nDeferredCons;
[ ] 88714        p->nStmtDefImmCons = db->nDeferredImmCons;
[ ] 88715      }
[ ] 88716    }
[ ] 88717    assert( pOp->p5==0 || pOp->p4type==P4_INT32 );
[ ] 88718    if( pOp->p5
[ ] 88719     && (iMeta!=pOp->p3
[ ] 88720        || db->aDb[pOp->p1].pSchema->iGeneration!=pOp->p4.i)
[ ] 88721    ){
[ ] 88722      /*
[ ] 88723      ** IMPLEMENTATION-OF: R-03189-51135 As each SQL statement runs, the schema
[ ] 88724      ** version is checked to ensure that the schema has not changed since the
[ ] 88725      ** SQL statement was prepared.
[ ] 88726      */
[ ] 88727      sqlite3DbFree(db, p->zErrMsg);
[ ] 88728      p->zErrMsg = sqlite3DbStrDup(db, "database schema has changed");
[ ] 88729      /* If the schema-cookie from the database file matches the cookie
[ ] 88730      ** stored with the in-memory representation of the schema, do
[ ] 88731      ** not reload the schema from the database file.
[ ] 88732      **
[ ] 88733      ** If virtual-tables are in use, this is not just an optimization.
[ ] 88734      ** Often, v-tables store their data in other SQLite tables, which
[ ] 88735      ** are queried from within xNext() and other v-table methods using
[ ] 88736      ** prepared queries. If such a query is out-of-date, we do not want to
[ ] 88737      ** discard the database schema, as the user code implementing the
[ ] 88738      ** v-table would have to be ready for the sqlite3_vtab structure itself
[ ] 88739      ** to be invalidated whenever sqlite3_step() is called from within
[ ] 88740      ** a v-table method.
[ ] 88741      */
[ ] 88742      if( db->aDb[pOp->p1].pSchema->schema_cookie!=iMeta ){
[ ] 88743        sqlite3ResetOneSchema(db, pOp->p1);
[ ] 88744      }
[ ] 88745      p->expired = 1;
[ ] 88746      rc = SQLITE_SCHEMA;
[ ] 88747    }
[ ] 88748    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88749    break;
[ ] 88750  }
[ ] 88751
[ ] 88752  /* Opcode: ReadCookie P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 88753  **
[ ] 88754  ** Read cookie number P3 from database P1 and write it into register P2.
[ ] 88755  ** P3==1 is the schema version.  P3==2 is the database format.
[ ] 88756  ** P3==3 is the recommended pager cache size, and so forth.  P1==0 is
[ ] 88757  ** the main database file and P1==1 is the database file used to store
[ ] 88758  ** temporary tables.
[ ] 88759  **
[ ] 88760  ** There must be a read-lock on the database (either a transaction
[ ] 88761  ** must be started or there must be an open cursor) before
[ ] 88762  ** executing this instruction.
[ ] 88763  */
[ ] 88764  case OP_ReadCookie: {               /* out2 */
[ ] 88765    int iMeta;
[ ] 88766    int iDb;
[ ] 88767    int iCookie;
[ ] 88768
[ ] 88769    assert( p->bIsReader );
[ ] 88770    iDb = pOp->p1;
[ ] 88771    iCookie = pOp->p3;
[ ] 88772    assert( pOp->p3<SQLITE_N_BTREE_META );
[ ] 88773    assert( iDb>=0 && iDb<db->nDb );
[ ] 88774    assert( db->aDb[iDb].pBt!=0 );
[ ] 88775    assert( DbMaskTest(p->btreeMask, iDb) );
[ ] 88776
[ ] 88777    sqlite3BtreeGetMeta(db->aDb[iDb].pBt, iCookie, (u32 *)&iMeta);
[ ] 88778    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 88779    pOut->u.i = iMeta;
[ ] 88780    break;
[ ] 88781  }
[ ] 88782
[ ] 88783  /* Opcode: SetCookie P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 88784  **
[ ] 88785  ** Write the integer value P3 into cookie number P2 of database P1.
[ ] 88786  ** P2==1 is the schema version.  P2==2 is the database format.
[ ] 88787  ** P2==3 is the recommended pager cache
[ ] 88788  ** size, and so forth.  P1==0 is the main database file and P1==1 is the
[ ] 88789  ** database file used to store temporary tables.
[ ] 88790  **
[ ] 88791  ** A transaction must be started before executing this opcode.
[ ] 88792  */
[ ] 88793  case OP_SetCookie: {
[ ] 88794    Db *pDb;
[ ] 88795
[ ] 88796    sqlite3VdbeIncrWriteCounter(p, 0);
[ ] 88797    assert( pOp->p2<SQLITE_N_BTREE_META );
[ ] 88798    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<db->nDb );
[ ] 88799    assert( DbMaskTest(p->btreeMask, pOp->p1) );
[ ] 88800    assert( p->readOnly==0 );
[ ] 88801    pDb = &db->aDb[pOp->p1];
[ ] 88802    assert( pDb->pBt!=0 );
[ ] 88803    assert( sqlite3SchemaMutexHeld(db, pOp->p1, 0) );
[ ] 88804    /* See note about index shifting on OP_ReadCookie */
[ ] 88805    rc = sqlite3BtreeUpdateMeta(pDb->pBt, pOp->p2, pOp->p3);
[ ] 88806    if( pOp->p2==BTREE_SCHEMA_VERSION ){
[ ] 88807      /* When the schema cookie changes, record the new cookie internally */
[ ] 88808      pDb->pSchema->schema_cookie = pOp->p3;
[ ] 88809      db->mDbFlags |= DBFLAG_SchemaChange;
[ ] 88810    }else if( pOp->p2==BTREE_FILE_FORMAT ){
[ ] 88811      /* Record changes in the file format */
[ ] 88812      pDb->pSchema->file_format = pOp->p3;
[ ] 88813    }
[ ] 88814    if( pOp->p1==1 ){
[ ] 88815      /* Invalidate all prepared statements whenever the TEMP database
[ ] 88816      ** schema is changed.  Ticket #1644 */
[ ] 88817      sqlite3ExpirePreparedStatements(db, 0);
[ ] 88818      p->expired = 0;
[ ] 88819    }
[ ] 88820    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88821    break;
[ ] 88822  }
[ ] 88823
[ ] 88824  /* Opcode: OpenRead P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 88825  ** Synopsis: root=P2 iDb=P3
[ ] 88826  **
[ ] 88827  ** Open a read-only cursor for the database table whose root page is
[ ] 88828  ** P2 in a database file.  The database file is determined by P3.
[ ] 88829  ** P3==0 means the main database, P3==1 means the database used for
[ ] 88830  ** temporary tables, and P3>1 means used the corresponding attached
[ ] 88831  ** database.  Give the new cursor an identifier of P1.  The P1
[ ] 88832  ** values need not be contiguous but all P1 values should be small integers.
[ ] 88833  ** It is an error for P1 to be negative.
[ ] 88834  **
[ ] 88835  ** Allowed P5 bits:
[ ] 88836  ** <ul>
[ ] 88837  ** <li>  <b>0x02 OPFLAG_SEEKEQ</b>: This cursor will only be used for
[ ] 88838  **       equality lookups (implemented as a pair of opcodes OP_SeekGE/OP_IdxGT
[ ] 88839  **       of OP_SeekLE/OP_IdxLT)
[ ] 88840  ** </ul>
[ ] 88841  **
[ ] 88842  ** The P4 value may be either an integer (P4_INT32) or a pointer to
[ ] 88843  ** a KeyInfo structure (P4_KEYINFO). If it is a pointer to a KeyInfo
[ ] 88844  ** object, then table being opened must be an [index b-tree] where the
[ ] 88845  ** KeyInfo object defines the content and collating
[ ] 88846  ** sequence of that index b-tree. Otherwise, if P4 is an integer
[ ] 88847  ** value, then the table being opened must be a [table b-tree] with a
[ ] 88848  ** number of columns no less than the value of P4.
[ ] 88849  **
[ ] 88850  ** See also: OpenWrite, ReopenIdx
[ ] 88851  */
[ ] 88852  /* Opcode: ReopenIdx P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 88853  ** Synopsis: root=P2 iDb=P3
[ ] 88854  **
[ ] 88855  ** The ReopenIdx opcode works like OP_OpenRead except that it first
[ ] 88856  ** checks to see if the cursor on P1 is already open on the same
[ ] 88857  ** b-tree and if it is this opcode becomes a no-op.  In other words,
[ ] 88858  ** if the cursor is already open, do not reopen it.
[ ] 88859  **
[ ] 88860  ** The ReopenIdx opcode may only be used with P5==0 or P5==OPFLAG_SEEKEQ
[ ] 88861  ** and with P4 being a P4_KEYINFO object.  Furthermore, the P3 value must
[ ] 88862  ** be the same as every other ReopenIdx or OpenRead for the same cursor
[ ] 88863  ** number.
[ ] 88864  **
[ ] 88865  ** Allowed P5 bits:
[ ] 88866  ** <ul>
[ ] 88867  ** <li>  <b>0x02 OPFLAG_SEEKEQ</b>: This cursor will only be used for
[ ] 88868  **       equality lookups (implemented as a pair of opcodes OP_SeekGE/OP_IdxGT
[ ] 88869  **       of OP_SeekLE/OP_IdxLT)
[ ] 88870  ** </ul>
[ ] 88871  **
[ ] 88872  ** See also: OP_OpenRead, OP_OpenWrite
[ ] 88873  */
[ ] 88874  /* Opcode: OpenWrite P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 88875  ** Synopsis: root=P2 iDb=P3
[ ] 88876  **
[ ] 88877  ** Open a read/write cursor named P1 on the table or index whose root
[ ] 88878  ** page is P2 (or whose root page is held in register P2 if the
[ ] 88879  ** OPFLAG_P2ISREG bit is set in P5 - see below).
[ ] 88880  **
[ ] 88881  ** The P4 value may be either an integer (P4_INT32) or a pointer to
[ ] 88882  ** a KeyInfo structure (P4_KEYINFO). If it is a pointer to a KeyInfo
[ ] 88883  ** object, then table being opened must be an [index b-tree] where the
[ ] 88884  ** KeyInfo object defines the content and collating
[ ] 88885  ** sequence of that index b-tree. Otherwise, if P4 is an integer
[ ] 88886  ** value, then the table being opened must be a [table b-tree] with a
[ ] 88887  ** number of columns no less than the value of P4.
[ ] 88888  **
[ ] 88889  ** Allowed P5 bits:
[ ] 88890  ** <ul>
[ ] 88891  ** <li>  <b>0x02 OPFLAG_SEEKEQ</b>: This cursor will only be used for
[ ] 88892  **       equality lookups (implemented as a pair of opcodes OP_SeekGE/OP_IdxGT
[ ] 88893  **       of OP_SeekLE/OP_IdxLT)
[ ] 88894  ** <li>  <b>0x08 OPFLAG_FORDELETE</b>: This cursor is used only to seek
[ ] 88895  **       and subsequently delete entries in an index btree.  This is a
[ ] 88896  **       hint to the storage engine that the storage engine is allowed to
[ ] 88897  **       ignore.  The hint is not used by the official SQLite b*tree storage
[ ] 88898  **       engine, but is used by COMDB2.
[ ] 88899  ** <li>  <b>0x10 OPFLAG_P2ISREG</b>: Use the content of register P2
[ ] 88900  **       as the root page, not the value of P2 itself.
[ ] 88901  ** </ul>
[ ] 88902  **
[ ] 88903  ** This instruction works like OpenRead except that it opens the cursor
[ ] 88904  ** in read/write mode.
[ ] 88905  **
[ ] 88906  ** See also: OP_OpenRead, OP_ReopenIdx
[ ] 88907  */
[ ] 88908  case OP_ReopenIdx: {
[ ] 88909    int nField;
[ ] 88910    KeyInfo *pKeyInfo;
[ ] 88911    int p2;
[ ] 88912    int iDb;
[ ] 88913    int wrFlag;
[ ] 88914    Btree *pX;
[ ] 88915    VdbeCursor *pCur;
[ ] 88916    Db *pDb;
[ ] 88917
[ ] 88918    assert( pOp->p5==0 || pOp->p5==OPFLAG_SEEKEQ );
[ ] 88919    assert( pOp->p4type==P4_KEYINFO );
[ ] 88920    pCur = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 88921    if( pCur && pCur->pgnoRoot==(u32)pOp->p2 ){
[ ] 88922      assert( pCur->iDb==pOp->p3 );      /* Guaranteed by the code generator */
[ ] 88923      goto open_cursor_set_hints;
[ ] 88924    }
[ ] 88925    /* If the cursor is not currently open or is open on a different
[ ] 88926    ** index, then fall through into OP_OpenRead to force a reopen */
[ ] 88927  case OP_OpenRead:
[ ] 88928  case OP_OpenWrite:
[ ] 88929
[ ] 88930    assert( pOp->opcode==OP_OpenWrite || pOp->p5==0 || pOp->p5==OPFLAG_SEEKEQ );
[ ] 88931    assert( p->bIsReader );
[ ] 88932    assert( pOp->opcode==OP_OpenRead || pOp->opcode==OP_ReopenIdx
[ ] 88933            || p->readOnly==0 );
[ ] 88934
[ ] 88935    if( p->expired==1 ){
[ ] 88936      rc = SQLITE_ABORT_ROLLBACK;
[ ] 88937      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 88938    }
[ ] 88939
[ ] 88940    nField = 0;
[ ] 88941    pKeyInfo = 0;
[ ] 88942    p2 = pOp->p2;
[ ] 88943    iDb = pOp->p3;
[ ] 88944    assert( iDb>=0 && iDb<db->nDb );
[ ] 88945    assert( DbMaskTest(p->btreeMask, iDb) );
[ ] 88946    pDb = &db->aDb[iDb];
[ ] 88947    pX = pDb->pBt;
[ ] 88948    assert( pX!=0 );
[ ] 88949    if( pOp->opcode==OP_OpenWrite ){
[ ] 88950      assert( OPFLAG_FORDELETE==BTREE_FORDELETE );
[ ] 88951      wrFlag = BTREE_WRCSR | (pOp->p5 & OPFLAG_FORDELETE);
[ ] 88952      assert( sqlite3SchemaMutexHeld(db, iDb, 0) );
[ ] 88953      if( pDb->pSchema->file_format < p->minWriteFileFormat ){
[ ] 88954        p->minWriteFileFormat = pDb->pSchema->file_format;
[ ] 88955      }
[ ] 88956    }else{
[ ] 88957      wrFlag = 0;
[ ] 88958    }
[ ] 88959    if( pOp->p5 & OPFLAG_P2ISREG ){
[ ] 88960      assert( p2>0 );
[ ] 88961      assert( p2<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 88962      assert( pOp->opcode==OP_OpenWrite );
[ ] 88963      pIn2 = &aMem[p2];
[ ] 88964      assert( memIsValid(pIn2) );
[ ] 88965      assert( (pIn2->flags & MEM_Int)!=0 );
[ ] 88966      sqlite3VdbeMemIntegerify(pIn2);
[ ] 88967      p2 = (int)pIn2->u.i;
[ ] 88968      /* The p2 value always comes from a prior OP_CreateBtree opcode and
[ ] 88969      ** that opcode will always set the p2 value to 2 or more or else fail.
[ ] 88970      ** If there were a failure, the prepared statement would have halted
[ ] 88971      ** before reaching this instruction. */
[ ] 88972      assert( p2>=2 );
[ ] 88973    }
[ ] 88974    if( pOp->p4type==P4_KEYINFO ){
[ ] 88975      pKeyInfo = pOp->p4.pKeyInfo;
[ ] 88976      assert( pKeyInfo->enc==ENC(db) );
[ ] 88977      assert( pKeyInfo->db==db );
[ ] 88978      nField = pKeyInfo->nAllField;
[ ] 88979    }else if( pOp->p4type==P4_INT32 ){
[ ] 88980      nField = pOp->p4.i;
[ ] 88981    }
[ ] 88982    assert( pOp->p1>=0 );
[ ] 88983    assert( nField>=0 );
[ ] 88984    testcase( nField==0 );  /* Table with INTEGER PRIMARY KEY and nothing else */
[ ] 88985    pCur = allocateCursor(p, pOp->p1, nField, iDb, CURTYPE_BTREE);
[ ] 88986    if( pCur==0 ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 88987    pCur->nullRow = 1;
[ ] 88988    pCur->isOrdered = 1;
[ ] 88989    pCur->pgnoRoot = p2;
[ ] 88990  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 88991    pCur->wrFlag = wrFlag;
[ ] 88992  #endif
[ ] 88993    rc = sqlite3BtreeCursor(pX, p2, wrFlag, pKeyInfo, pCur->uc.pCursor);
[ ] 88994    pCur->pKeyInfo = pKeyInfo;
[ ] 88995    /* Set the VdbeCursor.isTable variable. Previous versions of
[ ] 88996    ** SQLite used to check if the root-page flags were sane at this point
[ ] 88997    ** and report database corruption if they were not, but this check has
[ ] 88998    ** since moved into the btree layer.  */
[ ] 88999    pCur->isTable = pOp->p4type!=P4_KEYINFO;
[ ] 89000
[ ] 89001  open_cursor_set_hints:
[ ] 89002    assert( OPFLAG_BULKCSR==BTREE_BULKLOAD );
[ ] 89003    assert( OPFLAG_SEEKEQ==BTREE_SEEK_EQ );
[ ] 89004    testcase( pOp->p5 & OPFLAG_BULKCSR );
[ ] 89005    testcase( pOp->p2 & OPFLAG_SEEKEQ );
[ ] 89006    sqlite3BtreeCursorHintFlags(pCur->uc.pCursor,
[ ] 89007                                 (pOp->p5 & (OPFLAG_BULKCSR|OPFLAG_SEEKEQ)));
[ ] 89008    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 89009    break;
[ ] 89010  }
[ ] 89011
[ ] 89012  /* Opcode: OpenDup P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 89013  **
[ ] 89014  ** Open a new cursor P1 that points to the same ephemeral table as
[ ] 89015  ** cursor P2.  The P2 cursor must have been opened by a prior OP_OpenEphemeral
[ ] 89016  ** opcode.  Only ephemeral cursors may be duplicated.
[ ] 89017  **
[ ] 89018  ** Duplicate ephemeral cursors are used for self-joins of materialized views.
[ ] 89019  */
[ ] 89020  case OP_OpenDup: {
[ ] 89021    VdbeCursor *pOrig;    /* The original cursor to be duplicated */
[ ] 89022    VdbeCursor *pCx;      /* The new cursor */
[ ] 89023
[ ] 89024    pOrig = p->apCsr[pOp->p2];
[ ] 89025    assert( pOrig );
[ ] 89026    assert( pOrig->pBtx!=0 );  /* Only ephemeral cursors can be duplicated */
[ ] 89027
[ ] 89028    pCx = allocateCursor(p, pOp->p1, pOrig->nField, -1, CURTYPE_BTREE);
[ ] 89029    if( pCx==0 ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 89030    pCx->nullRow = 1;
[ ] 89031    pCx->isEphemeral = 1;
[ ] 89032    pCx->pKeyInfo = pOrig->pKeyInfo;
[ ] 89033    pCx->isTable = pOrig->isTable;
[ ] 89034    pCx->pgnoRoot = pOrig->pgnoRoot;
[ ] 89035    pCx->isOrdered = pOrig->isOrdered;
[ ] 89036    rc = sqlite3BtreeCursor(pOrig->pBtx, pCx->pgnoRoot, BTREE_WRCSR,
[ ] 89037                            pCx->pKeyInfo, pCx->uc.pCursor);
[ ] 89038    /* The sqlite3BtreeCursor() routine can only fail for the first cursor
[ ] 89039    ** opened for a database.  Since there is already an open cursor when this
[ ] 89040    ** opcode is run, the sqlite3BtreeCursor() cannot fail */
[ ] 89041    assert( rc==SQLITE_OK );
[ ] 89042    break;
[ ] 89043  }
[ ] 89044
[ ] 89045
[ ] 89046  /* Opcode: OpenEphemeral P1 P2 * P4 P5
[ ] 89047  ** Synopsis: nColumn=P2
[ ] 89048  **
[ ] 89049  ** Open a new cursor P1 to a transient table.
[ ] 89050  ** The cursor is always opened read/write even if
[ ] 89051  ** the main database is read-only.  The ephemeral
[ ] 89052  ** table is deleted automatically when the cursor is closed.
[ ] 89053  **
[ ] 89054  ** If the cursor P1 is already opened on an ephemeral table, the table
[ ] 89055  ** is cleared (all content is erased).
[ ] 89056  **
[ ] 89057  ** P2 is the number of columns in the ephemeral table.
[ ] 89058  ** The cursor points to a BTree table if P4==0 and to a BTree index
[ ] 89059  ** if P4 is not 0.  If P4 is not NULL, it points to a KeyInfo structure
[ ] 89060  ** that defines the format of keys in the index.
[ ] 89061  **
[ ] 89062  ** The P5 parameter can be a mask of the BTREE_* flags defined
[ ] 89063  ** in btree.h.  These flags control aspects of the operation of
[ ] 89064  ** the btree.  The BTREE_OMIT_JOURNAL and BTREE_SINGLE flags are
[ ] 89065  ** added automatically.
[ ] 89066  */
[ ] 89067  /* Opcode: OpenAutoindex P1 P2 * P4 *
[ ] 89068  ** Synopsis: nColumn=P2
[ ] 89069  **
[ ] 89070  ** This opcode works the same as OP_OpenEphemeral.  It has a
[ ] 89071  ** different name to distinguish its use.  Tables created using
[ ] 89072  ** by this opcode will be used for automatically created transient
[ ] 89073  ** indices in joins.
[ ] 89074  */
[ ] 89075  case OP_OpenAutoindex:
[ ] 89076  case OP_OpenEphemeral: {
[ ] 89077    VdbeCursor *pCx;
[ ] 89078    KeyInfo *pKeyInfo;
[ ] 89079
[ ] 89080    static const int vfsFlags =
[ ] 89081        SQLITE_OPEN_READWRITE |
[ ] 89082        SQLITE_OPEN_CREATE |
[ ] 89083        SQLITE_OPEN_EXCLUSIVE |
[ ] 89084        SQLITE_OPEN_DELETEONCLOSE |
[ ] 89085        SQLITE_OPEN_TRANSIENT_DB;
[ ] 89086    assert( pOp->p1>=0 );
[ ] 89087    assert( pOp->p2>=0 );
[ ] 89088    pCx = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 89089    if( pCx && pCx->pBtx ){
[ ] 89090      /* If the ephermeral table is already open, erase all existing content
[ ] 89091      ** so that the table is empty again, rather than creating a new table. */
[ ] 89092      assert( pCx->isEphemeral );
[ ] 89093      pCx->seqCount = 0;
[ ] 89094      pCx->cacheStatus = CACHE_STALE;
[ ] 89095      rc = sqlite3BtreeClearTable(pCx->pBtx, pCx->pgnoRoot, 0);
[ ] 89096    }else{
[ ] 89097      pCx = allocateCursor(p, pOp->p1, pOp->p2, -1, CURTYPE_BTREE);
[ ] 89098      if( pCx==0 ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 89099      pCx->isEphemeral = 1;
[ ] 89100      rc = sqlite3BtreeOpen(db->pVfs, 0, db, &pCx->pBtx,
[ ] 89101                            BTREE_OMIT_JOURNAL | BTREE_SINGLE | pOp->p5,
[ ] 89102                            vfsFlags);
[ ] 89103      if( rc==SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 89104        rc = sqlite3BtreeBeginTrans(pCx->pBtx, 1, 0);
[ ] 89105      }
[ ] 89106      if( rc==SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 89107        /* If a transient index is required, create it by calling
[ ] 89108        ** sqlite3BtreeCreateTable() with the BTREE_BLOBKEY flag before
[ ] 89109        ** opening it. If a transient table is required, just use the
[ ] 89110        ** automatically created table with root-page 1 (an BLOB_INTKEY table).
[ ] 89111        */
[ ] 89112        if( (pCx->pKeyInfo = pKeyInfo = pOp->p4.pKeyInfo)!=0 ){
[ ] 89113          assert( pOp->p4type==P4_KEYINFO );
[ ] 89114          rc = sqlite3BtreeCreateTable(pCx->pBtx, (int*)&pCx->pgnoRoot,
[ ] 89115                                       BTREE_BLOBKEY | pOp->p5);
[ ] 89116          if( rc==SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 89117            assert( pCx->pgnoRoot==SCHEMA_ROOT+1 );
[ ] 89118            assert( pKeyInfo->db==db );
[ ] 89119            assert( pKeyInfo->enc==ENC(db) );
[ ] 89120            rc = sqlite3BtreeCursor(pCx->pBtx, pCx->pgnoRoot, BTREE_WRCSR,
[ ] 89121                                    pKeyInfo, pCx->uc.pCursor);
[ ] 89122          }
[ ] 89123          pCx->isTable = 0;
[ ] 89124        }else{
[ ] 89125          pCx->pgnoRoot = SCHEMA_ROOT;
[ ] 89126          rc = sqlite3BtreeCursor(pCx->pBtx, SCHEMA_ROOT, BTREE_WRCSR,
[ ] 89127                                  0, pCx->uc.pCursor);
[ ] 89128          pCx->isTable = 1;
[ ] 89129        }
[ ] 89130      }
[ ] 89131      pCx->isOrdered = (pOp->p5!=BTREE_UNORDERED);
[ ] 89132    }
[ ] 89133    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 89134    pCx->nullRow = 1;
[ ] 89135    break;
[ ] 89136  }
[ ] 89137
[ ] 89138  /* Opcode: SorterOpen P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 89139  **
[ ] 89140  ** This opcode works like OP_OpenEphemeral except that it opens
[ ] 89141  ** a transient index that is specifically designed to sort large
[ ] 89142  ** tables using an external merge-sort algorithm.
[ ] 89143  **
[ ] 89144  ** If argument P3 is non-zero, then it indicates that the sorter may
[ ] 89145  ** assume that a stable sort considering the first P3 fields of each
[ ] 89146  ** key is sufficient to produce the required results.
[ ] 89147  */
[ ] 89148  case OP_SorterOpen: {
[ ] 89149    VdbeCursor *pCx;
[ ] 89150
[ ] 89151    assert( pOp->p1>=0 );
[ ] 89152    assert( pOp->p2>=0 );
[ ] 89153    pCx = allocateCursor(p, pOp->p1, pOp->p2, -1, CURTYPE_SORTER);
[ ] 89154    if( pCx==0 ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 89155    pCx->pKeyInfo = pOp->p4.pKeyInfo;
[ ] 89156    assert( pCx->pKeyInfo->db==db );
[ ] 89157    assert( pCx->pKeyInfo->enc==ENC(db) );
[ ] 89158    rc = sqlite3VdbeSorterInit(db, pOp->p3, pCx);
[ ] 89159    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 89160    break;
[ ] 89161  }
[ ] 89162
[ ] 89163  /* Opcode: SequenceTest P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 89164  ** Synopsis: if( cursor[P1].ctr++ ) pc = P2
[ ] 89165  **
[ ] 89166  ** P1 is a sorter cursor. If the sequence counter is currently zero, jump
[ ] 89167  ** to P2. Regardless of whether or not the jump is taken, increment the
[ ] 89168  ** the sequence value.
[ ] 89169  */
[ ] 89170  case OP_SequenceTest: {
[ ] 89171    VdbeCursor *pC;
[ ] 89172    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<p->nCursor );
[ ] 89173    pC = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 89174    assert( isSorter(pC) );
[ ] 89175    if( (pC->seqCount++)==0 ){
[ ] 89176      goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 89177    }
[ ] 89178    break;
[ ] 89179  }
[ ] 89180
[ ] 89181  /* Opcode: OpenPseudo P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 89182  ** Synopsis: P3 columns in r[P2]
[ ] 89183  **
[ ] 89184  ** Open a new cursor that points to a fake table that contains a single
[ ] 89185  ** row of data.  The content of that one row is the content of memory
[ ] 89186  ** register P2.  In other words, cursor P1 becomes an alias for the
[ ] 89187  ** MEM_Blob content contained in register P2.
[ ] 89188  **
[ ] 89189  ** A pseudo-table created by this opcode is used to hold a single
[ ] 89190  ** row output from the sorter so that the row can be decomposed into
[ ] 89191  ** individual columns using the OP_Column opcode.  The OP_Column opcode
[ ] 89192  ** is the only cursor opcode that works with a pseudo-table.
[ ] 89193  **
[ ] 89194  ** P3 is the number of fields in the records that will be stored by
[ ] 89195  ** the pseudo-table.
[ ] 89196  */
[ ] 89197  case OP_OpenPseudo: {
[ ] 89198    VdbeCursor *pCx;
[ ] 89199
[ ] 89200    assert( pOp->p1>=0 );
[ ] 89201    assert( pOp->p3>=0 );
[ ] 89202    pCx = allocateCursor(p, pOp->p1, pOp->p3, -1, CURTYPE_PSEUDO);
[ ] 89203    if( pCx==0 ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 89204    pCx->nullRow = 1;
[ ] 89205    pCx->seekResult = pOp->p2;
[ ] 89206    pCx->isTable = 1;
[ ] 89207    /* Give this pseudo-cursor a fake BtCursor pointer so that pCx
[ ] 89208    ** can be safely passed to sqlite3VdbeCursorMoveto().  This avoids a test
[ ] 89209    ** for pCx->eCurType==CURTYPE_BTREE inside of sqlite3VdbeCursorMoveto()
[ ] 89210    ** which is a performance optimization */
[ ] 89211    pCx->uc.pCursor = sqlite3BtreeFakeValidCursor();
[ ] 89212    assert( pOp->p5==0 );
[ ] 89213    break;
[ ] 89214  }
[ ] 89215
[ ] 89216  /* Opcode: Close P1 * * * *
[ ] 89217  **
[ ] 89218  ** Close a cursor previously opened as P1.  If P1 is not
[ ] 89219  ** currently open, this instruction is a no-op.
[ ] 89220  */
[ ] 89221  case OP_Close: {
[ ] 89222    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<p->nCursor );
[ ] 89223    sqlite3VdbeFreeCursor(p, p->apCsr[pOp->p1]);
[ ] 89224    p->apCsr[pOp->p1] = 0;
[ ] 89225    break;
[ ] 89226  }
[ ] 89227
[ ] 89228  #ifdef SQLITE_ENABLE_COLUMN_USED_MASK
[ ] 89229  /* Opcode: ColumnsUsed P1 * * P4 *
[ ] 89230  **
[ ] 89231  ** This opcode (which only exists if SQLite was compiled with
[ ] 89232  ** SQLITE_ENABLE_COLUMN_USED_MASK) identifies which columns of the
[ ] 89233  ** table or index for cursor P1 are used.  P4 is a 64-bit integer
[ ] 89234  ** (P4_INT64) in which the first 63 bits are one for each of the
[ ] 89235  ** first 63 columns of the table or index that are actually used
[ ] 89236  ** by the cursor.  The high-order bit is set if any column after
[ ] 89237  ** the 64th is used.
[ ] 89238  */
[ ] 89239  case OP_ColumnsUsed: {
[ ] 89240    VdbeCursor *pC;
[ ] 89241    pC = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 89242    assert( pC->eCurType==CURTYPE_BTREE );
[ ] 89243    pC->maskUsed = *(u64*)pOp->p4.pI64;
[ ] 89244    break;
[ ] 89245  }
[ ] 89246  #endif
[ ] 89247
[ ] 89248  /* Opcode: SeekGE P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 89249  ** Synopsis: key=r[P3@P4]
[ ] 89250  **
[ ] 89251  ** If cursor P1 refers to an SQL table (B-Tree that uses integer keys),
[ ] 89252  ** use the value in register P3 as the key.  If cursor P1 refers
[ ] 89253  ** to an SQL index, then P3 is the first in an array of P4 registers
[ ] 89254  ** that are used as an unpacked index key.
[ ] 89255  **
[ ] 89256  ** Reposition cursor P1 so that  it points to the smallest entry that
[ ] 89257  ** is greater than or equal to the key value. If there are no records
[ ] 89258  ** greater than or equal to the key and P2 is not zero, then jump to P2.
[ ] 89259  **
[ ] 89260  ** If the cursor P1 was opened using the OPFLAG_SEEKEQ flag, then this
[ ] 89261  ** opcode will either land on a record that exactly matches the key, or
[ ] 89262  ** else it will cause a jump to P2.  When the cursor is OPFLAG_SEEKEQ,
[ ] 89263  ** this opcode must be followed by an IdxLE opcode with the same arguments.
[ ] 89264  ** The IdxGT opcode will be skipped if this opcode succeeds, but the
[ ] 89265  ** IdxGT opcode will be used on subsequent loop iterations.  The
[ ] 89266  ** OPFLAG_SEEKEQ flags is a hint to the btree layer to say that this
[ ] 89267  ** is an equality search.
[ ] 89268  **
[ ] 89269  ** This opcode leaves the cursor configured to move in forward order,
[ ] 89270  ** from the beginning toward the end.  In other words, the cursor is
[ ] 89271  ** configured to use Next, not Prev.
[ ] 89272  **
[ ] 89273  ** See also: Found, NotFound, SeekLt, SeekGt, SeekLe
[ ] 89274  */
[ ] 89275  /* Opcode: SeekGT P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 89276  ** Synopsis: key=r[P3@P4]
[ ] 89277  **
[ ] 89278  ** If cursor P1 refers to an SQL table (B-Tree that uses integer keys),
[ ] 89279  ** use the value in register P3 as a key. If cursor P1 refers
[ ] 89280  ** to an SQL index, then P3 is the first in an array of P4 registers
[ ] 89281  ** that are used as an unpacked index key.
[ ] 89282  **
[ ] 89283  ** Reposition cursor P1 so that it points to the smallest entry that
[ ] 89284  ** is greater than the key value. If there are no records greater than
[ ] 89285  ** the key and P2 is not zero, then jump to P2.
[ ] 89286  **
[ ] 89287  ** This opcode leaves the cursor configured to move in forward order,
[ ] 89288  ** from the beginning toward the end.  In other words, the cursor is
[ ] 89289  ** configured to use Next, not Prev.
[ ] 89290  **
[ ] 89291  ** See also: Found, NotFound, SeekLt, SeekGe, SeekLe
[ ] 89292  */
[ ] 89293  /* Opcode: SeekLT P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 89294  ** Synopsis: key=r[P3@P4]
[ ] 89295  **
[ ] 89296  ** If cursor P1 refers to an SQL table (B-Tree that uses integer keys),
[ ] 89297  ** use the value in register P3 as a key. If cursor P1 refers
[ ] 89298  ** to an SQL index, then P3 is the first in an array of P4 registers
[ ] 89299  ** that are used as an unpacked index key.
[ ] 89300  **
[ ] 89301  ** Reposition cursor P1 so that  it points to the largest entry that
[ ] 89302  ** is less than the key value. If there are no records less than
[ ] 89303  ** the key and P2 is not zero, then jump to P2.
[ ] 89304  **
[ ] 89305  ** This opcode leaves the cursor configured to move in reverse order,
[ ] 89306  ** from the end toward the beginning.  In other words, the cursor is
[ ] 89307  ** configured to use Prev, not Next.
[ ] 89308  **
[ ] 89309  ** See also: Found, NotFound, SeekGt, SeekGe, SeekLe
[ ] 89310  */
[ ] 89311  /* Opcode: SeekLE P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 89312  ** Synopsis: key=r[P3@P4]
[ ] 89313  **
[ ] 89314  ** If cursor P1 refers to an SQL table (B-Tree that uses integer keys),
[ ] 89315  ** use the value in register P3 as a key. If cursor P1 refers
[ ] 89316  ** to an SQL index, then P3 is the first in an array of P4 registers
[ ] 89317  ** that are used as an unpacked index key.
[ ] 89318  **
[ ] 89319  ** Reposition cursor P1 so that it points to the largest entry that
[ ] 89320  ** is less than or equal to the key value. If there are no records
[ ] 89321  ** less than or equal to the key and P2 is not zero, then jump to P2.
[ ] 89322  **
[ ] 89323  ** This opcode leaves the cursor configured to move in reverse order,
[ ] 89324  ** from the end toward the beginning.  In other words, the cursor is
[ ] 89325  ** configured to use Prev, not Next.
[ ] 89326  **
[ ] 89327  ** If the cursor P1 was opened using the OPFLAG_SEEKEQ flag, then this
[ ] 89328  ** opcode will either land on a record that exactly matches the key, or
[ ] 89329  ** else it will cause a jump to P2.  When the cursor is OPFLAG_SEEKEQ,
[ ] 89330  ** this opcode must be followed by an IdxLE opcode with the same arguments.
[ ] 89331  ** The IdxGE opcode will be skipped if this opcode succeeds, but the
[ ] 89332  ** IdxGE opcode will be used on subsequent loop iterations.  The
[ ] 89333  ** OPFLAG_SEEKEQ flags is a hint to the btree layer to say that this
[ ] 89334  ** is an equality search.
[ ] 89335  **
[ ] 89336  ** See also: Found, NotFound, SeekGt, SeekGe, SeekLt
[ ] 89337  */
[ ] 89338  case OP_SeekLT:         /* jump, in3, group */
[ ] 89339  case OP_SeekLE:         /* jump, in3, group */
[ ] 89340  case OP_SeekGE:         /* jump, in3, group */
[ ] 89341  case OP_SeekGT: {       /* jump, in3, group */
[ ] 89342    int res;           /* Comparison result */
[ ] 89343    int oc;            /* Opcode */
[ ] 89344    VdbeCursor *pC;    /* The cursor to seek */
[ ] 89345    UnpackedRecord r;  /* The key to seek for */
[ ] 89346    int nField;        /* Number of columns or fields in the key */
[ ] 89347    i64 iKey;          /* The rowid we are to seek to */
[ ] 89348    int eqOnly;        /* Only interested in == results */
[ ] 89349
[ ] 89350    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<p->nCursor );
[ ] 89351    assert( pOp->p2!=0 );
[ ] 89352    pC = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 89353    assert( pC!=0 );
[ ] 89354    assert( pC->eCurType==CURTYPE_BTREE );
[ ] 89355    assert( OP_SeekLE == OP_SeekLT+1 );
[ ] 89356    assert( OP_SeekGE == OP_SeekLT+2 );
[ ] 89357    assert( OP_SeekGT == OP_SeekLT+3 );
[ ] 89358    assert( pC->isOrdered );
[ ] 89359    assert( pC->uc.pCursor!=0 );
[ ] 89360    oc = pOp->opcode;
[ ] 89361    eqOnly = 0;
[ ] 89362    pC->nullRow = 0;
[ ] 89363  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 89364    pC->seekOp = pOp->opcode;
[ ] 89365  #endif
[ ] 89366
[ ] 89367    pC->deferredMoveto = 0;
[ ] 89368    pC->cacheStatus = CACHE_STALE;
[ ] 89369    if( pC->isTable ){
[ ] 89370      u16 flags3, newType;
[ ] 89371      /* The OPFLAG_SEEKEQ/BTREE_SEEK_EQ flag is only set on index cursors */
[ ] 89372      assert( sqlite3BtreeCursorHasHint(pC->uc.pCursor, BTREE_SEEK_EQ)==0
[ ] 89373                || CORRUPT_DB );
[ ] 89374
[ ] 89375      /* The input value in P3 might be of any type: integer, real, string,
[ ] 89376      ** blob, or NULL.  But it needs to be an integer before we can do
[ ] 89377      ** the seek, so convert it. */
[ ] 89378      pIn3 = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 89379      flags3 = pIn3->flags;
[ ] 89380      if( (flags3 & (MEM_Int|MEM_Real|MEM_IntReal|MEM_Str))==MEM_Str ){
[ ] 89381        applyNumericAffinity(pIn3, 0);
[ ] 89382      }
[ ] 89383      iKey = sqlite3VdbeIntValue(pIn3); /* Get the integer key value */
[ ] 89384      newType = pIn3->flags; /* Record the type after applying numeric affinity */
[ ] 89385      pIn3->flags = flags3;  /* But convert the type back to its original */
[ ] 89386
[ ] 89387      /* If the P3 value could not be converted into an integer without
[ ] 89388      ** loss of information, then special processing is required... */
[ ] 89389      if( (newType & (MEM_Int|MEM_IntReal))==0 ){
[ ] 89390        if( (newType & MEM_Real)==0 ){
[ ] 89391          if( (newType & MEM_Null) || oc>=OP_SeekGE ){
[ ] 89392            VdbeBranchTaken(1,2);
[ ] 89393            goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 89394          }else{
[ ] 89395            rc = sqlite3BtreeLast(pC->uc.pCursor, &res);
[ ] 89396            if( rc!=SQLITE_OK ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 89397            goto seek_not_found;
[ ] 89398          }
[ ] 89399        }else
[ ] 89400
[ ] 89401        /* If the approximation iKey is larger than the actual real search
[ ] 89402        ** term, substitute >= for > and < for <=. e.g. if the search term
[ ] 89403        ** is 4.9 and the integer approximation 5:
[ ] 89404        **
[ ] 89405        **        (x >  4.9)    ->     (x >= 5)
[ ] 89406        **        (x <= 4.9)    ->     (x <  5)
[ ] 89407        */
[ ] 89408        if( pIn3->u.r<(double)iKey ){
[ ] 89409          assert( OP_SeekGE==(OP_SeekGT-1) );
[ ] 89410          assert( OP_SeekLT==(OP_SeekLE-1) );
[ ] 89411          assert( (OP_SeekLE & 0x0001)==(OP_SeekGT & 0x0001) );
[ ] 89412          if( (oc & 0x0001)==(OP_SeekGT & 0x0001) ) oc--;
[ ] 89413        }
[ ] 89414
[ ] 89415        /* If the approximation iKey is smaller than the actual real search
[ ] 89416        ** term, substitute <= for < and > for >=.  */
[ ] 89417        else if( pIn3->u.r>(double)iKey ){
[ ] 89418          assert( OP_SeekLE==(OP_SeekLT+1) );
[ ] 89419          assert( OP_SeekGT==(OP_SeekGE+1) );
[ ] 89420          assert( (OP_SeekLT & 0x0001)==(OP_SeekGE & 0x0001) );
[ ] 89421          if( (oc & 0x0001)==(OP_SeekLT & 0x0001) ) oc++;
[ ] 89422        }
[ ] 89423      }
[ ] 89424      rc = sqlite3BtreeMovetoUnpacked(pC->uc.pCursor, 0, (u64)iKey, 0, &res);
[ ] 89425      pC->movetoTarget = iKey;  /* Used by OP_Delete */
[ ] 89426      if( rc!=SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 89427        goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 89428      }
[ ] 89429    }else{
[ ] 89430      /* For a cursor with the OPFLAG_SEEKEQ/BTREE_SEEK_EQ hint, only the
[ ] 89431      ** OP_SeekGE and OP_SeekLE opcodes are allowed, and these must be
[ ] 89432      ** immediately followed by an OP_IdxGT or OP_IdxLT opcode, respectively,
[ ] 89433      ** with the same key.
[ ] 89434      */
[ ] 89435      if( sqlite3BtreeCursorHasHint(pC->uc.pCursor, BTREE_SEEK_EQ) ){
[ ] 89436        eqOnly = 1;
[ ] 89437        assert( pOp->opcode==OP_SeekGE || pOp->opcode==OP_SeekLE );
[ ] 89438        assert( pOp[1].opcode==OP_IdxLT || pOp[1].opcode==OP_IdxGT );
[ ] 89439        assert( pOp->opcode==OP_SeekGE || pOp[1].opcode==OP_IdxLT );
[ ] 89440        assert( pOp->opcode==OP_SeekLE || pOp[1].opcode==OP_IdxGT );
[ ] 89441        assert( pOp[1].p1==pOp[0].p1 );
[ ] 89442        assert( pOp[1].p2==pOp[0].p2 );
[ ] 89443        assert( pOp[1].p3==pOp[0].p3 );
[ ] 89444        assert( pOp[1].p4.i==pOp[0].p4.i );
[ ] 89445      }
[ ] 89446
[ ] 89447      nField = pOp->p4.i;
[ ] 89448      assert( pOp->p4type==P4_INT32 );
[ ] 89449      assert( nField>0 );
[ ] 89450      r.pKeyInfo = pC->pKeyInfo;
[ ] 89451      r.nField = (u16)nField;
[ ] 89452
[ ] 89453      /* The next line of code computes as follows, only faster:
[ ] 89454      **   if( oc==OP_SeekGT || oc==OP_SeekLE ){
[ ] 89455      **     r.default_rc = -1;
[ ] 89456      **   }else{
[ ] 89457      **     r.default_rc = +1;
[ ] 89458      **   }
[ ] 89459      */
[ ] 89460      r.default_rc = ((1 & (oc - OP_SeekLT)) ? -1 : +1);
[ ] 89461      assert( oc!=OP_SeekGT || r.default_rc==-1 );
[ ] 89462      assert( oc!=OP_SeekLE || r.default_rc==-1 );
[ ] 89463      assert( oc!=OP_SeekGE || r.default_rc==+1 );
[ ] 89464      assert( oc!=OP_SeekLT || r.default_rc==+1 );
[ ] 89465
[ ] 89466      r.aMem = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 89467  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 89468      { int i; for(i=0; i<r.nField; i++) assert( memIsValid(&r.aMem[i]) ); }
[ ] 89469  #endif
