[ ] 91276         "SELECT*FROM\"%w\".%s WHERE %s ORDER BY rowid",
[ ] 91277         db->aDb[iDb].zDbSName, zSchema, pOp->p4.z);
[ ] 91278      if( zSql==0 ){
[ ] 91279        rc = SQLITE_NOMEM_BKPT;
[ ] 91280      }else{
[ ] 91281        assert( db->init.busy==0 );
[ ] 91282        db->init.busy = 1;
[ ] 91283        initData.rc = SQLITE_OK;
[ ] 91284        initData.nInitRow = 0;
[ ] 91285        assert( !db->mallocFailed );
[ ] 91286        rc = sqlite3_exec(db, zSql, sqlite3InitCallback, &initData, 0);
[ ] 91287        if( rc==SQLITE_OK ) rc = initData.rc;
[ ] 91288        if( rc==SQLITE_OK && initData.nInitRow==0 ){
[ ] 91289          /* The OP_ParseSchema opcode with a non-NULL P4 argument should parse
[ ] 91290          ** at least one SQL statement. Any less than that indicates that
[ ] 91291          ** the sqlite_schema table is corrupt. */
[ ] 91292          rc = SQLITE_CORRUPT_BKPT;
[ ] 91293        }
[ ] 91294        sqlite3DbFreeNN(db, zSql);
[ ] 91295        db->init.busy = 0;
[ ] 91296      }
[ ] 91297    }
[ ] 91298    if( rc ){
[ ] 91299      sqlite3ResetAllSchemasOfConnection(db);
[ ] 91300      if( rc==SQLITE_NOMEM ){
[ ] 91301        goto no_mem;
[ ] 91302      }
[ ] 91303      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 91304    }
[ ] 91305    break;
[ ] 91306  }
[ ] 91307
[ ] 91308  #if !defined(SQLITE_OMIT_ANALYZE)
[ ] 91309  /* Opcode: LoadAnalysis P1 * * * *
[ ] 91310  **
[ ] 91311  ** Read the sqlite_stat1 table for database P1 and load the content
[ ] 91312  ** of that table into the internal index hash table.  This will cause
[ ] 91313  ** the analysis to be used when preparing all subsequent queries.
[ ] 91314  */
[ ] 91315  case OP_LoadAnalysis: {
[ ] 91316    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<db->nDb );
[ ] 91317    rc = sqlite3AnalysisLoad(db, pOp->p1);
[ ] 91318    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 91319    break;
[ ] 91320  }
[ ] 91321  #endif /* !defined(SQLITE_OMIT_ANALYZE) */
[ ] 91322
[ ] 91323  /* Opcode: DropTable P1 * * P4 *
[ ] 91324  **
[ ] 91325  ** Remove the internal (in-memory) data structures that describe
[ ] 91326  ** the table named P4 in database P1.  This is called after a table
[ ] 91327  ** is dropped from disk (using the Destroy opcode) in order to keep
[ ] 91328  ** the internal representation of the
[ ] 91329  ** schema consistent with what is on disk.
[ ] 91330  */
[ ] 91331  case OP_DropTable: {
[ ] 91332    sqlite3VdbeIncrWriteCounter(p, 0);
[ ] 91333    sqlite3UnlinkAndDeleteTable(db, pOp->p1, pOp->p4.z);
[ ] 91334    break;
[ ] 91335  }
[ ] 91336
[ ] 91337  /* Opcode: DropIndex P1 * * P4 *
[ ] 91338  **
[ ] 91339  ** Remove the internal (in-memory) data structures that describe
[ ] 91340  ** the index named P4 in database P1.  This is called after an index
[ ] 91341  ** is dropped from disk (using the Destroy opcode)
[ ] 91342  ** in order to keep the internal representation of the
[ ] 91343  ** schema consistent with what is on disk.
[ ] 91344  */
[ ] 91345  case OP_DropIndex: {
[ ] 91346    sqlite3VdbeIncrWriteCounter(p, 0);
[ ] 91347    sqlite3UnlinkAndDeleteIndex(db, pOp->p1, pOp->p4.z);
[ ] 91348    break;
[ ] 91349  }
[ ] 91350
[ ] 91351  /* Opcode: DropTrigger P1 * * P4 *
[ ] 91352  **
[ ] 91353  ** Remove the internal (in-memory) data structures that describe
[ ] 91354  ** the trigger named P4 in database P1.  This is called after a trigger
[ ] 91355  ** is dropped from disk (using the Destroy opcode) in order to keep
[ ] 91356  ** the internal representation of the
[ ] 91357  ** schema consistent with what is on disk.
[ ] 91358  */
[ ] 91359  case OP_DropTrigger: {
[ ] 91360    sqlite3VdbeIncrWriteCounter(p, 0);
[ ] 91361    sqlite3UnlinkAndDeleteTrigger(db, pOp->p1, pOp->p4.z);
[ ] 91362    break;
[ ] 91363  }
[ ] 91364
[ ] 91365
[ ] 91366  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_INTEGRITY_CHECK
[ ] 91367  /* Opcode: IntegrityCk P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 91368  **
[ ] 91369  ** Do an analysis of the currently open database.  Store in
[ ] 91370  ** register P1 the text of an error message describing any problems.
[ ] 91371  ** If no problems are found, store a NULL in register P1.
[ ] 91372  **
[ ] 91373  ** The register P3 contains one less than the maximum number of allowed errors.
[ ] 91374  ** At most reg(P3) errors will be reported.
[ ] 91375  ** In other words, the analysis stops as soon as reg(P1) errors are
[ ] 91376  ** seen.  Reg(P1) is updated with the number of errors remaining.
[ ] 91377  **
[ ] 91378  ** The root page numbers of all tables in the database are integers
[ ] 91379  ** stored in P4_INTARRAY argument.
[ ] 91380  **
[ ] 91381  ** If P5 is not zero, the check is done on the auxiliary database
[ ] 91382  ** file, not the main database file.
[ ] 91383  **
[ ] 91384  ** This opcode is used to implement the integrity_check pragma.
[ ] 91385  */
[ ] 91386  case OP_IntegrityCk: {
[ ] 91387    int nRoot;      /* Number of tables to check.  (Number of root pages.) */
[ ] 91388    int *aRoot;     /* Array of rootpage numbers for tables to be checked */
[ ] 91389    int nErr;       /* Number of errors reported */
[ ] 91390    char *z;        /* Text of the error report */
[ ] 91391    Mem *pnErr;     /* Register keeping track of errors remaining */
[ ] 91392
[ ] 91393    assert( p->bIsReader );
[ ] 91394    nRoot = pOp->p2;
[ ] 91395    aRoot = pOp->p4.ai;
[ ] 91396    assert( nRoot>0 );
[ ] 91397    assert( aRoot[0]==nRoot );
[ ] 91398    assert( pOp->p3>0 && pOp->p3<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 91399    pnErr = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 91400    assert( (pnErr->flags & MEM_Int)!=0 );
[ ] 91401    assert( (pnErr->flags & (MEM_Str|MEM_Blob))==0 );
[ ] 91402    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91403    assert( pOp->p5<db->nDb );
[ ] 91404    assert( DbMaskTest(p->btreeMask, pOp->p5) );
[ ] 91405    z = sqlite3BtreeIntegrityCheck(db, db->aDb[pOp->p5].pBt, &aRoot[1], nRoot,
[ ] 91406                                   (int)pnErr->u.i+1, &nErr);
[ ] 91407    sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pIn1);
[ ] 91408    if( nErr==0 ){
[ ] 91409      assert( z==0 );
[ ] 91410    }else if( z==0 ){
[ ] 91411      goto no_mem;
[ ] 91412    }else{
[ ] 91413      pnErr->u.i -= nErr-1;
[ ] 91414      sqlite3VdbeMemSetStr(pIn1, z, -1, SQLITE_UTF8, sqlite3_free);
[ ] 91415    }
[ ] 91416    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pIn1);
[ ] 91417    sqlite3VdbeChangeEncoding(pIn1, encoding);
[ ] 91418    goto check_for_interrupt;
[ ] 91419  }
[ ] 91420  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_INTEGRITY_CHECK */
[ ] 91421
[ ] 91422  /* Opcode: RowSetAdd P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 91423  ** Synopsis: rowset(P1)=r[P2]
[ ] 91424  **
[ ] 91425  ** Insert the integer value held by register P2 into a RowSet object
[ ] 91426  ** held in register P1.
[ ] 91427  **
[ ] 91428  ** An assertion fails if P2 is not an integer.
[ ] 91429  */
[ ] 91430  case OP_RowSetAdd: {       /* in1, in2 */
[ ] 91431    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91432    pIn2 = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 91433    assert( (pIn2->flags & MEM_Int)!=0 );
[ ] 91434    if( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Blob)==0 ){
[ ] 91435      if( sqlite3VdbeMemSetRowSet(pIn1) ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 91436    }
[ ] 91437    assert( sqlite3VdbeMemIsRowSet(pIn1) );
[ ] 91438    sqlite3RowSetInsert((RowSet*)pIn1->z, pIn2->u.i);
[ ] 91439    break;
[ ] 91440  }
[ ] 91441
[ ] 91442  /* Opcode: RowSetRead P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 91443  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=rowset(P1)
[ ] 91444  **
[ ] 91445  ** Extract the smallest value from the RowSet object in P1
[ ] 91446  ** and put that value into register P3.
[ ] 91447  ** Or, if RowSet object P1 is initially empty, leave P3
[ ] 91448  ** unchanged and jump to instruction P2.
[ ] 91449  */
[ ] 91450  case OP_RowSetRead: {       /* jump, in1, out3 */
[ ] 91451    i64 val;
[ ] 91452
[ ] 91453    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91454    assert( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Blob)==0 || sqlite3VdbeMemIsRowSet(pIn1) );
[ ] 91455    if( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Blob)==0
[ ] 91456     || sqlite3RowSetNext((RowSet*)pIn1->z, &val)==0
[ ] 91457    ){
[ ] 91458      /* The boolean index is empty */
[ ] 91459      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pIn1);
[ ] 91460      VdbeBranchTaken(1,2);
[ ] 91461      goto jump_to_p2_and_check_for_interrupt;
[ ] 91462    }else{
[ ] 91463      /* A value was pulled from the index */
[ ] 91464      VdbeBranchTaken(0,2);
[ ] 91465      sqlite3VdbeMemSetInt64(&aMem[pOp->p3], val);
[ ] 91466    }
[ ] 91467    goto check_for_interrupt;
[ ] 91468  }
[ ] 91469
[ ] 91470  /* Opcode: RowSetTest P1 P2 P3 P4
[ ] 91471  ** Synopsis: if r[P3] in rowset(P1) goto P2
[ ] 91472  **
[ ] 91473  ** Register P3 is assumed to hold a 64-bit integer value. If register P1
[ ] 91474  ** contains a RowSet object and that RowSet object contains
[ ] 91475  ** the value held in P3, jump to register P2. Otherwise, insert the
[ ] 91476  ** integer in P3 into the RowSet and continue on to the
[ ] 91477  ** next opcode.
[ ] 91478  **
[ ] 91479  ** The RowSet object is optimized for the case where sets of integers
[ ] 91480  ** are inserted in distinct phases, which each set contains no duplicates.
[ ] 91481  ** Each set is identified by a unique P4 value. The first set
[ ] 91482  ** must have P4==0, the final set must have P4==-1, and for all other sets
[ ] 91483  ** must have P4>0.
[ ] 91484  **
[ ] 91485  ** This allows optimizations: (a) when P4==0 there is no need to test
[ ] 91486  ** the RowSet object for P3, as it is guaranteed not to contain it,
[ ] 91487  ** (b) when P4==-1 there is no need to insert the value, as it will
[ ] 91488  ** never be tested for, and (c) when a value that is part of set X is
[ ] 91489  ** inserted, there is no need to search to see if the same value was
[ ] 91490  ** previously inserted as part of set X (only if it was previously
[ ] 91491  ** inserted as part of some other set).
[ ] 91492  */
[ ] 91493  case OP_RowSetTest: {                     /* jump, in1, in3 */
[ ] 91494    int iSet;
[ ] 91495    int exists;
[ ] 91496
[ ] 91497    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91498    pIn3 = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 91499    iSet = pOp->p4.i;
[ ] 91500    assert( pIn3->flags&MEM_Int );
[ ] 91501
[ ] 91502    /* If there is anything other than a rowset object in memory cell P1,
[ ] 91503    ** delete it now and initialize P1 with an empty rowset
[ ] 91504    */
[ ] 91505    if( (pIn1->flags & MEM_Blob)==0 ){
[ ] 91506      if( sqlite3VdbeMemSetRowSet(pIn1) ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 91507    }
[ ] 91508    assert( sqlite3VdbeMemIsRowSet(pIn1) );
[ ] 91509    assert( pOp->p4type==P4_INT32 );
[ ] 91510    assert( iSet==-1 || iSet>=0 );
[ ] 91511    if( iSet ){
[ ] 91512      exists = sqlite3RowSetTest((RowSet*)pIn1->z, iSet, pIn3->u.i);
[ ] 91513      VdbeBranchTaken(exists!=0,2);
[ ] 91514      if( exists ) goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 91515    }
[ ] 91516    if( iSet>=0 ){
[ ] 91517      sqlite3RowSetInsert((RowSet*)pIn1->z, pIn3->u.i);
[ ] 91518    }
[ ] 91519    break;
[ ] 91520  }
[ ] 91521
[ ] 91522
[ ] 91523  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_TRIGGER
[ ] 91524
[ ] 91525  /* Opcode: Program P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 91526  **
[ ] 91527  ** Execute the trigger program passed as P4 (type P4_SUBPROGRAM).
[ ] 91528  **
[ ] 91529  ** P1 contains the address of the memory cell that contains the first memory
[ ] 91530  ** cell in an array of values used as arguments to the sub-program. P2
[ ] 91531  ** contains the address to jump to if the sub-program throws an IGNORE
[ ] 91532  ** exception using the RAISE() function. Register P3 contains the address
[ ] 91533  ** of a memory cell in this (the parent) VM that is used to allocate the
[ ] 91534  ** memory required by the sub-vdbe at runtime.
[ ] 91535  **
[ ] 91536  ** P4 is a pointer to the VM containing the trigger program.
[ ] 91537  **
[ ] 91538  ** If P5 is non-zero, then recursive program invocation is enabled.
[ ] 91539  */
[ ] 91540  case OP_Program: {        /* jump */
[ ] 91541    int nMem;               /* Number of memory registers for sub-program */
[ ] 91542    int nByte;              /* Bytes of runtime space required for sub-program */
[ ] 91543    Mem *pRt;               /* Register to allocate runtime space */
[ ] 91544    Mem *pMem;              /* Used to iterate through memory cells */
[ ] 91545    Mem *pEnd;              /* Last memory cell in new array */
[ ] 91546    VdbeFrame *pFrame;      /* New vdbe frame to execute in */
[ ] 91547    SubProgram *pProgram;   /* Sub-program to execute */
[ ] 91548    void *t;                /* Token identifying trigger */
[ ] 91549
[ ] 91550    pProgram = pOp->p4.pProgram;
[ ] 91551    pRt = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 91552    assert( pProgram->nOp>0 );
[ ] 91553
[ ] 91554    /* If the p5 flag is clear, then recursive invocation of triggers is
[ ] 91555    ** disabled for backwards compatibility (p5 is set if this sub-program
[ ] 91556    ** is really a trigger, not a foreign key action, and the flag set
[ ] 91557    ** and cleared by the "PRAGMA recursive_triggers" command is clear).
[ ] 91558    **
[ ] 91559    ** It is recursive invocation of triggers, at the SQL level, that is
[ ] 91560    ** disabled. In some cases a single trigger may generate more than one
[ ] 91561    ** SubProgram (if the trigger may be executed with more than one different
[ ] 91562    ** ON CONFLICT algorithm). SubProgram structures associated with a
[ ] 91563    ** single trigger all have the same value for the SubProgram.token
[ ] 91564    ** variable.  */
[ ] 91565    if( pOp->p5 ){
[ ] 91566      t = pProgram->token;
[ ] 91567      for(pFrame=p->pFrame; pFrame && pFrame->token!=t; pFrame=pFrame->pParent);
[ ] 91568      if( pFrame ) break;
[ ] 91569    }
[ ] 91570
[ ] 91571    if( p->nFrame>=db->aLimit[SQLITE_LIMIT_TRIGGER_DEPTH] ){
[ ] 91572      rc = SQLITE_ERROR;
[ ] 91573      sqlite3VdbeError(p, "too many levels of trigger recursion");
[ ] 91574      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 91575    }
[ ] 91576
[ ] 91577    /* Register pRt is used to store the memory required to save the state
[ ] 91578    ** of the current program, and the memory required at runtime to execute
[ ] 91579    ** the trigger program. If this trigger has been fired before, then pRt
[ ] 91580    ** is already allocated. Otherwise, it must be initialized.  */
[ ] 91581    if( (pRt->flags&MEM_Blob)==0 ){
[ ] 91582      /* SubProgram.nMem is set to the number of memory cells used by the
[ ] 91583      ** program stored in SubProgram.aOp. As well as these, one memory
[ ] 91584      ** cell is required for each cursor used by the program. Set local
[ ] 91585      ** variable nMem (and later, VdbeFrame.nChildMem) to this value.
[ ] 91586      */
[ ] 91587      nMem = pProgram->nMem + pProgram->nCsr;
[ ] 91588      assert( nMem>0 );
[ ] 91589      if( pProgram->nCsr==0 ) nMem++;
[ ] 91590      nByte = ROUND8(sizeof(VdbeFrame))
[ ] 91591                + nMem * sizeof(Mem)
[ ] 91592                + pProgram->nCsr * sizeof(VdbeCursor*)
[ ] 91593                + (pProgram->nOp + 7)/8;
[ ] 91594      pFrame = sqlite3DbMallocZero(db, nByte);
[ ] 91595      if( !pFrame ){
[ ] 91596        goto no_mem;
[ ] 91597      }
[ ] 91598      sqlite3VdbeMemRelease(pRt);
[ ] 91599      pRt->flags = MEM_Blob|MEM_Dyn;
[ ] 91600      pRt->z = (char*)pFrame;
[ ] 91601      pRt->n = nByte;
[ ] 91602      pRt->xDel = sqlite3VdbeFrameMemDel;
[ ] 91603
[ ] 91604      pFrame->v = p;
[ ] 91605      pFrame->nChildMem = nMem;
[ ] 91606      pFrame->nChildCsr = pProgram->nCsr;
[ ] 91607      pFrame->pc = (int)(pOp - aOp);
[ ] 91608      pFrame->aMem = p->aMem;
[ ] 91609      pFrame->nMem = p->nMem;
[ ] 91610      pFrame->apCsr = p->apCsr;
[ ] 91611      pFrame->nCursor = p->nCursor;
[ ] 91612      pFrame->aOp = p->aOp;
[ ] 91613      pFrame->nOp = p->nOp;
[ ] 91614      pFrame->token = pProgram->token;
[ ] 91615  #ifdef SQLITE_ENABLE_STMT_SCANSTATUS
[ ] 91616      pFrame->anExec = p->anExec;
[ ] 91617  #endif
[ ] 91618  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 91619      pFrame->iFrameMagic = SQLITE_FRAME_MAGIC;
[ ] 91620  #endif
[ ] 91621
[ ] 91622      pEnd = &VdbeFrameMem(pFrame)[pFrame->nChildMem];
[ ] 91623      for(pMem=VdbeFrameMem(pFrame); pMem!=pEnd; pMem++){
[ ] 91624        pMem->flags = MEM_Undefined;
[ ] 91625        pMem->db = db;
[ ] 91626      }
[ ] 91627    }else{
[ ] 91628      pFrame = (VdbeFrame*)pRt->z;
[ ] 91629      assert( pRt->xDel==sqlite3VdbeFrameMemDel );
[ ] 91630      assert( pProgram->nMem+pProgram->nCsr==pFrame->nChildMem
[ ] 91631          || (pProgram->nCsr==0 && pProgram->nMem+1==pFrame->nChildMem) );
[ ] 91632      assert( pProgram->nCsr==pFrame->nChildCsr );
[ ] 91633      assert( (int)(pOp - aOp)==pFrame->pc );
[ ] 91634    }
[ ] 91635
[ ] 91636    p->nFrame++;
[ ] 91637    pFrame->pParent = p->pFrame;
[ ] 91638    pFrame->lastRowid = db->lastRowid;
[ ] 91639    pFrame->nChange = p->nChange;
[ ] 91640    pFrame->nDbChange = p->db->nChange;
[ ] 91641    assert( pFrame->pAuxData==0 );
[ ] 91642    pFrame->pAuxData = p->pAuxData;
[ ] 91643    p->pAuxData = 0;
[ ] 91644    p->nChange = 0;
[ ] 91645    p->pFrame = pFrame;
[ ] 91646    p->aMem = aMem = VdbeFrameMem(pFrame);
[ ] 91647    p->nMem = pFrame->nChildMem;
[ ] 91648    p->nCursor = (u16)pFrame->nChildCsr;
[ ] 91649    p->apCsr = (VdbeCursor **)&aMem[p->nMem];
[ ] 91650    pFrame->aOnce = (u8*)&p->apCsr[pProgram->nCsr];
[ ] 91651    memset(pFrame->aOnce, 0, (pProgram->nOp + 7)/8);
[ ] 91652    p->aOp = aOp = pProgram->aOp;
[ ] 91653    p->nOp = pProgram->nOp;
[ ] 91654  #ifdef SQLITE_ENABLE_STMT_SCANSTATUS
[ ] 91655    p->anExec = 0;
[ ] 91656  #endif
[ ] 91657  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 91658    /* Verify that second and subsequent executions of the same trigger do not
[ ] 91659    ** try to reuse register values from the first use. */
[ ] 91660    {
[ ] 91661      int i;
[ ] 91662      for(i=0; i<p->nMem; i++){
[ ] 91663        aMem[i].pScopyFrom = 0;  /* Prevent false-positive AboutToChange() errs */
[ ] 91664        MemSetTypeFlag(&aMem[i], MEM_Undefined); /* Fault if this reg is reused */
[ ] 91665      }
[ ] 91666    }
[ ] 91667  #endif
[ ] 91668    pOp = &aOp[-1];
[ ] 91669    goto check_for_interrupt;
[ ] 91670  }
[ ] 91671
[ ] 91672  /* Opcode: Param P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 91673  **
[ ] 91674  ** This opcode is only ever present in sub-programs called via the
[ ] 91675  ** OP_Program instruction. Copy a value currently stored in a memory
[ ] 91676  ** cell of the calling (parent) frame to cell P2 in the current frames
[ ] 91677  ** address space. This is used by trigger programs to access the new.*
[ ] 91678  ** and old.* values.
[ ] 91679  **
[ ] 91680  ** The address of the cell in the parent frame is determined by adding
[ ] 91681  ** the value of the P1 argument to the value of the P1 argument to the
[ ] 91682  ** calling OP_Program instruction.
[ ] 91683  */
[ ] 91684  case OP_Param: {           /* out2 */
[ ] 91685    VdbeFrame *pFrame;
[ ] 91686    Mem *pIn;
[ ] 91687    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 91688    pFrame = p->pFrame;
[ ] 91689    pIn = &pFrame->aMem[pOp->p1 + pFrame->aOp[pFrame->pc].p1];
[ ] 91690    sqlite3VdbeMemShallowCopy(pOut, pIn, MEM_Ephem);
[ ] 91691    break;
[ ] 91692  }
[ ] 91693
[ ] 91694  #endif /* #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_TRIGGER */
[ ] 91695
[ ] 91696  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_FOREIGN_KEY
[ ] 91697  /* Opcode: FkCounter P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 91698  ** Synopsis: fkctr[P1]+=P2
[ ] 91699  **
[ ] 91700  ** Increment a "constraint counter" by P2 (P2 may be negative or positive).
[ ] 91701  ** If P1 is non-zero, the database constraint counter is incremented
[ ] 91702  ** (deferred foreign key constraints). Otherwise, if P1 is zero, the
[ ] 91703  ** statement counter is incremented (immediate foreign key constraints).
[ ] 91704  */
[ ] 91705  case OP_FkCounter: {
[ ] 91706    if( db->flags & SQLITE_DeferFKs ){
[ ] 91707      db->nDeferredImmCons += pOp->p2;
[ ] 91708    }else if( pOp->p1 ){
[ ] 91709      db->nDeferredCons += pOp->p2;
[ ] 91710    }else{
[ ] 91711      p->nFkConstraint += pOp->p2;
[ ] 91712    }
[ ] 91713    break;
[ ] 91714  }
[ ] 91715
[ ] 91716  /* Opcode: FkIfZero P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 91717  ** Synopsis: if fkctr[P1]==0 goto P2
[ ] 91718  **
[ ] 91719  ** This opcode tests if a foreign key constraint-counter is currently zero.
[ ] 91720  ** If so, jump to instruction P2. Otherwise, fall through to the next
[ ] 91721  ** instruction.
[ ] 91722  **
[ ] 91723  ** If P1 is non-zero, then the jump is taken if the database constraint-counter
[ ] 91724  ** is zero (the one that counts deferred constraint violations). If P1 is
[ ] 91725  ** zero, the jump is taken if the statement constraint-counter is zero
[ ] 91726  ** (immediate foreign key constraint violations).
[ ] 91727  */
[ ] 91728  case OP_FkIfZero: {         /* jump */
[ ] 91729    if( pOp->p1 ){
[ ] 91730      VdbeBranchTaken(db->nDeferredCons==0 && db->nDeferredImmCons==0, 2);
[ ] 91731      if( db->nDeferredCons==0 && db->nDeferredImmCons==0 ) goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 91732    }else{
[ ] 91733      VdbeBranchTaken(p->nFkConstraint==0 && db->nDeferredImmCons==0, 2);
[ ] 91734      if( p->nFkConstraint==0 && db->nDeferredImmCons==0 ) goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 91735    }
[ ] 91736    break;
[ ] 91737  }
[ ] 91738  #endif /* #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_FOREIGN_KEY */
[ ] 91739
[ ] 91740  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_AUTOINCREMENT
[ ] 91741  /* Opcode: MemMax P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 91742  ** Synopsis: r[P1]=max(r[P1],r[P2])
[ ] 91743  **
[ ] 91744  ** P1 is a register in the root frame of this VM (the root frame is
[ ] 91745  ** different from the current frame if this instruction is being executed
[ ] 91746  ** within a sub-program). Set the value of register P1 to the maximum of
[ ] 91747  ** its current value and the value in register P2.
[ ] 91748  **
[ ] 91749  ** This instruction throws an error if the memory cell is not initially
[ ] 91750  ** an integer.
[ ] 91751  */
[ ] 91752  case OP_MemMax: {        /* in2 */
[ ] 91753    VdbeFrame *pFrame;
[ ] 91754    if( p->pFrame ){
[ ] 91755      for(pFrame=p->pFrame; pFrame->pParent; pFrame=pFrame->pParent);
[ ] 91756      pIn1 = &pFrame->aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91757    }else{
[ ] 91758      pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91759    }
[ ] 91760    assert( memIsValid(pIn1) );
[ ] 91761    sqlite3VdbeMemIntegerify(pIn1);
[ ] 91762    pIn2 = &aMem[pOp->p2];
[ ] 91763    sqlite3VdbeMemIntegerify(pIn2);
[ ] 91764    if( pIn1->u.i<pIn2->u.i){
[ ] 91765      pIn1->u.i = pIn2->u.i;
[ ] 91766    }
[ ] 91767    break;
[ ] 91768  }
[ ] 91769  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_AUTOINCREMENT */
[ ] 91770
[ ] 91771  /* Opcode: IfPos P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 91772  ** Synopsis: if r[P1]>0 then r[P1]-=P3, goto P2
[ ] 91773  **
[ ] 91774  ** Register P1 must contain an integer.
[ ] 91775  ** If the value of register P1 is 1 or greater, subtract P3 from the
[ ] 91776  ** value in P1 and jump to P2.
[ ] 91777  **
[ ] 91778  ** If the initial value of register P1 is less than 1, then the
[ ] 91779  ** value is unchanged and control passes through to the next instruction.
[ ] 91780  */
[ ] 91781  case OP_IfPos: {        /* jump, in1 */
[ ] 91782    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91783    assert( pIn1->flags&MEM_Int );
[ ] 91784    VdbeBranchTaken( pIn1->u.i>0, 2);
[ ] 91785    if( pIn1->u.i>0 ){
[ ] 91786      pIn1->u.i -= pOp->p3;
[ ] 91787      goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 91788    }
[ ] 91789    break;
[ ] 91790  }
[ ] 91791
[ ] 91792  /* Opcode: OffsetLimit P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 91793  ** Synopsis: if r[P1]>0 then r[P2]=r[P1]+max(0,r[P3]) else r[P2]=(-1)
[ ] 91794  **
[ ] 91795  ** This opcode performs a commonly used computation associated with
[ ] 91796  ** LIMIT and OFFSET process.  r[P1] holds the limit counter.  r[P3]
[ ] 91797  ** holds the offset counter.  The opcode computes the combined value
[ ] 91798  ** of the LIMIT and OFFSET and stores that value in r[P2].  The r[P2]
[ ] 91799  ** value computed is the total number of rows that will need to be
[ ] 91800  ** visited in order to complete the query.
[ ] 91801  **
[ ] 91802  ** If r[P3] is zero or negative, that means there is no OFFSET
[ ] 91803  ** and r[P2] is set to be the value of the LIMIT, r[P1].
[ ] 91804  **
[ ] 91805  ** if r[P1] is zero or negative, that means there is no LIMIT
[ ] 91806  ** and r[P2] is set to -1.
[ ] 91807  **
[ ] 91808  ** Otherwise, r[P2] is set to the sum of r[P1] and r[P3].
[ ] 91809  */
[ ] 91810  case OP_OffsetLimit: {    /* in1, out2, in3 */
[ ] 91811    i64 x;
[ ] 91812    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91813    pIn3 = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 91814    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 91815    assert( pIn1->flags & MEM_Int );
[ ] 91816    assert( pIn3->flags & MEM_Int );
[ ] 91817    x = pIn1->u.i;
[ ] 91818    if( x<=0 || sqlite3AddInt64(&x, pIn3->u.i>0?pIn3->u.i:0) ){
[ ] 91819      /* If the LIMIT is less than or equal to zero, loop forever.  This
[ ] 91820      ** is documented.  But also, if the LIMIT+OFFSET exceeds 2^63 then
[ ] 91821      ** also loop forever.  This is undocumented.  In fact, one could argue
[ ] 91822      ** that the loop should terminate.  But assuming 1 billion iterations
[ ] 91823      ** per second (far exceeding the capabilities of any current hardware)
[ ] 91824      ** it would take nearly 300 years to actually reach the limit.  So
[ ] 91825      ** looping forever is a reasonable approximation. */
[ ] 91826      pOut->u.i = -1;
[ ] 91827    }else{
[ ] 91828      pOut->u.i = x;
[ ] 91829    }
[ ] 91830    break;
[ ] 91831  }
[ ] 91832
[ ] 91833  /* Opcode: IfNotZero P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 91834  ** Synopsis: if r[P1]!=0 then r[P1]--, goto P2
[ ] 91835  **
[ ] 91836  ** Register P1 must contain an integer.  If the content of register P1 is
[ ] 91837  ** initially greater than zero, then decrement the value in register P1.
[ ] 91838  ** If it is non-zero (negative or positive) and then also jump to P2.
[ ] 91839  ** If register P1 is initially zero, leave it unchanged and fall through.
[ ] 91840  */
[ ] 91841  case OP_IfNotZero: {        /* jump, in1 */
[ ] 91842    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91843    assert( pIn1->flags&MEM_Int );
[ ] 91844    VdbeBranchTaken(pIn1->u.i<0, 2);
[ ] 91845    if( pIn1->u.i ){
[ ] 91846       if( pIn1->u.i>0 ) pIn1->u.i--;
[ ] 91847       goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 91848    }
[ ] 91849    break;
[ ] 91850  }
[ ] 91851
[ ] 91852  /* Opcode: DecrJumpZero P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 91853  ** Synopsis: if (--r[P1])==0 goto P2
[ ] 91854  **
[ ] 91855  ** Register P1 must hold an integer.  Decrement the value in P1
[ ] 91856  ** and jump to P2 if the new value is exactly zero.
[ ] 91857  */
[ ] 91858  case OP_DecrJumpZero: {      /* jump, in1 */
[ ] 91859    pIn1 = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 91860    assert( pIn1->flags&MEM_Int );
[ ] 91861    if( pIn1->u.i>SMALLEST_INT64 ) pIn1->u.i--;
[ ] 91862    VdbeBranchTaken(pIn1->u.i==0, 2);
[ ] 91863    if( pIn1->u.i==0 ) goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 91864    break;
[ ] 91865  }
[ ] 91866
[ ] 91867
[ ] 91868  /* Opcode: AggStep * P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 91869  ** Synopsis: accum=r[P3] step(r[P2@P5])
[ ] 91870  **
[ ] 91871  ** Execute the xStep function for an aggregate.
[ ] 91872  ** The function has P5 arguments.  P4 is a pointer to the
[ ] 91873  ** FuncDef structure that specifies the function.  Register P3 is the
[ ] 91874  ** accumulator.
[ ] 91875  **
[ ] 91876  ** The P5 arguments are taken from register P2 and its
[ ] 91877  ** successors.
[ ] 91878  */
[ ] 91879  /* Opcode: AggInverse * P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 91880  ** Synopsis: accum=r[P3] inverse(r[P2@P5])
[ ] 91881  **
[ ] 91882  ** Execute the xInverse function for an aggregate.
[ ] 91883  ** The function has P5 arguments.  P4 is a pointer to the
[ ] 91884  ** FuncDef structure that specifies the function.  Register P3 is the
[ ] 91885  ** accumulator.
[ ] 91886  **
[ ] 91887  ** The P5 arguments are taken from register P2 and its
[ ] 91888  ** successors.
[ ] 91889  */
[ ] 91890  /* Opcode: AggStep1 P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 91891  ** Synopsis: accum=r[P3] step(r[P2@P5])
[ ] 91892  **
[ ] 91893  ** Execute the xStep (if P1==0) or xInverse (if P1!=0) function for an
[ ] 91894  ** aggregate.  The function has P5 arguments.  P4 is a pointer to the
[ ] 91895  ** FuncDef structure that specifies the function.  Register P3 is the
[ ] 91896  ** accumulator.
[ ] 91897  **
[ ] 91898  ** The P5 arguments are taken from register P2 and its
[ ] 91899  ** successors.
[ ] 91900  **
[ ] 91901  ** This opcode is initially coded as OP_AggStep0.  On first evaluation,
[ ] 91902  ** the FuncDef stored in P4 is converted into an sqlite3_context and
[ ] 91903  ** the opcode is changed.  In this way, the initialization of the
[ ] 91904  ** sqlite3_context only happens once, instead of on each call to the
[ ] 91905  ** step function.
[ ] 91906  */
[ ] 91907  case OP_AggInverse:
[ ] 91908  case OP_AggStep: {
[ ] 91909    int n;
[ ] 91910    sqlite3_context *pCtx;
[ ] 91911
[ ] 91912    assert( pOp->p4type==P4_FUNCDEF );
[ ] 91913    n = pOp->p5;
[ ] 91914    assert( pOp->p3>0 && pOp->p3<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 91915    assert( n==0 || (pOp->p2>0 && pOp->p2+n<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)+1) );
[ ] 91916    assert( pOp->p3<pOp->p2 || pOp->p3>=pOp->p2+n );
[ ] 91917    pCtx = sqlite3DbMallocRawNN(db, n*sizeof(sqlite3_value*) +
[ ] 91918                 (sizeof(pCtx[0]) + sizeof(Mem) - sizeof(sqlite3_value*)));
[ ] 91919    if( pCtx==0 ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 91920    pCtx->pMem = 0;
[ ] 91921    pCtx->pOut = (Mem*)&(pCtx->argv[n]);
[ ] 91922    sqlite3VdbeMemInit(pCtx->pOut, db, MEM_Null);
[ ] 91923    pCtx->pFunc = pOp->p4.pFunc;
[ ] 91924    pCtx->iOp = (int)(pOp - aOp);
[ ] 91925    pCtx->pVdbe = p;
[ ] 91926    pCtx->skipFlag = 0;
[ ] 91927    pCtx->isError = 0;
[ ] 91928    pCtx->argc = n;
[ ] 91929    pOp->p4type = P4_FUNCCTX;
[ ] 91930    pOp->p4.pCtx = pCtx;
[ ] 91931
[ ] 91932    /* OP_AggInverse must have P1==1 and OP_AggStep must have P1==0 */
[ ] 91933    assert( pOp->p1==(pOp->opcode==OP_AggInverse) );
[ ] 91934
[ ] 91935    pOp->opcode = OP_AggStep1;
[ ] 91936    /* Fall through into OP_AggStep */
[ ] 91937  }
[ ] 91938  case OP_AggStep1: {
[ ] 91939    int i;
[ ] 91940    sqlite3_context *pCtx;
[ ] 91941    Mem *pMem;
[ ] 91942
[ ] 91943    assert( pOp->p4type==P4_FUNCCTX );
[ ] 91944    pCtx = pOp->p4.pCtx;
[ ] 91945    pMem = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 91946
[ ] 91947  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 91948    if( pOp->p1 ){
[ ] 91949      /* This is an OP_AggInverse call.  Verify that xStep has always
[ ] 91950      ** been called at least once prior to any xInverse call. */
[ ] 91951      assert( pMem->uTemp==0x1122e0e3 );
[ ] 91952    }else{
[ ] 91953      /* This is an OP_AggStep call.  Mark it as such. */
[ ] 91954      pMem->uTemp = 0x1122e0e3;
[ ] 91955    }
[ ] 91956  #endif
[ ] 91957
[ ] 91958    /* If this function is inside of a trigger, the register array in aMem[]
[ ] 91959    ** might change from one evaluation to the next.  The next block of code
[ ] 91960    ** checks to see if the register array has changed, and if so it
[ ] 91961    ** reinitializes the relavant parts of the sqlite3_context object */
[ ] 91962    if( pCtx->pMem != pMem ){
[ ] 91963      pCtx->pMem = pMem;
[ ] 91964      for(i=pCtx->argc-1; i>=0; i--) pCtx->argv[i] = &aMem[pOp->p2+i];
[ ] 91965    }
[ ] 91966
[ ] 91967  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 91968    for(i=0; i<pCtx->argc; i++){
[ ] 91969      assert( memIsValid(pCtx->argv[i]) );
[ ] 91970      REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p2+i, pCtx->argv[i]);
[ ] 91971    }
[ ] 91972  #endif
[ ] 91973
[ ] 91974    pMem->n++;
[ ] 91975    assert( pCtx->pOut->flags==MEM_Null );
[ ] 91976    assert( pCtx->isError==0 );
[ ] 91977    assert( pCtx->skipFlag==0 );
[ ] 91978  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_WINDOWFUNC
[ ] 91979    if( pOp->p1 ){
[ ] 91980      (pCtx->pFunc->xInverse)(pCtx,pCtx->argc,pCtx->argv);
[ ] 91981    }else
[ ] 91982  #endif
[ ] 91983    (pCtx->pFunc->xSFunc)(pCtx,pCtx->argc,pCtx->argv); /* IMP: R-24505-23230 */
[ ] 91984
[ ] 91985    if( pCtx->isError ){
[ ] 91986      if( pCtx->isError>0 ){
[ ] 91987        sqlite3VdbeError(p, "%s", sqlite3_value_text(pCtx->pOut));
[ ] 91988        rc = pCtx->isError;
[ ] 91989      }
[ ] 91990      if( pCtx->skipFlag ){
[ ] 91991        assert( pOp[-1].opcode==OP_CollSeq );
[ ] 91992        i = pOp[-1].p1;
[ ] 91993        if( i ) sqlite3VdbeMemSetInt64(&aMem[i], 1);
[ ] 91994        pCtx->skipFlag = 0;
[ ] 91995      }
[ ] 91996      sqlite3VdbeMemRelease(pCtx->pOut);
[ ] 91997      pCtx->pOut->flags = MEM_Null;
[ ] 91998      pCtx->isError = 0;
[ ] 91999      if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92000    }
[ ] 92001    assert( pCtx->pOut->flags==MEM_Null );
[ ] 92002    assert( pCtx->skipFlag==0 );
[ ] 92003    break;
[ ] 92004  }
[ ] 92005
[ ] 92006  /* Opcode: AggFinal P1 P2 * P4 *
[ ] 92007  ** Synopsis: accum=r[P1] N=P2
[ ] 92008  **
[ ] 92009  ** P1 is the memory location that is the accumulator for an aggregate
[ ] 92010  ** or window function.  Execute the finalizer function
[ ] 92011  ** for an aggregate and store the result in P1.
[ ] 92012  **
[ ] 92013  ** P2 is the number of arguments that the step function takes and
[ ] 92014  ** P4 is a pointer to the FuncDef for this function.  The P2
[ ] 92015  ** argument is not used by this opcode.  It is only there to disambiguate
[ ] 92016  ** functions that can take varying numbers of arguments.  The
[ ] 92017  ** P4 argument is only needed for the case where
[ ] 92018  ** the step function was not previously called.
[ ] 92019  */
[ ] 92020  /* Opcode: AggValue * P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 92021  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=value N=P2
[ ] 92022  **
[ ] 92023  ** Invoke the xValue() function and store the result in register P3.
[ ] 92024  **
[ ] 92025  ** P2 is the number of arguments that the step function takes and
[ ] 92026  ** P4 is a pointer to the FuncDef for this function.  The P2
[ ] 92027  ** argument is not used by this opcode.  It is only there to disambiguate
[ ] 92028  ** functions that can take varying numbers of arguments.  The
[ ] 92029  ** P4 argument is only needed for the case where
[ ] 92030  ** the step function was not previously called.
[ ] 92031  */
[ ] 92032  case OP_AggValue:
[ ] 92033  case OP_AggFinal: {
[ ] 92034    Mem *pMem;
[ ] 92035    assert( pOp->p1>0 && pOp->p1<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 92036    assert( pOp->p3==0 || pOp->opcode==OP_AggValue );
[ ] 92037    pMem = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 92038    assert( (pMem->flags & ~(MEM_Null|MEM_Agg))==0 );
[ ] 92039  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_WINDOWFUNC
[ ] 92040    if( pOp->p3 ){
[ ] 92041      memAboutToChange(p, &aMem[pOp->p3]);
[ ] 92042      rc = sqlite3VdbeMemAggValue(pMem, &aMem[pOp->p3], pOp->p4.pFunc);
[ ] 92043      pMem = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 92044    }else
[ ] 92045  #endif
[ ] 92046    {
[ ] 92047      rc = sqlite3VdbeMemFinalize(pMem, pOp->p4.pFunc);
[ ] 92048    }
[ ] 92049
[ ] 92050    if( rc ){
[ ] 92051      sqlite3VdbeError(p, "%s", sqlite3_value_text(pMem));
[ ] 92052      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92053    }
[ ] 92054    sqlite3VdbeChangeEncoding(pMem, encoding);
[ ] 92055    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pMem);
[ ] 92056    if( sqlite3VdbeMemTooBig(pMem) ){
[ ] 92057      goto too_big;
[ ] 92058    }
[ ] 92059    break;
[ ] 92060  }
[ ] 92061
[ ] 92062  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_WAL
[ ] 92063  /* Opcode: Checkpoint P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 92064  **
[ ] 92065  ** Checkpoint database P1. This is a no-op if P1 is not currently in
[ ] 92066  ** WAL mode. Parameter P2 is one of SQLITE_CHECKPOINT_PASSIVE, FULL,
[ ] 92067  ** RESTART, or TRUNCATE.  Write 1 or 0 into mem[P3] if the checkpoint returns
[ ] 92068  ** SQLITE_BUSY or not, respectively.  Write the number of pages in the
[ ] 92069  ** WAL after the checkpoint into mem[P3+1] and the number of pages
[ ] 92070  ** in the WAL that have been checkpointed after the checkpoint
[ ] 92071  ** completes into mem[P3+2].  However on an error, mem[P3+1] and
[ ] 92072  ** mem[P3+2] are initialized to -1.
[ ] 92073  */
[ ] 92074  case OP_Checkpoint: {
[ ] 92075    int i;                          /* Loop counter */
[ ] 92076    int aRes[3];                    /* Results */
[ ] 92077    Mem *pMem;                      /* Write results here */
[ ] 92078
[ ] 92079    assert( p->readOnly==0 );
[ ] 92080    aRes[0] = 0;
[ ] 92081    aRes[1] = aRes[2] = -1;
[ ] 92082    assert( pOp->p2==SQLITE_CHECKPOINT_PASSIVE
[ ] 92083         || pOp->p2==SQLITE_CHECKPOINT_FULL
[ ] 92084         || pOp->p2==SQLITE_CHECKPOINT_RESTART
[ ] 92085         || pOp->p2==SQLITE_CHECKPOINT_TRUNCATE
[ ] 92086    );
[ ] 92087    rc = sqlite3Checkpoint(db, pOp->p1, pOp->p2, &aRes[1], &aRes[2]);
[ ] 92088    if( rc ){
[ ] 92089      if( rc!=SQLITE_BUSY ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92090      rc = SQLITE_OK;
[ ] 92091      aRes[0] = 1;
[ ] 92092    }
[ ] 92093    for(i=0, pMem = &aMem[pOp->p3]; i<3; i++, pMem++){
[ ] 92094      sqlite3VdbeMemSetInt64(pMem, (i64)aRes[i]);
[ ] 92095    }
[ ] 92096    break;
[ ] 92097  };
[ ] 92098  #endif
[ ] 92099
[ ] 92100  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_PRAGMA
[ ] 92101  /* Opcode: JournalMode P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 92102  **
[ ] 92103  ** Change the journal mode of database P1 to P3. P3 must be one of the
[ ] 92104  ** PAGER_JOURNALMODE_XXX values. If changing between the various rollback
[ ] 92105  ** modes (delete, truncate, persist, off and memory), this is a simple
[ ] 92106  ** operation. No IO is required.
[ ] 92107  **
[ ] 92108  ** If changing into or out of WAL mode the procedure is more complicated.
[ ] 92109  **
[ ] 92110  ** Write a string containing the final journal-mode to register P2.
[ ] 92111  */
[ ] 92112  case OP_JournalMode: {    /* out2 */
[ ] 92113    Btree *pBt;                     /* Btree to change journal mode of */
[ ] 92114    Pager *pPager;                  /* Pager associated with pBt */
[ ] 92115    int eNew;                       /* New journal mode */
[ ] 92116    int eOld;                       /* The old journal mode */
[ ] 92117  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_WAL
[ ] 92118    const char *zFilename;          /* Name of database file for pPager */
[ ] 92119  #endif
[ ] 92120
[ ] 92121    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 92122    eNew = pOp->p3;
[ ] 92123    assert( eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_DELETE
[ ] 92124         || eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_TRUNCATE
[ ] 92125         || eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_PERSIST
[ ] 92126         || eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_OFF
[ ] 92127         || eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_MEMORY
[ ] 92128         || eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_WAL
[ ] 92129         || eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_QUERY
[ ] 92130    );
[ ] 92131    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<db->nDb );
[ ] 92132    assert( p->readOnly==0 );
[ ] 92133
[ ] 92134    pBt = db->aDb[pOp->p1].pBt;
[ ] 92135    pPager = sqlite3BtreePager(pBt);
[ ] 92136    eOld = sqlite3PagerGetJournalMode(pPager);
[ ] 92137    if( eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_QUERY ) eNew = eOld;
[ ] 92138    if( !sqlite3PagerOkToChangeJournalMode(pPager) ) eNew = eOld;
[ ] 92139
[ ] 92140  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_WAL
[ ] 92141    zFilename = sqlite3PagerFilename(pPager, 1);
[ ] 92142
[ ] 92143    /* Do not allow a transition to journal_mode=WAL for a database
[ ] 92144    ** in temporary storage or if the VFS does not support shared memory
[ ] 92145    */
[ ] 92146    if( eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_WAL
[ ] 92147     && (sqlite3Strlen30(zFilename)==0           /* Temp file */
[ ] 92148         || !sqlite3PagerWalSupported(pPager))   /* No shared-memory support */
[ ] 92149    ){
[ ] 92150      eNew = eOld;
[ ] 92151    }
[ ] 92152
[ ] 92153    if( (eNew!=eOld)
[ ] 92154     && (eOld==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_WAL || eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_WAL)
[ ] 92155    ){
[ ] 92156      if( !db->autoCommit || db->nVdbeRead>1 ){
[ ] 92157        rc = SQLITE_ERROR;
[ ] 92158        sqlite3VdbeError(p,
[ ] 92159            "cannot change %s wal mode from within a transaction",
[ ] 92160            (eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_WAL ? "into" : "out of")
[ ] 92161        );
[ ] 92162        goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92163      }else{
[ ] 92164
[ ] 92165        if( eOld==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_WAL ){
[ ] 92166          /* If leaving WAL mode, close the log file. If successful, the call
[ ] 92167          ** to PagerCloseWal() checkpoints and deletes the write-ahead-log
[ ] 92168          ** file. An EXCLUSIVE lock may still be held on the database file
[ ] 92169          ** after a successful return.
[ ] 92170          */
[ ] 92171          rc = sqlite3PagerCloseWal(pPager, db);
[ ] 92172          if( rc==SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 92173            sqlite3PagerSetJournalMode(pPager, eNew);
[ ] 92174          }
[ ] 92175        }else if( eOld==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_MEMORY ){
[ ] 92176          /* Cannot transition directly from MEMORY to WAL.  Use mode OFF
[ ] 92177          ** as an intermediate */
[ ] 92178          sqlite3PagerSetJournalMode(pPager, PAGER_JOURNALMODE_OFF);
[ ] 92179        }
[ ] 92180
[ ] 92181        /* Open a transaction on the database file. Regardless of the journal
[ ] 92182        ** mode, this transaction always uses a rollback journal.
[ ] 92183        */
[ ] 92184        assert( sqlite3BtreeIsInTrans(pBt)==0 );
[ ] 92185        if( rc==SQLITE_OK ){
[ ] 92186          rc = sqlite3BtreeSetVersion(pBt, (eNew==PAGER_JOURNALMODE_WAL ? 2 : 1));
[ ] 92187        }
[ ] 92188      }
[ ] 92189    }
[ ] 92190  #endif /* ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_WAL */
[ ] 92191
[ ] 92192    if( rc ) eNew = eOld;
[ ] 92193    eNew = sqlite3PagerSetJournalMode(pPager, eNew);
[ ] 92194
[ ] 92195    pOut->flags = MEM_Str|MEM_Static|MEM_Term;
[ ] 92196    pOut->z = (char *)sqlite3JournalModename(eNew);
[ ] 92197    pOut->n = sqlite3Strlen30(pOut->z);
[ ] 92198    pOut->enc = SQLITE_UTF8;
[ ] 92199    sqlite3VdbeChangeEncoding(pOut, encoding);
[ ] 92200    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92201    break;
[ ] 92202  };
[ ] 92203  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_PRAGMA */
[ ] 92204
[ ] 92205  #if !defined(SQLITE_OMIT_VACUUM) && !defined(SQLITE_OMIT_ATTACH)
[ ] 92206  /* Opcode: Vacuum P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 92207  **
[ ] 92208  ** Vacuum the entire database P1.  P1 is 0 for "main", and 2 or more
[ ] 92209  ** for an attached database.  The "temp" database may not be vacuumed.
[ ] 92210  **
[ ] 92211  ** If P2 is not zero, then it is a register holding a string which is
[ ] 92212  ** the file into which the result of vacuum should be written.  When
[ ] 92213  ** P2 is zero, the vacuum overwrites the original database.
[ ] 92214  */
[ ] 92215  case OP_Vacuum: {
[ ] 92216    assert( p->readOnly==0 );
[ ] 92217    rc = sqlite3RunVacuum(&p->zErrMsg, db, pOp->p1,
[ ] 92218                          pOp->p2 ? &aMem[pOp->p2] : 0);
[ ] 92219    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92220    break;
[ ] 92221  }
[ ] 92222  #endif
[ ] 92223
[ ] 92224  #if !defined(SQLITE_OMIT_AUTOVACUUM)
[ ] 92225  /* Opcode: IncrVacuum P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 92226  **
[ ] 92227  ** Perform a single step of the incremental vacuum procedure on
[ ] 92228  ** the P1 database. If the vacuum has finished, jump to instruction
[ ] 92229  ** P2. Otherwise, fall through to the next instruction.
[ ] 92230  */
[ ] 92231  case OP_IncrVacuum: {        /* jump */
[ ] 92232    Btree *pBt;
[ ] 92233
[ ] 92234    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<db->nDb );
[ ] 92235    assert( DbMaskTest(p->btreeMask, pOp->p1) );
[ ] 92236    assert( p->readOnly==0 );
[ ] 92237    pBt = db->aDb[pOp->p1].pBt;
[ ] 92238    rc = sqlite3BtreeIncrVacuum(pBt);
[ ] 92239    VdbeBranchTaken(rc==SQLITE_DONE,2);
[ ] 92240    if( rc ){
[ ] 92241      if( rc!=SQLITE_DONE ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92242      rc = SQLITE_OK;
[ ] 92243      goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 92244    }
[ ] 92245    break;
[ ] 92246  }
[ ] 92247  #endif
[ ] 92248
[ ] 92249  /* Opcode: Expire P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 92250  **
[ ] 92251  ** Cause precompiled statements to expire.  When an expired statement
[ ] 92252  ** is executed using sqlite3_step() it will either automatically
[ ] 92253  ** reprepare itself (if it was originally created using sqlite3_prepare_v2())
[ ] 92254  ** or it will fail with SQLITE_SCHEMA.
[ ] 92255  **
[ ] 92256  ** If P1 is 0, then all SQL statements become expired. If P1 is non-zero,
[ ] 92257  ** then only the currently executing statement is expired.
[ ] 92258  **
[ ] 92259  ** If P2 is 0, then SQL statements are expired immediately.  If P2 is 1,
[ ] 92260  ** then running SQL statements are allowed to continue to run to completion.
[ ] 92261  ** The P2==1 case occurs when a CREATE INDEX or similar schema change happens
[ ] 92262  ** that might help the statement run faster but which does not affect the
[ ] 92263  ** correctness of operation.
[ ] 92264  */
[ ] 92265  case OP_Expire: {
[ ] 92266    assert( pOp->p2==0 || pOp->p2==1 );
[ ] 92267    if( !pOp->p1 ){
[ ] 92268      sqlite3ExpirePreparedStatements(db, pOp->p2);
[ ] 92269    }else{
[ ] 92270      p->expired = pOp->p2+1;
[ ] 92271    }
[ ] 92272    break;
[ ] 92273  }
[ ] 92274
[ ] 92275  /* Opcode: CursorLock P1 * * * *
[ ] 92276  **
[ ] 92277  ** Lock the btree to which cursor P1 is pointing so that the btree cannot be
[ ] 92278  ** written by an other cursor.
[ ] 92279  */
[ ] 92280  case OP_CursorLock: {
[ ] 92281    VdbeCursor *pC;
[ ] 92282    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<p->nCursor );
[ ] 92283    pC = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 92284    assert( pC!=0 );
[ ] 92285    assert( pC->eCurType==CURTYPE_BTREE );
[ ] 92286    sqlite3BtreeCursorPin(pC->uc.pCursor);
[ ] 92287    break;
[ ] 92288  }
[ ] 92289
[ ] 92290  /* Opcode: CursorUnlock P1 * * * *
[ ] 92291  **
[ ] 92292  ** Unlock the btree to which cursor P1 is pointing so that it can be
[ ] 92293  ** written by other cursors.
[ ] 92294  */
[ ] 92295  case OP_CursorUnlock: {
[ ] 92296    VdbeCursor *pC;
[ ] 92297    assert( pOp->p1>=0 && pOp->p1<p->nCursor );
[ ] 92298    pC = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 92299    assert( pC!=0 );
[ ] 92300    assert( pC->eCurType==CURTYPE_BTREE );
[ ] 92301    sqlite3BtreeCursorUnpin(pC->uc.pCursor);
[ ] 92302    break;
[ ] 92303  }
[ ] 92304
[ ] 92305  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_SHARED_CACHE
[ ] 92306  /* Opcode: TableLock P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 92307  ** Synopsis: iDb=P1 root=P2 write=P3
[ ] 92308  **
[ ] 92309  ** Obtain a lock on a particular table. This instruction is only used when
[ ] 92310  ** the shared-cache feature is enabled.
[ ] 92311  **
[ ] 92312  ** P1 is the index of the database in sqlite3.aDb[] of the database
[ ] 92313  ** on which the lock is acquired.  A readlock is obtained if P3==0 or
[ ] 92314  ** a write lock if P3==1.
[ ] 92315  **
[ ] 92316  ** P2 contains the root-page of the table to lock.
[ ] 92317  **
[ ] 92318  ** P4 contains a pointer to the name of the table being locked. This is only
[ ] 92319  ** used to generate an error message if the lock cannot be obtained.
[ ] 92320  */
[ ] 92321  case OP_TableLock: {
[ ] 92322    u8 isWriteLock = (u8)pOp->p3;
[ ] 92323    if( isWriteLock || 0==(db->flags&SQLITE_ReadUncommit) ){
[ ] 92324      int p1 = pOp->p1;
[ ] 92325      assert( p1>=0 && p1<db->nDb );
[ ] 92326      assert( DbMaskTest(p->btreeMask, p1) );
[ ] 92327      assert( isWriteLock==0 || isWriteLock==1 );
[ ] 92328      rc = sqlite3BtreeLockTable(db->aDb[p1].pBt, pOp->p2, isWriteLock);
[ ] 92329      if( rc ){
[ ] 92330        if( (rc&0xFF)==SQLITE_LOCKED ){
[ ] 92331          const char *z = pOp->p4.z;
[ ] 92332          sqlite3VdbeError(p, "database table is locked: %s", z);
[ ] 92333        }
[ ] 92334        goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92335      }
[ ] 92336    }
[ ] 92337    break;
[ ] 92338  }
[ ] 92339  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_SHARED_CACHE */
[ ] 92340
[ ] 92341  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 92342  /* Opcode: VBegin * * * P4 *
[ ] 92343  **
[ ] 92344  ** P4 may be a pointer to an sqlite3_vtab structure. If so, call the
[ ] 92345  ** xBegin method for that table.
[ ] 92346  **
[ ] 92347  ** Also, whether or not P4 is set, check that this is not being called from
[ ] 92348  ** within a callback to a virtual table xSync() method. If it is, the error
[ ] 92349  ** code will be set to SQLITE_LOCKED.
[ ] 92350  */
[ ] 92351  case OP_VBegin: {
[ ] 92352    VTable *pVTab;
[ ] 92353    pVTab = pOp->p4.pVtab;
[ ] 92354    rc = sqlite3VtabBegin(db, pVTab);
[ ] 92355    if( pVTab ) sqlite3VtabImportErrmsg(p, pVTab->pVtab);
[ ] 92356    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92357    break;
[ ] 92358  }
[ ] 92359  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE */
[ ] 92360
[ ] 92361  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 92362  /* Opcode: VCreate P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 92363  **
[ ] 92364  ** P2 is a register that holds the name of a virtual table in database
[ ] 92365  ** P1. Call the xCreate method for that table.
[ ] 92366  */
[ ] 92367  case OP_VCreate: {
[ ] 92368    Mem sMem;          /* For storing the record being decoded */
[ ] 92369    const char *zTab;  /* Name of the virtual table */
[ ] 92370
[ ] 92371    memset(&sMem, 0, sizeof(sMem));
[ ] 92372    sMem.db = db;
[ ] 92373    /* Because P2 is always a static string, it is impossible for the
[ ] 92374    ** sqlite3VdbeMemCopy() to fail */
[ ] 92375    assert( (aMem[pOp->p2].flags & MEM_Str)!=0 );
[ ] 92376    assert( (aMem[pOp->p2].flags & MEM_Static)!=0 );
[ ] 92377    rc = sqlite3VdbeMemCopy(&sMem, &aMem[pOp->p2]);
[ ] 92378    assert( rc==SQLITE_OK );
[ ] 92379    zTab = (const char*)sqlite3_value_text(&sMem);
[ ] 92380    assert( zTab || db->mallocFailed );
[ ] 92381    if( zTab ){
[ ] 92382      rc = sqlite3VtabCallCreate(db, pOp->p1, zTab, &p->zErrMsg);
[ ] 92383    }
[ ] 92384    sqlite3VdbeMemRelease(&sMem);
[ ] 92385    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92386    break;
[ ] 92387  }
[ ] 92388  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE */
[ ] 92389
[ ] 92390  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 92391  /* Opcode: VDestroy P1 * * P4 *
[ ] 92392  **
[ ] 92393  ** P4 is the name of a virtual table in database P1.  Call the xDestroy method
[ ] 92394  ** of that table.
[ ] 92395  */
[ ] 92396  case OP_VDestroy: {
[ ] 92397    db->nVDestroy++;
[ ] 92398    rc = sqlite3VtabCallDestroy(db, pOp->p1, pOp->p4.z);
[ ] 92399    db->nVDestroy--;
[ ] 92400    assert( p->errorAction==OE_Abort && p->usesStmtJournal );
[ ] 92401    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92402    break;
[ ] 92403  }
[ ] 92404  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE */
[ ] 92405
[ ] 92406  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 92407  /* Opcode: VOpen P1 * * P4 *
[ ] 92408  **
[ ] 92409  ** P4 is a pointer to a virtual table object, an sqlite3_vtab structure.
[ ] 92410  ** P1 is a cursor number.  This opcode opens a cursor to the virtual
[ ] 92411  ** table and stores that cursor in P1.
[ ] 92412  */
[ ] 92413  case OP_VOpen: {
[ ] 92414    VdbeCursor *pCur;
[ ] 92415    sqlite3_vtab_cursor *pVCur;
[ ] 92416    sqlite3_vtab *pVtab;
[ ] 92417    const sqlite3_module *pModule;
[ ] 92418
[ ] 92419    assert( p->bIsReader );
[ ] 92420    pCur = 0;
[ ] 92421    pVCur = 0;
[ ] 92422    pVtab = pOp->p4.pVtab->pVtab;
[ ] 92423    if( pVtab==0 || NEVER(pVtab->pModule==0) ){
[ ] 92424      rc = SQLITE_LOCKED;
[ ] 92425      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92426    }
[ ] 92427    pModule = pVtab->pModule;
[ ] 92428    rc = pModule->xOpen(pVtab, &pVCur);
[ ] 92429    sqlite3VtabImportErrmsg(p, pVtab);
[ ] 92430    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92431
[ ] 92432    /* Initialize sqlite3_vtab_cursor base class */
[ ] 92433    pVCur->pVtab = pVtab;
[ ] 92434
[ ] 92435    /* Initialize vdbe cursor object */
[ ] 92436    pCur = allocateCursor(p, pOp->p1, 0, -1, CURTYPE_VTAB);
[ ] 92437    if( pCur ){
[ ] 92438      pCur->uc.pVCur = pVCur;
[ ] 92439      pVtab->nRef++;
[ ] 92440    }else{
[ ] 92441      assert( db->mallocFailed );
[ ] 92442      pModule->xClose(pVCur);
[ ] 92443      goto no_mem;
[ ] 92444    }
[ ] 92445    break;
[ ] 92446  }
[ ] 92447  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE */
[ ] 92448
[ ] 92449  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 92450  /* Opcode: VFilter P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 92451  ** Synopsis: iplan=r[P3] zplan='P4'
[ ] 92452  **
[ ] 92453  ** P1 is a cursor opened using VOpen.  P2 is an address to jump to if
[ ] 92454  ** the filtered result set is empty.
[ ] 92455  **
[ ] 92456  ** P4 is either NULL or a string that was generated by the xBestIndex
[ ] 92457  ** method of the module.  The interpretation of the P4 string is left
[ ] 92458  ** to the module implementation.
[ ] 92459  **
[ ] 92460  ** This opcode invokes the xFilter method on the virtual table specified
[ ] 92461  ** by P1.  The integer query plan parameter to xFilter is stored in register
[ ] 92462  ** P3. Register P3+1 stores the argc parameter to be passed to the
[ ] 92463  ** xFilter method. Registers P3+2..P3+1+argc are the argc
[ ] 92464  ** additional parameters which are passed to
[ ] 92465  ** xFilter as argv. Register P3+2 becomes argv[0] when passed to xFilter.
[ ] 92466  **
[ ] 92467  ** A jump is made to P2 if the result set after filtering would be empty.
[ ] 92468  */
[ ] 92469  case OP_VFilter: {   /* jump */
[ ] 92470    int nArg;
[ ] 92471    int iQuery;
[ ] 92472    const sqlite3_module *pModule;
[ ] 92473    Mem *pQuery;
[ ] 92474    Mem *pArgc;
[ ] 92475    sqlite3_vtab_cursor *pVCur;
[ ] 92476    sqlite3_vtab *pVtab;
[ ] 92477    VdbeCursor *pCur;
[ ] 92478    int res;
[ ] 92479    int i;
[ ] 92480    Mem **apArg;
[ ] 92481
[ ] 92482    pQuery = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 92483    pArgc = &pQuery[1];
[ ] 92484    pCur = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 92485    assert( memIsValid(pQuery) );
[ ] 92486    REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p3, pQuery);
[ ] 92487    assert( pCur->eCurType==CURTYPE_VTAB );
[ ] 92488    pVCur = pCur->uc.pVCur;
[ ] 92489    pVtab = pVCur->pVtab;
[ ] 92490    pModule = pVtab->pModule;
[ ] 92491
[ ] 92492    /* Grab the index number and argc parameters */
[ ] 92493    assert( (pQuery->flags&MEM_Int)!=0 && pArgc->flags==MEM_Int );
[ ] 92494    nArg = (int)pArgc->u.i;
[ ] 92495    iQuery = (int)pQuery->u.i;
[ ] 92496
[ ] 92497    /* Invoke the xFilter method */
[ ] 92498    res = 0;
[ ] 92499    apArg = p->apArg;
[ ] 92500    for(i = 0; i<nArg; i++){
[ ] 92501      apArg[i] = &pArgc[i+1];
[ ] 92502    }
[ ] 92503    rc = pModule->xFilter(pVCur, iQuery, pOp->p4.z, nArg, apArg);
[ ] 92504    sqlite3VtabImportErrmsg(p, pVtab);
[ ] 92505    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92506    res = pModule->xEof(pVCur);
[ ] 92507    pCur->nullRow = 0;
[ ] 92508    VdbeBranchTaken(res!=0,2);
[ ] 92509    if( res ) goto jump_to_p2;
[ ] 92510    break;
[ ] 92511  }
[ ] 92512  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE */
[ ] 92513
[ ] 92514  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 92515  /* Opcode: VColumn P1 P2 P3 * P5
[ ] 92516  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=vcolumn(P2)
[ ] 92517  **
[ ] 92518  ** Store in register P3 the value of the P2-th column of
[ ] 92519  ** the current row of the virtual-table of cursor P1.
[ ] 92520  **
[ ] 92521  ** If the VColumn opcode is being used to fetch the value of
[ ] 92522  ** an unchanging column during an UPDATE operation, then the P5
[ ] 92523  ** value is OPFLAG_NOCHNG.  This will cause the sqlite3_vtab_nochange()
[ ] 92524  ** function to return true inside the xColumn method of the virtual
[ ] 92525  ** table implementation.  The P5 column might also contain other
[ ] 92526  ** bits (OPFLAG_LENGTHARG or OPFLAG_TYPEOFARG) but those bits are
[ ] 92527  ** unused by OP_VColumn.
[ ] 92528  */
[ ] 92529  case OP_VColumn: {
[ ] 92530    sqlite3_vtab *pVtab;
[ ] 92531    const sqlite3_module *pModule;
[ ] 92532    Mem *pDest;
[ ] 92533    sqlite3_context sContext;
[ ] 92534
[ ] 92535    VdbeCursor *pCur = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 92536    assert( pCur->eCurType==CURTYPE_VTAB );
[ ] 92537    assert( pOp->p3>0 && pOp->p3<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor) );
[ ] 92538    pDest = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 92539    memAboutToChange(p, pDest);
[ ] 92540    if( pCur->nullRow ){
[ ] 92541      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pDest);
[ ] 92542      break;
[ ] 92543    }
[ ] 92544    pVtab = pCur->uc.pVCur->pVtab;
[ ] 92545    pModule = pVtab->pModule;
[ ] 92546    assert( pModule->xColumn );
[ ] 92547    memset(&sContext, 0, sizeof(sContext));
[ ] 92548    sContext.pOut = pDest;
[ ] 92549    assert( pOp->p5==OPFLAG_NOCHNG || pOp->p5==0 );
[ ] 92550    if( pOp->p5 & OPFLAG_NOCHNG ){
[ ] 92551      sqlite3VdbeMemSetNull(pDest);
[ ] 92552      pDest->flags = MEM_Null|MEM_Zero;
[ ] 92553      pDest->u.nZero = 0;
[ ] 92554    }else{
[ ] 92555      MemSetTypeFlag(pDest, MEM_Null);
[ ] 92556    }
[ ] 92557    rc = pModule->xColumn(pCur->uc.pVCur, &sContext, pOp->p2);
[ ] 92558    sqlite3VtabImportErrmsg(p, pVtab);
[ ] 92559    if( sContext.isError>0 ){
[ ] 92560      sqlite3VdbeError(p, "%s", sqlite3_value_text(pDest));
[ ] 92561      rc = sContext.isError;
[ ] 92562    }
[ ] 92563    sqlite3VdbeChangeEncoding(pDest, encoding);
[ ] 92564    REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p3, pDest);
[ ] 92565    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pDest);
[ ] 92566
[ ] 92567    if( sqlite3VdbeMemTooBig(pDest) ){
[ ] 92568      goto too_big;
[ ] 92569    }
[ ] 92570    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92571    break;
[ ] 92572  }
[ ] 92573  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE */
[ ] 92574
[ ] 92575  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 92576  /* Opcode: VNext P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 92577  **
[ ] 92578  ** Advance virtual table P1 to the next row in its result set and
[ ] 92579  ** jump to instruction P2.  Or, if the virtual table has reached
[ ] 92580  ** the end of its result set, then fall through to the next instruction.
[ ] 92581  */
[ ] 92582  case OP_VNext: {   /* jump */
[ ] 92583    sqlite3_vtab *pVtab;
[ ] 92584    const sqlite3_module *pModule;
[ ] 92585    int res;
[ ] 92586    VdbeCursor *pCur;
[ ] 92587
[ ] 92588    res = 0;
[ ] 92589    pCur = p->apCsr[pOp->p1];
[ ] 92590    assert( pCur->eCurType==CURTYPE_VTAB );
[ ] 92591    if( pCur->nullRow ){
[ ] 92592      break;
[ ] 92593    }
[ ] 92594    pVtab = pCur->uc.pVCur->pVtab;
[ ] 92595    pModule = pVtab->pModule;
[ ] 92596    assert( pModule->xNext );
[ ] 92597
[ ] 92598    /* Invoke the xNext() method of the module. There is no way for the
[ ] 92599    ** underlying implementation to return an error if one occurs during
[ ] 92600    ** xNext(). Instead, if an error occurs, true is returned (indicating that
[ ] 92601    ** data is available) and the error code returned when xColumn or
[ ] 92602    ** some other method is next invoked on the save virtual table cursor.
[ ] 92603    */
[ ] 92604    rc = pModule->xNext(pCur->uc.pVCur);
[ ] 92605    sqlite3VtabImportErrmsg(p, pVtab);
[ ] 92606    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92607    res = pModule->xEof(pCur->uc.pVCur);
[ ] 92608    VdbeBranchTaken(!res,2);
[ ] 92609    if( !res ){
[ ] 92610      /* If there is data, jump to P2 */
[ ] 92611      goto jump_to_p2_and_check_for_interrupt;
[ ] 92612    }
[ ] 92613    goto check_for_interrupt;
[ ] 92614  }
[ ] 92615  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE */
[ ] 92616
[ ] 92617  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 92618  /* Opcode: VRename P1 * * P4 *
[ ] 92619  **
[ ] 92620  ** P4 is a pointer to a virtual table object, an sqlite3_vtab structure.
[ ] 92621  ** This opcode invokes the corresponding xRename method. The value
[ ] 92622  ** in register P1 is passed as the zName argument to the xRename method.
[ ] 92623  */
[ ] 92624  case OP_VRename: {
[ ] 92625    sqlite3_vtab *pVtab;
[ ] 92626    Mem *pName;
[ ] 92627    int isLegacy;
[ ] 92628
[ ] 92629    isLegacy = (db->flags & SQLITE_LegacyAlter);
[ ] 92630    db->flags |= SQLITE_LegacyAlter;
[ ] 92631    pVtab = pOp->p4.pVtab->pVtab;
[ ] 92632    pName = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[ ] 92633    assert( pVtab->pModule->xRename );
[ ] 92634    assert( memIsValid(pName) );
[ ] 92635    assert( p->readOnly==0 );
[ ] 92636    REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p1, pName);
[ ] 92637    assert( pName->flags & MEM_Str );
[ ] 92638    testcase( pName->enc==SQLITE_UTF8 );
[ ] 92639    testcase( pName->enc==SQLITE_UTF16BE );
[ ] 92640    testcase( pName->enc==SQLITE_UTF16LE );
[ ] 92641    rc = sqlite3VdbeChangeEncoding(pName, SQLITE_UTF8);
[ ] 92642    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92643    rc = pVtab->pModule->xRename(pVtab, pName->z);
[ ] 92644    if( isLegacy==0 ) db->flags &= ~(u64)SQLITE_LegacyAlter;
[ ] 92645    sqlite3VtabImportErrmsg(p, pVtab);
[ ] 92646    p->expired = 0;
[ ] 92647    if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92648    break;
[ ] 92649  }
[ ] 92650  #endif
[ ] 92651
[ ] 92652  #ifndef SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE
[ ] 92653  /* Opcode: VUpdate P1 P2 P3 P4 P5
[ ] 92654  ** Synopsis: data=r[P3@P2]
[ ] 92655  **
[ ] 92656  ** P4 is a pointer to a virtual table object, an sqlite3_vtab structure.
[ ] 92657  ** This opcode invokes the corresponding xUpdate method. P2 values
[ ] 92658  ** are contiguous memory cells starting at P3 to pass to the xUpdate
[ ] 92659  ** invocation. The value in register (P3+P2-1) corresponds to the
[ ] 92660  ** p2th element of the argv array passed to xUpdate.
[ ] 92661  **
[ ] 92662  ** The xUpdate method will do a DELETE or an INSERT or both.
[ ] 92663  ** The argv[0] element (which corresponds to memory cell P3)
[ ] 92664  ** is the rowid of a row to delete.  If argv[0] is NULL then no
[ ] 92665  ** deletion occurs.  The argv[1] element is the rowid of the new
[ ] 92666  ** row.  This can be NULL to have the virtual table select the new
[ ] 92667  ** rowid for itself.  The subsequent elements in the array are
[ ] 92668  ** the values of columns in the new row.
[ ] 92669  **
[ ] 92670  ** If P2==1 then no insert is performed.  argv[0] is the rowid of
[ ] 92671  ** a row to delete.
[ ] 92672  **
[ ] 92673  ** P1 is a boolean flag. If it is set to true and the xUpdate call
[ ] 92674  ** is successful, then the value returned by sqlite3_last_insert_rowid()
[ ] 92675  ** is set to the value of the rowid for the row just inserted.
[ ] 92676  **
[ ] 92677  ** P5 is the error actions (OE_Replace, OE_Fail, OE_Ignore, etc) to
[ ] 92678  ** apply in the case of a constraint failure on an insert or update.
[ ] 92679  */
[ ] 92680  case OP_VUpdate: {
[ ] 92681    sqlite3_vtab *pVtab;
[ ] 92682    const sqlite3_module *pModule;
[ ] 92683    int nArg;
[ ] 92684    int i;
[ ] 92685    sqlite_int64 rowid;
[ ] 92686    Mem **apArg;
[ ] 92687    Mem *pX;
[ ] 92688
[ ] 92689    assert( pOp->p2==1        || pOp->p5==OE_Fail   || pOp->p5==OE_Rollback
[ ] 92690         || pOp->p5==OE_Abort || pOp->p5==OE_Ignore || pOp->p5==OE_Replace
[ ] 92691    );
[ ] 92692    assert( p->readOnly==0 );
[ ] 92693    if( db->mallocFailed ) goto no_mem;
[ ] 92694    sqlite3VdbeIncrWriteCounter(p, 0);
[ ] 92695    pVtab = pOp->p4.pVtab->pVtab;
[ ] 92696    if( pVtab==0 || NEVER(pVtab->pModule==0) ){
[ ] 92697      rc = SQLITE_LOCKED;
[ ] 92698      goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92699    }
[ ] 92700    pModule = pVtab->pModule;
[ ] 92701    nArg = pOp->p2;
[ ] 92702    assert( pOp->p4type==P4_VTAB );
[ ] 92703    if( ALWAYS(pModule->xUpdate) ){
[ ] 92704      u8 vtabOnConflict = db->vtabOnConflict;
[ ] 92705      apArg = p->apArg;
[ ] 92706      pX = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 92707      for(i=0; i<nArg; i++){
[ ] 92708        assert( memIsValid(pX) );
[ ] 92709        memAboutToChange(p, pX);
[ ] 92710        apArg[i] = pX;
[ ] 92711        pX++;
[ ] 92712      }
[ ] 92713      db->vtabOnConflict = pOp->p5;
[ ] 92714      rc = pModule->xUpdate(pVtab, nArg, apArg, &rowid);
[ ] 92715      db->vtabOnConflict = vtabOnConflict;
[ ] 92716      sqlite3VtabImportErrmsg(p, pVtab);
[ ] 92717      if( rc==SQLITE_OK && pOp->p1 ){
[ ] 92718        assert( nArg>1 && apArg[0] && (apArg[0]->flags&MEM_Null) );
[ ] 92719        db->lastRowid = rowid;
[ ] 92720      }
[ ] 92721      if( (rc&0xff)==SQLITE_CONSTRAINT && pOp->p4.pVtab->bConstraint ){
[ ] 92722        if( pOp->p5==OE_Ignore ){
[ ] 92723          rc = SQLITE_OK;
[ ] 92724        }else{
[ ] 92725          p->errorAction = ((pOp->p5==OE_Replace) ? OE_Abort : pOp->p5);
[ ] 92726        }
[ ] 92727      }else{
[ ] 92728        p->nChange++;
[ ] 92729      }
[ ] 92730      if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92731    }
[ ] 92732    break;
[ ] 92733  }
[ ] 92734  #endif /* SQLITE_OMIT_VIRTUALTABLE */
[ ] 92735
[ ] 92736  #ifndef  SQLITE_OMIT_PAGER_PRAGMAS
[ ] 92737  /* Opcode: Pagecount P1 P2 * * *
[ ] 92738  **
[ ] 92739  ** Write the current number of pages in database P1 to memory cell P2.
[ ] 92740  */
[ ] 92741  case OP_Pagecount: {            /* out2 */
[ ] 92742    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 92743    pOut->u.i = sqlite3BtreeLastPage(db->aDb[pOp->p1].pBt);
[ ] 92744    break;
[ ] 92745  }
[ ] 92746  #endif
[ ] 92747
[ ] 92748
[ ] 92749  #ifndef  SQLITE_OMIT_PAGER_PRAGMAS
[ ] 92750  /* Opcode: MaxPgcnt P1 P2 P3 * *
[ ] 92751  **
[ ] 92752  ** Try to set the maximum page count for database P1 to the value in P3.
[ ] 92753  ** Do not let the maximum page count fall below the current page count and
[ ] 92754  ** do not change the maximum page count value if P3==0.
[ ] 92755  **
[ ] 92756  ** Store the maximum page count after the change in register P2.
[ ] 92757  */
[ ] 92758  case OP_MaxPgcnt: {            /* out2 */
[ ] 92759    unsigned int newMax;
[ ] 92760    Btree *pBt;
[ ] 92761
[ ] 92762    pOut = out2Prerelease(p, pOp);
[ ] 92763    pBt = db->aDb[pOp->p1].pBt;
[ ] 92764    newMax = 0;
[ ] 92765    if( pOp->p3 ){
[ ] 92766      newMax = sqlite3BtreeLastPage(pBt);
[ ] 92767      if( newMax < (unsigned)pOp->p3 ) newMax = (unsigned)pOp->p3;
[ ] 92768    }
[ ] 92769    pOut->u.i = sqlite3BtreeMaxPageCount(pBt, newMax);
[ ] 92770    break;
[ ] 92771  }
[ ] 92772  #endif
[ ] 92773
[ ] 92774  /* Opcode: Function P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 92775  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=func(r[P2@NP])
[ ] 92776  **
[ ] 92777  ** Invoke a user function (P4 is a pointer to an sqlite3_context object that
[ ] 92778  ** contains a pointer to the function to be run) with arguments taken
[ ] 92779  ** from register P2 and successors.  The number of arguments is in
[ ] 92780  ** the sqlite3_context object that P4 points to.
[ ] 92781  ** The result of the function is stored
[ ] 92782  ** in register P3.  Register P3 must not be one of the function inputs.
[ ] 92783  **
[ ] 92784  ** P1 is a 32-bit bitmask indicating whether or not each argument to the
[ ] 92785  ** function was determined to be constant at compile time. If the first
[ ] 92786  ** argument was constant then bit 0 of P1 is set. This is used to determine
[ ] 92787  ** whether meta data associated with a user function argument using the
[ ] 92788  ** sqlite3_set_auxdata() API may be safely retained until the next
[ ] 92789  ** invocation of this opcode.
[ ] 92790  **
[ ] 92791  ** See also: AggStep, AggFinal, PureFunc
[ ] 92792  */
[ ] 92793  /* Opcode: PureFunc P1 P2 P3 P4 *
[ ] 92794  ** Synopsis: r[P3]=func(r[P2@NP])
[ ] 92795  **
[ ] 92796  ** Invoke a user function (P4 is a pointer to an sqlite3_context object that
[ ] 92797  ** contains a pointer to the function to be run) with arguments taken
[ ] 92798  ** from register P2 and successors.  The number of arguments is in
[ ] 92799  ** the sqlite3_context object that P4 points to.
[ ] 92800  ** The result of the function is stored
[ ] 92801  ** in register P3.  Register P3 must not be one of the function inputs.
[ ] 92802  **
[ ] 92803  ** P1 is a 32-bit bitmask indicating whether or not each argument to the
[ ] 92804  ** function was determined to be constant at compile time. If the first
[ ] 92805  ** argument was constant then bit 0 of P1 is set. This is used to determine
[ ] 92806  ** whether meta data associated with a user function argument using the
[ ] 92807  ** sqlite3_set_auxdata() API may be safely retained until the next
[ ] 92808  ** invocation of this opcode.
[ ] 92809  **
[ ] 92810  ** This opcode works exactly like OP_Function.  The only difference is in
[ ] 92811  ** its name.  This opcode is used in places where the function must be
[ ] 92812  ** purely non-deterministic.  Some built-in date/time functions can be
[ ] 92813  ** either determinitic of non-deterministic, depending on their arguments.
[ ] 92814  ** When those function are used in a non-deterministic way, they will check
[ ] 92815  ** to see if they were called using OP_PureFunc instead of OP_Function, and
[ ] 92816  ** if they were, they throw an error.
[ ] 92817  **
[ ] 92818  ** See also: AggStep, AggFinal, Function
[ ] 92819  */
[ ] 92820  case OP_PureFunc:              /* group */
[ ] 92821  case OP_Function: {            /* group */
[ ] 92822    int i;
[ ] 92823    sqlite3_context *pCtx;
[ ] 92824
[ ] 92825    assert( pOp->p4type==P4_FUNCCTX );
[ ] 92826    pCtx = pOp->p4.pCtx;
[ ] 92827
[ ] 92828    /* If this function is inside of a trigger, the register array in aMem[]
[ ] 92829    ** might change from one evaluation to the next.  The next block of code
[ ] 92830    ** checks to see if the register array has changed, and if so it
[ ] 92831    ** reinitializes the relavant parts of the sqlite3_context object */
[ ] 92832    pOut = &aMem[pOp->p3];
[ ] 92833    if( pCtx->pOut != pOut ){
[ ] 92834      pCtx->pVdbe = p;
[ ] 92835      pCtx->pOut = pOut;
[ ] 92836      for(i=pCtx->argc-1; i>=0; i--) pCtx->argv[i] = &aMem[pOp->p2+i];
[ ] 92837    }
[ ] 92838    assert( pCtx->pVdbe==p );
[ ] 92839
[ ] 92840    memAboutToChange(p, pOut);
[ ] 92841  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 92842    for(i=0; i<pCtx->argc; i++){
[ ] 92843      assert( memIsValid(pCtx->argv[i]) );
[ ] 92844      REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p2+i, pCtx->argv[i]);
[ ] 92845    }
[ ] 92846  #endif
[ ] 92847    MemSetTypeFlag(pOut, MEM_Null);
[ ] 92848    assert( pCtx->isError==0 );
[ ] 92849    (*pCtx->pFunc->xSFunc)(pCtx, pCtx->argc, pCtx->argv);/* IMP: R-24505-23230 */
[ ] 92850
[ ] 92851    /* If the function returned an error, throw an exception */
[ ] 92852    if( pCtx->isError ){
[ ] 92853      if( pCtx->isError>0 ){
[ ] 92854        sqlite3VdbeError(p, "%s", sqlite3_value_text(pOut));
[ ] 92855        rc = pCtx->isError;
[ ] 92856      }
[ ] 92857      sqlite3VdbeDeleteAuxData(db, &p->pAuxData, pCtx->iOp, pOp->p1);
[ ] 92858      pCtx->isError = 0;
[ ] 92859      if( rc ) goto abort_due_to_error;
[ ] 92860    }
[ ] 92861
[ ] 92862    /* Copy the result of the function into register P3 */
[ ] 92863    if( pOut->flags & (MEM_Str|MEM_Blob) ){
[ ] 92864      sqlite3VdbeChangeEncoding(pOut, encoding);
[ ] 92865      if( sqlite3VdbeMemTooBig(pOut) ) goto too_big;
[ ] 92866    }
[ ] 92867
[ ] 92868    REGISTER_TRACE(pOp->p3, pOut);
[ ] 92869    UPDATE_MAX_BLOBSIZE(pOut);
[ ] 92870    break;
[ ] 92871  }
[ ] 92872

[ ] 92884  ** opcode.
[ ] 92885  **
[ ] 92886  ** If tracing is enabled (by the sqlite3_trace()) interface, then
[ ] 92887  ** the UTF-8 string contained in P4 is emitted on the trace callback.
[ ] 92888  ** Or if P4 is blank, use the string returned by sqlite3_sql().
[ ] 92889  **
[ ] 92890  ** If P2 is not zero, jump to instruction P2.

[ ] 92893  ** first time they are evaluated for this run.

[ ] 93010  #ifdef SQLITE_DEBUG
[ ] 93011  /* Opcode:  ReleaseReg   P1 P2 P3 * P5
[ ] 93012  ** Synopsis: release r[P1@P2] mask P3
[ ] 93013  **
[ ] 93014  ** Release registers from service.  Any content that was in the
[ ] 93015  ** the registers is unreliable after this opcode completes.
[ ] 93016  **
[ ] 93017  ** The registers released will be the P2 registers starting at P1,
[ ] 93018  ** except if bit ii of P3 set, then do not release register P1+ii.
[ ] 93019  ** In other words, P3 is a mask of registers to preserve.
[ ] 93020  **
[ ] 93021  ** Releasing a register clears the Mem.pScopyFrom pointer.  That means
[ ] 93022  ** that if the content of the released register was set using OP_SCopy,
[ ] 93023  ** a change to the value of the source register for the OP_SCopy will no longer
[ ] 93024  ** generate an assertion fault in sqlite3VdbeMemAboutToChange().
[ ] 93025  **
[ ] 93026  ** If P5 is set, then all released registers have their type set
[ ] 93027  ** to MEM_Undefined so that any subsequent attempt to read the released
[ ] 93028  ** register (before it is reinitialized) will generate an assertion fault.
[ ] 93029  **
[ ] 93030  ** P5 ought to be set on every call to this opcode.
[ ] 93031  ** However, there are places in the code generator will release registers
[ ] 93032  ** before their are used, under the (valid) assumption that the registers
[ ] 93033  ** will not be reallocated for some other purpose before they are used and
[ ] 93034  ** hence are safe to release.
[ ] 93035  **
[ ] 93036  ** This opcode is only available in testing and debugging builds.  It is
[ ] 93037  ** not generated for release builds.  The purpose of this opcode is to help
[ ] 93038  ** validate the generated bytecode.  This opcode does not actually contribute
[ ] 93039  ** to computing an answer.
[ ] 93040  */

[W] 93042    Mem *pMem;
[W] 93043    int i;
[W] 93044    u32 constMask;
[W] 93045    assert( pOp->p1>0 );
[W] 93046    assert( pOp->p1+pOp->p2<=(p->nMem+1 - p->nCursor)+1 );
[W] 93047    pMem = &aMem[pOp->p1];
[W] 93048    constMask = pOp->p3;
[W] 93049    for(i=0; i<pOp->p2; i++, pMem++){
[W] 93050      if( i>=32 || (constMask & MASKBIT32(i))==0 ){
[W] 93051        pMem->pScopyFrom = 0;
[W] 93052        if( i<32 && pOp->p5 ) MemSetTypeFlag(pMem, MEM_Undefined);
[W] 93053      }
[W] 93054    }
[W] 93055    break;
[W] 93056  }
[ ] 93057  #endif

==== MECHANISM CONTEXT (involved fuzzers only) ====
--- naive ---
**Instrumentation**: SanitizerCoverage edge counters
(`__sanitizer_cov_trace_pc_guard*` callbacks compiled in via clang
`-fsanitize-coverage=...`).

**Feedback**: per-edge hit-count bucket; a new bucket triggers a
corpus-add (LibAFL `MaxMapFeedback` over the edge map).

**Mutators**: havoc + token stack — `ByteFlipMutator`, `ByteRandMutator`,
`ByteIncMutator`, `ByteDecMutator`, `ByteAddMutator`, `WordAddMutator`,
`DwordAddMutator`, `QwordAddMutator`, `BytesDeleteMutator`,
`BytesInsertMutator`, `BytesInsertCopyMutator`, `BytesExpandMutator`,
`BytesRandInsertMutator`, `BytesRandSetMutator`, `BytesCopyMutator`,
`BytesSwapMutator`, `WordInterestingMutator`, `DwordInterestingMutator`,
`ByteInterestingMutator`, `CrossoverInsertMutator`,
`CrossoverReplaceMutator`, `TokenInsert`, `TokenReplace`.

**Observed `mutation_op` in seed metadata**: any of the above. No I2S.

**Per-execution cost**: one edge-counter increment per executed BB edge.

--- value_profile ---
**Instrumentation**: naive's edge counters **plus** integer-CMP
interception, but instead of buffering operands per execution (cmplog),
each CMP callback writes into a `CMP_MAP` keyed by (PC, operand-distance
bucket). The distance bucket is a coarse encoding of how close the two
operands were (Hamming distance bucket for `trace_cmp*`; matching-prefix
length for string/memory CMPs).

**Feedback**: edge-bucket signal **plus** new-CMP_MAP-bucket signal
(both via `MaxMapFeedback`-style coverage). An input that produces a
CMP-operand pair closer to matching than any previously-seen pair
adds a new CMP_MAP bucket and is preserved as corpus.

**Mutators**: naive's havoc + token stack. No `I2SRandReplace`.

**Observed `mutation_op` in seed metadata**: havoc/token names only —
no ParentInfo-only entries (no `mutation_op = -` rows). Absence of
the dash signal is direct evidence the seed was found by naive or
value_profile, not by an I2S stage.

**Per-execution cost**: edge increment + CMP_MAP update per intercepted
CMP per execution.
